<seg id="493">THE BOY BATHING</seg>
<seg id="493">洗澡的小男孩</seg>
<seg id="494">A Boy was bathing in a river and got out of his depth, and was in great danger of being drowned.</seg>
<seg id="494">一天，有个小男孩正在河里洗澡，他走到了水深没顶的地方，眼看就要被淹死了。</seg>
<seg id="495">A man who was passing along a road heard his cries for help, and went to the riverside and began to scold him for being so careless as to get into deep water, but made no attempt to help him.</seg>
<seg id="495">一个正经过此路的行人听到了男孩的呼救声，他走到河边，开始教训小男孩太鲁莽地进入深水区，但是并没有要去救人的意思。</seg>
<seg id="496">"Oh, sir," cried the Boy, "please help me first and scold me afterwards."</seg>
<seg id="496">小男孩大声喊道：“先生，拜托你，还是先把我救起来，再好好教训吧。”</seg>
<seg id="497">Give assistance, not advice, in a crisis.</seg>
<seg id="497">危急之中应伸出援手，而非建议。</seg>
<seg id="498">THE QUACK FROG</seg>
<seg id="498">庸医青蛙</seg>
<seg id="499">Once upon a time a Frog came forth from his home in the marshes and proclaimed to all the world that he was a learned physician, skilled in drugs and able to cure all diseases.</seg>
<seg id="499">从前，有一只青蛙从他那湿地中的家里蹦了出来，向所有的动物宣称自己是一个博学多才的医生，精通于药学，能治百病。</seg>
<seg id="500">Among the crowd was a Fox, who called out, "You a doctor!</seg>
<seg id="500">其中，有一只狐狸问他：“你这样的医生，</seg>
<seg id="501">Why, how can you set up to heal others when you cannot even cure your own lame legs and blotched and wrinkled skin?"</seg>
<seg id="501">连自己的跛足和斑驳起皱的皮都治不好，怎么还敢吹牛说能给别人治病呢？”</seg>
<seg id="502">Physician, heal thyself.</seg>
<seg id="502">要医人，先医己。</seg>
<seg id="503">THE SWOLLEN FOX</seg>
<seg id="503">胀肚的狐狸</seg>
<seg id="504">A hungry Fox found in a hollow tree a quantity of bread and meat, which some shepherds had placed there against their return.</seg>
<seg id="504">饥饿的狐狸在一棵中空的树干中发现了一些牧羊人存留的面包和肉。</seg>
<seg id="505">Delighted with his find he slipped in through the narrow aperture and greedily devoured it all.</seg>
<seg id="505">高兴之余，他立即通过那狭窄的缝隙挤进去，贪婪地大吃起来。</seg>
<seg id="506">But when he tried to get out again he found himself so swollen after his big meal that he could not squeeze through the hole, and fell to whining and groaning over his misfortune.</seg>
<seg id="506">然而，当他吃饱之后，却发现自己的肚子胀鼓鼓的，即便费了九牛二虎之力，却怎么也钻不出那个洞来，便在树洞里唉声叹气。</seg>
<seg id="507">Another Fox, happening to pass that way, came and asked him what the matter was;</seg>
<seg id="507">另一只狐狸恰巧经过那里，听到他的呻吟，便过去问他原因。</seg>
<seg id="508">and, on learning the state of the case, said, "Well, my friend, I see nothing for it but for you to stay where you are till you shrink to your former size;</seg>
<seg id="508">听明白缘由后，那只狐狸便说道：“我的朋友，你就老老实实待在里边吧，等到恢复了钻进去之前的身材，</seg>
<seg id="509">you'll get out then easily enough."</seg>
<seg id="509">你就能轻松地出来了。”</seg>
<seg id="510">THE MOUSE, THE FROG, AND THE HAWK</seg>
<seg id="510">老鼠、青蛙和老鹰</seg>
<seg id="511">A Mouse and a Frog struck up a friendship; they were not well mated, for the Mouse lived entirely on land, while the Frog was equally at home on land or in the water.</seg>
<seg id="511">一只老鼠与一只青蛙建立起了友谊。但是他们并非十分相配，因为老鼠完全生活在陆地上，而青蛙则除了陆地上的生活外，还时常在水中生活。</seg>
<seg id="512">In order that they might never be separated, the Frog tied himself and the Mouse together by the leg with a piece of thread.</seg>
<seg id="512">为了永远不分开，青蛙用一根绳子把自己的腿和老鼠的腿绑在了一起。</seg>
<seg id="513">As long as they kept on dry land all went fairly well;</seg>
<seg id="513">他们在干燥的地面上行走时，一切都正常，</seg>
<seg id="514">but, coming to the edge of a pool, the Frog jumped in, taking the Mouse with him, and began swimming about and croaking with pleasure.</seg>
<seg id="514">可是当他们来到池塘边时，青蛙带着老鼠一起跳进了水里，一边游泳，一边高兴得呱呱大叫。</seg>
<seg id="515">The unhappy Mouse, however, was soon drowned, and floated about on the surface in the wake of the Frog.</seg>
<seg id="515">然而，可怜的老鼠很快就被淹死了，并且尾随着青蛙漂浮在水面。</seg>
<seg id="516">There he was spied by a Hawk, who pounced down on him and seized him in his talons.</seg>
<seg id="516">这时，一只鹰发现了老鼠，猛然冲向水面，用鹰爪把他抓了起来。</seg>
<seg id="517">The Frog was unable to loose the knot which bound him to the Mouse, and thus was carried off along with him and eaten by the Hawk.</seg>
<seg id="517">青蛙无法松开与老鼠绑在一起的绳结，于是也一同被抓走，成了老鹰的美食。</seg>
<seg id="518">THE BOY AND THE NETTLES</seg>
<seg id="518">男孩和荨麻</seg>
<seg id="519">A Boy was gathering berries from a hedge when his hand was stung by a Nettle.</seg>
<seg id="519">一个小男孩在篱笆丛中采集浆果，一不小心被荨麻刺伤了。</seg>
<seg id="520">Smarting with the pain, he ran to tell his mother, and said to her between his sobs, "I only touched it ever so lightly, mother."</seg>
<seg id="520">带着难受的刺痛感，他急忙跑回家，边哭边对妈妈说：“妈妈，我只是轻轻地碰了它一下。”</seg>
<seg id="521">"That's just why you got stung, my son," she said;</seg>
<seg id="521">妈妈说：“这就是你被刺痛的原因，我的儿子。</seg>
<seg id="522">"if you had grasped it firmly, it wouldn't have hurt you in the least."</seg>
<seg id="522">如果你勇敢地一把抓住它，就不会被刺伤了。”</seg>
<seg id="523">THE PEASANT AND THE APPLE-TREE</seg>
<seg id="523">农夫和苹果树</seg>
<seg id="524">A Peasant had an Apple-tree growing in his garden, which bore no fruit, but merely served to provide a shelter from the heat for the sparrows and grasshoppers which sat and chirped in its branches.</seg>
<seg id="524">有一个农夫，他的园子里有一棵苹果树，这棵树并不茂盛，只能为麻雀和蝉提供一个可栖息的地方，让他们坐在枝桠上歇息和喋喋不休地吵闹。</seg>
<seg id="525">Disappointed at its barrenness he determined to cut it down, and went and fetched his axe for the purpose.</seg>
<seg id="525">农夫认为这棵树没有什么大用处，决定把它砍掉，于是便拿起斧头走过去砍起树来。</seg>
<seg id="526">But when the sparrows and the grasshoppers saw what he was about to do, they begged him to spare it, and said to him, "If you destroy the tree we shall have to seek shelter elsewhere, and you will no longer have our merry chirping to enliven your work in the garden."</seg>
<seg id="526">然而，那些蝉和麻雀看到农夫的行为后，便请求农夫留下这棵树，并且对他说：“如果你砍掉这棵树，我们还得另外再找一个窝，而你也不会在园子里干活时听到我们为你鼓劲的欢快歌声了。”</seg>
<seg id="527">He, however, refused to listen to them, and set to work with a will to cut through the trunk.</seg>
<seg id="527">农夫没理睬他们，继续拿起斧头砍这棵树。</seg>
<seg id="528">A few strokes showed that it was hollow inside and contained a swarm of bees and a large store of honey.</seg>
<seg id="528">几斧下去之后，树上出现了一个洞，他发现树洞里有蜂巢和蜂蜜。</seg>
<seg id="529">Delighted with his find he threw down his axe, saying, "The old tree is worth keeping after all."</seg>
<seg id="529">他高兴地连忙抛下斧头，说：“这棵老树还真是值得保留下来。”</seg>
<seg id="530">Utility is most men's test of worth.</seg>
<seg id="530">实用性是大多数人对价值的检验。</seg>
<seg id="531">THE JACKDAW AND THE PIGEONS</seg>
<seg id="531">寒鸦与鸽子</seg>
<seg id="532">A Jackdaw, watching some Pigeons in a farmyard, was filled with envy when he saw how well they were fed, and determined to disguise himself as one of them, in order to secure a share of the good things they enjoyed.</seg>
<seg id="532">看见一群住在农场里的鸽子不愁吃喝，过着悠闲舒适的生活，一只寒鸦便心生嫉妒。为了能分享鸽子的食物，他决定将自己伪装成一只鸽子。</seg>
<seg id="533">So he painted himself white from head to foot and joined the flock;</seg>
<seg id="533">于是，寒鸦将自己的羽毛全都涂成白色，跑到鸽群中，</seg>
<seg id="534">and, so long as he was silent, they never suspected that he was not a pigeon like themselves.</seg>
<seg id="534">而且，寒鸦一直都保持着沉默，鸽子们从未怀疑过他不是一只鸽子。</seg>
<seg id="535">But one day he was unwise enough to start chattering, when they at once saw through his disguise and pecked him so unmercifully that he was glad to escape and join his own kind again.</seg>
<seg id="535">可是，有一天，他不小心发出了叫声，鸽子们立刻看穿了他的伪装，毫不留情地去啄他。寒鸦侥幸逃出了鸽群的袭击，回到同类之中。</seg>
<seg id="536">But the other jackdaws did not recognise him in his white dress, and would not let him feed with them, but drove him away:</seg>
<seg id="536">然而，因为他的毛色与以前不同了，所以其它寒鸦都没认出他来，也不让他参与集体生活，而且还赶他走。</seg>
<seg id="537">and so he became a homeless wanderer for his pains.</seg>
<seg id="537">就这样，这只寒鸦为了自己的贪心而成了无家可归的流浪汉。</seg>
<seg id="538">JUPITER AND THE TORTOISE</seg>
<seg id="538">朱庇特与乌龟</seg>
<seg id="539">Jupiter was about to marry a wife, and determined to celebrate the event by inviting all the animals to a banquet.</seg>
<seg id="539">朱庇特将要娶妻了，他决定举行盛大宴会，招待所有动物，以庆祝这件婚姻大事。</seg>
<seg id="540">They all came except the Tortoise, who did not put in an appearance, much to Jupiter's surprise.</seg>
<seg id="540">除了乌龟之外，所有动物都出席了，这让朱庇特大为吃惊。</seg>
<seg id="541">So when he next saw the Tortoise he asked him why he had not been at the banquet.</seg>
<seg id="541">于是，当他再次见到乌龟时，便问他为什么没来赴宴。</seg>
<seg id="542">"I don't care for going out," said the Tortoise; "there's no place like home."</seg>
<seg id="542">“我不喜欢出门，”乌龟回答说，“哪里也不如自己的家里舒服。”</seg>
<seg id="543">Jupiter was so much annoyed by this reply that he decreed that from that time forth the Tortoise should carry his house upon his back, and never be able to get away from home even if he wished to.</seg>
<seg id="543">朱庇特听到乌龟的回答很生气，于是就下令，从此让乌龟永远驮着他的家行走，即便想卸下来都不行。</seg>
<seg id="544">THE DOG IN THE MANGER</seg>
<seg id="544">狗占牛槽</seg>
<seg id="545">A Dog was lying in a Manger on the hay which had been put there for the cattle, and when they came and tried to eat, he growled and snapped at them and wouldn't let them get at their food.</seg>
<seg id="545">一条狗躺在牛吃草的饲料槽中，而狗身下的草正是为牛准备的食料。当牛向着牛槽走过去，准备吃草时，狗不仅冲着他们大吼大叫，而且还抓咬他们，不让牛吃干草。</seg>
<seg id="546">"What a selfish beast," said one of them to his companions;</seg>
<seg id="546">“这条狗太自私了！”其中一头牛对同伴说，</seg>
<seg id="547">"he can't eat himself and yet he won't let those eat who can."</seg>
<seg id="547">“他自己不能吃干草，还不让能吃的去吃。”</seg>
<seg id="548">THE TWO BAGS</seg>
<seg id="548">两个口袋</seg>
<seg id="549">Every man carries Two Bags about with him, one in front and one behind, and both are packed full of faults.</seg>
<seg id="549">每个人生来都带着两个口袋，一个在前，一个在后，两个口袋里都满载缺点。</seg>
<seg id="550">The Bag in front contains his neighbours' faults, the one behind his own.</seg>
<seg id="550">前面那只口袋里装的是别人的缺点，而后面那只口袋里则装的是自己的缺点。</seg>
<seg id="551">Hence it is that men do not see their own faults, but never fail to see those of others.</seg>
<seg id="551">因此，人们总是看不见自己的缺点，却永远不会忽视去看别人的缺点。</seg>
<seg id="552">THE OXEN AND THE AXLETREES</seg>
<seg id="552">公牛和车轴</seg>
<seg id="553">A pair of Oxen were drawing a heavily loaded waggon along the highway, and, as they tugged and strained at the yoke, the Axletrees creaked and groaned terribly.</seg>
<seg id="553">几头公牛正用劲拉着超重的货车在大路上行走，当他们用劲拖拉货车和牛轭时，车轴被压得吱吱作响。</seg>
<seg id="554">This was too much for the Oxen, who turned round indignantly and said, "Hullo, you there!</seg>
<seg id="554">牛有点不耐烦了，回过头对车轴说道：“喂，朋友，</seg>
<seg id="555">Why do you make such a noise when we do all the work?"</seg>
<seg id="555">我们正在努力地干活，你叫唤什么？”</seg>
<seg id="556">They complain most who suffer least.</seg>
<seg id="556">没受什么苦难的人往往最爱抱怨。</seg>
<seg id="557">THE BOY AND THE FILBERTS</seg>
<seg id="557">男孩和榛子</seg>
<seg id="558">A Boy put his hand into a jar of Filberts, and grasped as many as his fist could possibly hold.</seg>
<seg id="558">一个小男孩把手伸进装满榛子的瓶中，用尽全力去抓了一大把。</seg>
<seg id="559">But when he tried to pull it out again, he found he couldn't do so, for the neck of the jar was too small to allow of the passage of so large a handful.</seg>
<seg id="559">但当他想要缩回手时，却发现根本出不来，因为相对于他那抓满榛子的手来说，瓶口太小了。</seg>
<seg id="560">Unwilling to lose his nuts but unable to withdraw his hand, he burst into tears.</seg>
<seg id="560">他既不想放弃手中的一部分榛子，又不能拿出手来，于是大哭起来。</seg>
<seg id="561">A bystander, who saw where the trouble lay, said to him, "Come, my boy, don't be so greedy:</seg>
<seg id="561">一个旁观者看出了他的麻烦，便对他说：“孩子，不要太贪婪，</seg>
<seg id="562">be content with half the amount, and you'll be able to get your hand out without difficulty."</seg>
<seg id="562">只要少拿一半，你的手就能很容易地出来了。”</seg>
<seg id="563">Do not attempt too much at once.</seg>
<seg id="563">不要总想一口吃成个大胖子。</seg>
<seg id="564">THE FROGS ASKING FOR A KING</seg>
<seg id="564">青蛙求王</seg>
<seg id="565">Time was when the Frogs were discontented because they had no one to rule over them:</seg>
<seg id="565">因为缺少一个统领者，青蛙们大为不悦。</seg>
<seg id="566">so they sent a deputation to Jupiter to ask him to give them a King.</seg>
<seg id="566">于是，他们派了一个代表去拜见朱庇特，请求赐给他们一个国王。</seg>
<seg id="567">Jupiter, despising the folly of their request, cast a log into the pool where they lived, and said that that should be their King.</seg>
<seg id="567">朱庇特不屑于他们如此愚蠢的请求，便将一根木头扔到青蛙居住的池塘中，并且说这就是他们的国王。</seg>
<seg id="568">The Frogs were terrified at first by the splash, and scuttled away into the deepest parts of the pool;</seg>
<seg id="568">刚听到木头落下的声音时，青蛙们都吓了一大跳，纷纷潜入池塘深处；</seg>
<seg id="569">but by and by, when they saw that the log remained motionless, one by one they ventured to the surface again, and before long, growing bolder, they began to feel such contempt for it that they even took to sitting upon it.</seg>
<seg id="569">没过多久，当他们发现木头依旧静止在那里时，一个接一个地又游出水面来；不久之后，他们愈发大胆了，发现木头没什么了不起的，甚至于爬上木块，坐在它的上面。</seg>
<seg id="570">Thinking that a King of that sort was an insult to their dignity, they sent to Jupiter a second time, and begged him to take away the sluggish King he had given them, and to give them another and a better one.</seg>
<seg id="570">他们认为这样一个国王简直是对自己尊严的侮辱，于是又去求见朱庇特，请求把赐予他们的这个木头疙瘩拿走，再换一个更好的国王。</seg>
<seg id="571">Jupiter, annoyed at being pestered in this way, sent a Stork to rule over them, who no sooner arrived among them than he began to catch and eat the Frogs as fast as he could.</seg>
<seg id="571">朱庇特对此十分生气，便派了一只鹳去管制青蛙。结果，鹳一来到池塘里，便开始全力逮吃青蛙。</seg>
<seg id="572">THE OLIVE-TREE AND THE FIG-TREE</seg>
<seg id="572">橄榄树与无花果树</seg>
<seg id="573">An Olive-tree taunted a Fig-tree with the loss of her leaves at a certain season of the year.</seg>
<seg id="573">在某一个季节，橄榄树讥笑无花果树的叶子全都凋零了。</seg>
<seg id="574">"You," she said, "lose your leaves every autumn, and are bare till the spring:</seg>
<seg id="574">她说：“你的树叶一到秋天就会逐渐凋落，等到春天时才会再次长出来；</seg>
<seg id="575">whereas I, as you see, remain green and flourishing all the year round."</seg>
<seg id="575">而我的叶子就像你看到的这样，一年四季都是常青的。”</seg>
<seg id="576">Soon afterwards there came a heavy fall of snow, which settled on the leaves of the Olive so that she bent and broke under the weight;</seg>
<seg id="576">正当他夸夸其谈时，突然下起了大雪，雪花全都压在橄榄树的叶子上，不一会儿就把他压垮了；</seg>
<seg id="577">but the flakes fell harmlessly through the bare branches of the Fig, which survived to bear many another crop.</seg>
<seg id="577">而光秃秃的无花果树，一点也没被雪花伤害，反倒生存下来等待着来年的绽放。</seg>
<seg id="578">THE LION AND THE BOAR</seg>
<seg id="578">狮子和野猪</seg>
<seg id="579">One hot and thirsty day in the height of summer a Lion and a Boar came down to a little spring at the same moment to drink.</seg>
<seg id="579">炎热的夏季，难耐的酷暑使人口渴，一只狮子和一只野猪同时来到一个小泉边喝水。</seg>
<seg id="580">In a trice they were quarrelling as to who should drink first.</seg>
<seg id="580">他们立刻为谁应该先喝水而争吵起来。</seg>
<seg id="581">The quarrel soon became a fight and they attacked one another with the utmost fury.</seg>
<seg id="581">很快，争吵升级成了战争，他们互相攻击，斗得你死我活。</seg>
<seg id="582">Presently, stopping for a moment to take breath, they saw some vultures seated on a rock above evidently waiting for one of them to be killed, when they would fly down and feed upon the carcase.</seg>
<seg id="582">就在他们喘气休息时，忽然回过头去，看见几只秃鹰正坐在岩石上，显然他们正在等着看谁先败下阵来，接着就会冲过来吃掉那个尸体。</seg>
<seg id="583">The sight sobered them at once, and they made up their quarrel, saying, "We had much better be friends than fight and be eaten by vultures."</seg>
<seg id="583">一看到秃鹰，他们立刻停止了争斗，说：“我们还是成为朋友吧，总比相互争斗并被秃鹰吃掉好得多。”</seg>
<seg id="584">THE WALNUT-TREE</seg>
<seg id="584">核桃树</seg>
<seg id="585">A Walnut-tree, which grew by the roadside, bore every year a plentiful crop of nuts.</seg>
<seg id="585">有一棵长在路旁的核桃树，每年都能结很多核桃。</seg>
<seg id="586">Every one who passed by pelted its branches with sticks and stones, in order to bring down the fruit, and the tree suffered severely.</seg>
<seg id="586">为了得到树上的核桃，几乎每个路过的人都会用枝条和石头去敲打它。</seg>
<seg id="587">"It is hard," it cried, "that the very persons who enjoy my fruit should thus reward me with insults and blows."</seg>
<seg id="587">核桃树暗自悲叹自己所遭受的痛苦，自言自语道：“我真倒霉，每一个享用我的果实的人，都会用这样无情的损害与鞭打来回报我。”</seg>
<seg id="588">THE MAN AND THE LION</seg>
<seg id="588">人和同行的狮子</seg>
<seg id="589">A Man and a Lion were companions on a journey, and in the course of conversation they began to boast about their prowess, and each claimed to be superior to the other in strength and courage.</seg>
<seg id="589">有一次，狮子与人同行，交谈中他们开始吹嘘各自的英勇，双方都强调自己更勇敢。</seg>
<seg id="590">They were still arguing with some heat when they came to a cross-road where there was a statue of a Man strangling a Lion.</seg>
<seg id="590">就这样面红耳赤地争吵着，他们来到了一个十字路口，看到塑像上雕刻着一个人征服几头狮子的场景。</seg>
<seg id="591">"There!" said the Man triumphantly, "look at that!</seg>
<seg id="591">那个人立刻得意洋洋地说：“你看那里，</seg>
<seg id="592">Doesn't that prove to you that we are stronger than you?"</seg>
<seg id="592">事实证明我们比你们强得多了吧。”</seg>
<seg id="593">"Not so fast, my friend," said the Lion:</seg>
<seg id="593">“不要急，我的朋友，”狮子笑着说，</seg>
<seg id="594">"that is only your view of the case.</seg>
<seg id="594">“这只是你们的看法而已。</seg>
<seg id="595">If we Lions could make statues, you may be sure that in most of them you would see the Man underneath."</seg>
<seg id="595">如果狮子会雕刻，你就会看见众多人败倒在狮子脚下了。”</seg>
<seg id="596">There are two sides to every question.</seg>
<seg id="596">任何问题都有两面性。</seg>
<seg id="597">THE TORTOISE AND THE EAGLE</seg>
<seg id="597">乌龟和老鹰</seg>
<seg id="598">A Tortoise, discontented with his lowly life, and envious of the birds he saw disporting themselves in the air, begged an Eagle to teach him to fly.</seg>
<seg id="598">一只乌龟，不满足于自己的地面生活，很羡慕鸟儿能在空中玩耍，于是便请求老鹰教他飞翔。</seg>
<seg id="599">The Eagle protested that it was idle for him to try, as nature had not provided him with wings;</seg>
<seg id="599">老鹰劝他，这是他的一个白日梦，因为大自然并没有赋予他可以飞翔的翅膀。</seg>
<seg id="600">but the Tortoise pressed him with entreaties and promises of treasure, insisting that it could only be a question of learning the craft of the air.</seg>
<seg id="600">可是乌龟再三恳求，还用珍宝利诱老鹰，一再坚持这只是一个了解如何在空中飞翔的问题。</seg>
<seg id="601">So at length the Eagle consented to do the best he could for him, and picked him up in his talons.</seg>
<seg id="601">于是，老鹰为了满足乌龟的愿望，一把抓起他，</seg>
<seg id="602">Soaring with him to a great height in the sky he then let him go, and the wretched Tortoise fell headlong and was dashed to pieces on a rock.</seg>
<seg id="602">带着乌龟飞到一定高度后，就松开了鹰爪，而乌龟则落在了岩石上，被摔得粉身碎骨。</seg>
<seg id="603">THE KID ON THE HOUSETOP</seg>
<seg id="603">站在屋顶的小山羊与狼</seg>
<seg id="604">A Kid climbed up on to the roof of an outhouse, attracted by the grass and other things that grew in the thatch;</seg>
<seg id="604">被青草和其它东西所吸引的一只小山羊，爬到了屋外的草棚顶上。</seg>
<seg id="605">and as he stood there browsing away, he caught sight of a Wolf passing below, and jeered at him because he couldn't reach him.</seg>
<seg id="605">就在他四处观望时，看见一只狼从底下经过，便嘲笑他抓不到自己。</seg>
<seg id="606">The Wolf only looked up and said, "I hear you, my young friend;</seg>
<seg id="606">狼只是抬眼看了一下，说道：“嘿，伙计，</seg>
<seg id="607">but it is not you who mock me, but the roof on which you are standing."</seg>
<seg id="607">笑话我的可不是你，而是你所处的地势。”</seg>
<seg id="608">THE FOX WITHOUT A TAIL</seg>
<seg id="608">断尾巴狐狸</seg>
<seg id="609">A fox once fell into a trap, and after a struggle managed to get free, but with the loss of his brush.</seg>
<seg id="609">有一只狐狸曾经落入捕兽器的圈套，经过一番斗争，他终于逃脱了，但却失去了一条尾巴。</seg>
<seg id="610">He was then so much ashamed of his appearance that he thought life was not worth living unless he could persuade the other Foxes to part with their tails also, and thus divert attention from his own loss.</seg>
<seg id="610">经此劫难，他觉得自己脸上无光，还不如一死了之，除非能够劝说其它狐狸也舍弃自己的尾巴，这样大家就不会再关注他的断尾了。</seg>
<seg id="611">So he called a meeting of all the Foxes, and advised them to cut off their tails:</seg>
<seg id="611">于是他召集了所有狐狸开会，劝说他们也割掉自己的尾巴，</seg>
<seg id="612">"They're ugly things anyhow," he said, "and besides they're heavy, and it's tiresome to be always carrying them about with you."</seg>
<seg id="612">他当众宣称：“你们的尾巴实在太难看了，一直带着尾巴四处走，这简直太让人厌恶了。”</seg>
<seg id="613">But one of the other Foxes said, "My friend, if you hadn't lost your own tail, you wouldn't be so keen on getting us to cut off ours."</seg>
<seg id="613">然而，有一只狐狸站出来反驳道：“喂，朋友，如果你没有丢掉自己的尾巴，就不会这样煞费苦心地来劝说我们了。”</seg>
<seg id="614">THE VAIN JACKDAW</seg>
<seg id="614">爱慕虚荣的寒鸦</seg>
<seg id="615">Jupiter announced that he intended to appoint a king over the birds, and named a day on which they were to appear before his throne, when he would select the most beautiful of them all to be their ruler.</seg>
<seg id="615">朱庇特想在鸟类中指定一个王，便指定了一个日子，令百鸟全都按时出席，届时他将挑选其中最美丽的鸟为百鸟之王。</seg>
<seg id="616">Wishing to look their best on the occasion they repaired to the banks of a stream, where they busied themselves in washing and preening their feathers.</seg>
<seg id="616">为了展现自己最好的一面，众鸟都跑到河里忙于梳理自己的羽毛。</seg>
<seg id="617">The Jackdaw was there along with the rest, and realised that, with his ugly plumage, he would have no chance of being chosen as he was:</seg>
<seg id="617">像那些有自知之明的鸟一样，寒鸦也意识到自己的丑陋，根本不可能被选为百鸟之王，</seg>
<seg id="618">so he waited till they were all gone, and then picked up the most gaudy of the feathers they had dropped, and fastened them about his own body, with the result that he looked gayer than any of them.</seg>
<seg id="618">于是他在河边等着众鸟散去，捡起他们脱落下的羽毛，小心翼翼地全固定在自己身上，结果他看上去比其它鸟都华丽。</seg>
<seg id="619">When the appointed day came, the birds assembled before Jupiter's throne;</seg>
<seg id="619">指定的日子来临了，众鸟都来到朱庇特的王位前。</seg>
<seg id="620">and, after passing them in review, he was about to make the Jackdaw king, when all the rest set upon the king-elect, stripped him of his borrowed plumes, and exposed him for the Jackdaw that he was.</seg>
<seg id="620">浏览了一遍眼前的众鸟，朱庇特决定立寒鸦为王。为了王位大选而来的其它鸟，纷纷从寒鸦身上拔下本属于自己的羽毛，暴露出寒鸦那丑陋的本来面目。</seg>
<seg id="621">THE TRAVELLER AND HIS DOG</seg>
<seg id="621">旅人和他的狗</seg>
<seg id="622">A Traveller was about to start on a journey, and said to his Dog, who was stretching himself by the door, "Come, what are you yawning for?</seg>
<seg id="622">有一个人正准备踏上一段旅途，于是对正在门口站着打呵欠的狗说：“你还站在那里打什么呵欠呀？</seg>
<seg id="623">Hurry up and get ready:</seg>
<seg id="623">快点过来，一切都准备好了，</seg>
<seg id="624">I mean you to go with me."</seg>
<seg id="624">就差你跟我走了！”</seg>
<seg id="625">But the Dog merely wagged his tail and said quietly, "I'm ready, master:</seg>
<seg id="625">但是，狗却摇着尾巴，静静地回答说：“我早就准备好了，</seg>
<seg id="626">it's you I'm waiting for."</seg>
<seg id="626">倒是一直在等你呢。”</seg>
<seg id="627">THE SHIPWRECKED MAN AND THE SEA</seg>
<seg id="627">遇难者与海</seg>
<seg id="628">A Shipwrecked Man cast up on the beach fell asleep after his struggle with the waves.</seg>
<seg id="628">一个遇上海难的人经过一番风浪里的挣扎，终于被冲上岸，他筋疲力尽地躺在沙滩上睡着了。</seg>
<seg id="629">When he woke up, he bitterly reproached the Sea for its treachery in enticing men with its smooth and smiling surface, and then, when they were well embarked, turning in fury upon them and sending both ship and sailors to destruction.</seg>
<seg id="629">不一会儿，当他醒过来后，便开始指责大海总以平静、温和的外表引诱人们，然而，就在人们上当受骗之后，大海就变得凶暴和残忍，最终致使船和船上的人同归于尽。</seg>
<seg id="630">The Sea arose in the form of a woman, and replied, "Lay not the blame on me, O sailor, but on the Winds.</seg>
<seg id="630">这时，大海以女人的形象出现了，并且对他说：“喂，朋友，你别责怪我，应该责怪风！</seg>
<seg id="631">By nature I am as calm and safe as the land itself:</seg>
<seg id="631">我本是平静的，</seg>
<seg id="632">but the Winds fall upon me with their gusts and gales, and lash me into a fury that is not natural to me."</seg>
<seg id="632">但是只要风猛然刮过来，就会掀起惊涛骇浪，使我变得残暴。这并不是我的本性。”</seg>
<seg id="633">THE WILD BOAR AND THE FOX</seg>
<seg id="633">野猪与狐狸</seg>
<seg id="634">A Wild Boar was engaged in whetting his tusks upon the trunk of a tree in the forest when a Fox came by and, seeing what he was at, said to him, "Why are you doing that, pray?</seg>
<seg id="634">一头野猪在森林里的一棵树干上磨他的牙齿，这时，狐狸走过来，看到野猪在磨牙，便不解地问道：“你在做什么，祈祷吗？</seg>
<seg id="635">The huntsmen are not out to-day, and there are no other dangers at hand that I can see."</seg>
<seg id="635">今天猎人没出来，我也没看到有什么危险来临呀。”</seg>
<seg id="636">"True, my friend," replied the Boar, "but the instant my life is in danger I shall need to use my tusks.</seg>
<seg id="636">“的确如此，我的朋友，”野猪回答说，“不过，一旦危险降临，我就可以利用磨好的利牙了。</seg>
<seg id="637">There'll be no time to sharpen them then."</seg>
<seg id="637">那时根本没有工夫再来磨牙了。”</seg>
<seg id="638">MERCURY AND THE SCULPTOR</seg>
<seg id="638">墨丘利与雕刻家</seg>
<seg id="639">Mercury was very anxious to know in what estimation he was held by mankind;</seg>
<seg id="639">墨丘利急于了解自己有多么受人尊重，</seg>
<seg id="640">so he disguised himself as a man and walked into a Sculptor's studio, where there were a number of statues finished and ready for sale.</seg>
<seg id="640">便化做一个凡人，来到一个雕刻家的工作室，那里有很多已经完工的雕像正待出售。</seg>
<seg id="641">Seeing a statue of Jupiter among the rest, he inquired the price of it.</seg>
<seg id="641">他看见了一尊朱庇特的雕像，便问要多少钱。</seg>
<seg id="642">"A crown," said the Sculptor.</seg>
<seg id="642">“一块银元。”雕刻家回答说。</seg>
<seg id="643">"Is that all?" said he, laughing;</seg>
<seg id="643">“就这么多？”他笑着问，</seg>
<seg id="644">"and" (pointing to one of Juno) "how much is that one?"</seg>
<seg id="644">“那么，”（他指着朱诺的像——朱庇特的妻子）“这一尊要多少钱？”</seg>
<seg id="645">"That," was the reply, "is half a crown."</seg>
<seg id="645">雕刻家回答说：“那个要半块银元。”</seg>
<seg id="646">"And how much might you be wanting for that one over there, now?" he continued, pointing to a statue of himself.</seg>
<seg id="646">“那边那个雕像，你想卖多少钱呢？”他指着自己的雕像继续问道。</seg>
<seg id="647">"That one?" said the Sculptor;</seg>
<seg id="647">“那个？”雕刻家说，</seg>
<seg id="648">"Oh, I'll throw him in for nothing if you'll buy the other two."</seg>
<seg id="648">“假如你要买那两个的话，我便把这个白送给你。”</seg>
<seg id="649">THE FAWN AND HIS MOTHER</seg>
<seg id="649">小鹿和妈妈</seg>
<seg id="650">A Hind said to her Fawn, who was now well grown and strong, "My son, Nature has given you a powerful body and a stout pair of horns, and I can't think why you are such a coward as to run away from the hounds."</seg>
<seg id="650">一只母鹿对已经长大了的小鹿说：“我的儿子，自然赋予了你健硕的体魄和一对结实的鹿角，我简直想不到，你为何这么胆小，竟然会从猎狗身边逃跑。”</seg>
<seg id="651">Just then they both heard the sound of a pack in full cry, but at a considerable distance.</seg>
<seg id="651">就在这时，母子俩都听到了远处一群猎狗的狂吠声。</seg>
<seg id="652">"You stay where you are," said the Hind; "never mind me":</seg>
<seg id="652">“你就待在原地吧，”母鹿说，“不要管我。”</seg>
<seg id="653">and with that she ran off as fast as her legs could carry her.</seg>
<seg id="653">话音刚落，她就飞也似的跑了。</seg>
<seg id="654">THE FOX AND THE LION</seg>
<seg id="654">狐狸和狮子</seg>
<seg id="655">A Fox who had never seen a Lion one day met one, and was so terrified at the sight of him that he was ready to die with fear.</seg>
<seg id="655">有一天，从来没有见过狮子的一只狐狸第一次碰见了狮子，刚看见狮子的一刹那，狐狸竟被吓得半死。</seg>
<seg id="656">After a time he met him again, and was still rather frightened, but not nearly so much as he had been when he met him first.</seg>
<seg id="656">没过多久，他又一次遇到了狮子，仍然很害怕，但是已经不像第一次见到时那样了。</seg>
<seg id="657">But when he saw him for the third time he was so far from being afraid that he went up to him and began to talk to him as if he had known him all his life.</seg>
<seg id="657">然而，当狐狸第三次遇到狮子时，他竟有胆量走上前去与狮子交谈，仿佛老朋友一样。</seg>
<seg id="658">THE EAGLE AND HIS CAPTOR</seg>
<seg id="658">鹰与捕鹰者</seg>
<seg id="659">A Man once caught an Eagle, and after clipping his wings turned him loose among the fowls in his hen-house, where he moped in a corner, looking very dejected and forlorn.</seg>
<seg id="659">从前，有一个人捉住了一只鹰，随后便剪断了他的翅膀，放入鸡窝中与其它家禽一起饲养，鹰一直待在角落里暗自悲伤，看上去甚为沮丧和绝望。</seg>
<seg id="660">After a while his Captor was glad enough to sell him to a neighbour, who took him home and let his wings grow again.</seg>
<seg id="660">没过多久，捕获老鹰的那个人很高兴地将鹰卖给了一个邻居，邻居把鹰带回家后又帮他长出了新的翅膀。</seg>
<seg id="661">As soon as he had recovered the use of them, the Eagle flew out and caught a hare, which he brought home and presented to his benefactor.</seg>
<seg id="661">鹰飞出去抓住一只兔子，立刻带回家给恩人。</seg>
<seg id="662">A fox observed this, and said to the Eagle, "Don't waste your gifts on him!</seg>
<seg id="662">一只狐狸看到后，便对老鹰说：“不要在他身上浪费你的猎物！</seg>
<seg id="663">Go and give them to the man who first caught you; make him your friend, and then perhaps he won't catch you and clip your wings a second time."</seg>
<seg id="663">把这份礼物送给以前捕获你的那个人，和他交个朋友，那么，或许他不会再次捕获你，并剪断你的翅膀。”</seg>
<seg id="664">THE BLACKSMITH AND HIS DOG</seg>
<seg id="664">铁匠与小狗</seg>
<seg id="665">A Blacksmith had a little Dog, which used to sleep when his master was at work, but was very wide awake indeed when it was time for meals.</seg>
<seg id="665">铁匠家有一条小狗，小狗常常在主人打铁时睡觉，但是一到了吃饭时间，便异常清醒起来。</seg>
<seg id="666">One day his master pretended to be disgusted at this, and when he had thrown him a bone as usual, he said, "What on earth is the good of a lazy cur like you?</seg>
<seg id="666">有一天，铁匠假装对此很生气，一边像往常一样扔给小狗一块骨头，一边说：“地球上还有像你一样懒惰的坏蛋吗？</seg>
<seg id="667">When I am hammering away at my anvil, you just curl up and go to sleep:</seg>
<seg id="667">你这家伙，总是在我卖力工作时，蜷缩起来睡觉，</seg>
<seg id="668">but no sooner do I stop for a mouthful of food than you wake up and wag your tail to be fed."</seg>
<seg id="668">可是，只要我一停下来吃点东西，你就清醒地摇着尾巴过来讨饭吃。”</seg>
<seg id="669">Those who will not work deserve to starve.</seg>
<seg id="669">不卖力工作的人理应挨饿。</seg>
<seg id="670">THE STAG AT THE POOL</seg>
<seg id="670">池边的雄鹿</seg>
<seg id="671">A thirsty Stag went down to a pool to drink.</seg>
<seg id="671">一只非常口渴的鹿，跑到池塘边去喝水。</seg>
<seg id="672">As he bent over the surface he saw his own reflection in the water, and was struck with admiration for his fine spreading antlers, but at the same time he felt nothing but disgust for the weakness and slenderness of his legs.</seg>
<seg id="672">当他在池边俯下身去喝水时，看到了水面上自己的倒影，一边得意洋洋地欣赏着自己那完美修长的鹿角，一边又为自己的小细腿而闷闷不乐。</seg>
<seg id="673">While he stood there looking at himself, he was seen and attacked by a Lion;</seg>
<seg id="673">正当他看得入神时，被一头看见他的狮子袭击了。</seg>
<seg id="674">but in the chase which ensued, he soon drew away from his pursuer, and kept his lead as long as the ground over which he ran was open and free of trees.</seg>
<seg id="674">他拼命地向着空旷、没有树木的平原跑去，很快就摆脱了身后的追逐者。</seg>
<seg id="675">But coming presently to a wood, he was caught by his antlers in the branches, and fell a victim to the teeth and claws of his enemy.</seg>
<seg id="675">可是，当他跑进一片树林中时，眼看着那美丽的鹿角就被挂在了树枝上，终于被跟踪而来的敌人擒获，成了狮子的美味佳肴。</seg>
<seg id="676">"Woe is me!" he cried with his last breath;</seg>
<seg id="676">“真是不幸呀！”鹿在临死前哀叹道，</seg>
<seg id="677">"I despised my legs, which might have saved my life:</seg>
<seg id="677">“我小瞧了自己的腿，可是它们却救了我的命；</seg>
<seg id="678">but I gloried in my horns, and they have proved my ruin."</seg>
<seg id="678">我以自己的角为傲，可是它们却葬送了我的性命。”</seg>
<seg id="679">What is worth most is often valued least.</seg>
<seg id="679">最值得的东西往往被视为最没价值的。</seg>
<seg id="680">THE DOG AND THE SHADOW</seg>
<seg id="680">叼着肉的狗</seg>
<seg id="681">A Dog was crossing a plank bridge over a stream with a piece of meat in his mouth, when he happened to see his own reflection in the water.</seg>
<seg id="681">一条狗嘴里叼着一块肉，在穿过小河上的一个木板桥时，碰巧看见了水中自己的倒影。</seg>
<seg id="682">He thought it was another dog with a piece of meat twice as big;</seg>
<seg id="682">他以为是另一条狗叼着一块更大的肉，</seg>
<seg id="683">so he let go his own, and flew at the other dog to get the larger piece.</seg>
<seg id="683">于是，他扑到水中，想去抢另一条狗嘴里那块更大的肉。</seg>
<seg id="684">But, of course, all that happened was that he got neither;</seg>
<seg id="684">然而，他最终什么也没有得到。</seg>
<seg id="685">for one was only a shadow, and the other was carried away by the current.</seg>
<seg id="685">因为水中那块肉本来就只是个影子，而原来的那块肉也被河水冲走了。</seg>
<seg id="686">MERCURY AND THE TRADESMEN</seg>
<seg id="686">墨丘利与商人</seg>
<seg id="687">When Jupiter was creating man, he told Mercury to make an infusion of lies, and to add a little of it to the other ingredients which went to the making of the Tradesmen.</seg>
<seg id="687">朱庇特在创造人类时，吩咐墨丘利制造一点让人说谎的药，并添加到其他要素上，从而形成商人。</seg>
<seg id="688">Mercury did so, and introduced an equal amount into each in turn--the tallow-chandler, and the greengrocer, and the haberdasher, and all, till he came to the horse-dealer, who was last on the list, when, finding that he had a quantity of the infusion still left, he put it all into him.</seg>
<seg id="688">墨丘利遵命研制好药之后，依次平均地添加到每种生意人身上——卖蜡烛的商贩、卖蔬菜瓜果的商贩、卖杂货的商贩等。最后轮到了马贩子，这是最后一个要添药的商人了，但是墨丘利却发现还剩下很多药，于是，他便将剩余的药全部加在了马贩子身上。</seg>
<seg id="689">This is why all Tradesmen lie more or less, but they none of them lie like a horse-dealer.</seg>
<seg id="689">这正是商人多少都会说谎的原因，尤其是马贩子更为厉害。</seg>
<seg id="690">THE MICE AND THE WEASELS</seg>
<seg id="690">老鼠和黄鼠狼</seg>
<seg id="691">There was war between the Mice and the Weasels, in which the Mice always got the worst of it, numbers of them being killed and eaten by the Weasels.</seg>
<seg id="691">老鼠和黄鼠狼打起仗来，老鼠每次都处于劣势，大量老鼠都被黄鼠狼杀死并吃掉了。</seg>
<seg id="692">So they called a council of war, in which an old Mouse got up and said, "It's no wonder we are always beaten, for we have no generals to plan our battles and direct our movements in the field."</seg>
<seg id="692">于是，他们召开了一次战事会议，其中，一个年长的老鼠站起来发言：“毫无疑问，我们总是被打败的一方，因为没有统领来规划我们的战斗，在战场上指挥我们的行动，所以才会屡次失败。”</seg>
<seg id="693">Acting on his advice, they chose the biggest Mice to be their leaders, and these, in order to be distinguished from the rank and file, provided themselves with helmets bearing large plumes of straw.</seg>
<seg id="693">根据他的建议，老鼠们推选出那些个头大的老鼠作为带队将领，并且，为了在老鼠群中区分这些将领，还让他们戴上用草编成的头盔。</seg>
<seg id="694">They then led out the Mice to battle, confident of victory:</seg>
<seg id="694">然后，老鼠带着必胜的信心再次投入到战斗中。</seg>
<seg id="695">but they were defeated as usual, and were soon scampering as fast as they could to their holes.</seg>
<seg id="695">可是，他们依旧被打败了，鼠群纷纷逃回洞中。</seg>
<seg id="696">All made their way to safety without difficulty except the leaders, who were so hampered by the badges of their rank that they could not get into their holes, and fell easy victims to their pursuers.</seg>
<seg id="696">除了那些将领之外，所有老鼠都轻易地逃进了洞里，因为头盔妨碍他们钻进小小的老鼠洞，所以将领们都被黄鼠狼吃掉了。</seg>
<seg id="697">Greatness carries its own penalties.</seg>
<seg id="697">伟大的形象也要付出代价。</seg>
<seg id="698">THE PEACOCK AND JUNO</seg>
<seg id="698">孔雀和朱诺</seg>
<seg id="699">The Peacock was greatly discontented because he had not a beautiful voice like the nightingale, and he went and complained to Juno about it.</seg>
<seg id="699">因为自己没有夜莺那悠扬动听的歌声，孔雀大为不悦，于是跑到朱诺面前抱怨。</seg>
<seg id="700">"The nightingale's song," said he, "is the envy of all the birds;</seg>
<seg id="700">“所有的鸟都羡慕夜莺的歌声，”她说，</seg>
<seg id="701">but whenever I utter a sound I become a laughing-stock."</seg>
<seg id="701">“但是，只要我一开口发声，就成了大家的笑料。”</seg>
<seg id="702">The goddess tried to console him by saying, "You have not, it is true, the power of song, but then you far excel all the rest in beauty:</seg>
<seg id="702">女神朱诺为了尽量安慰她，说道：“你的确没有唱歌的优势，但是你却有着超凡的美丽外表。</seg>
<seg id="703">your neck flashes like the emerald and your splendid tail is a marvel of gorgeous colour."</seg>
<seg id="703">你的脖子闪耀着绿宝石一样的光辉，你那开屏的尾巴更是华丽富贵、光彩照人。”</seg>
<seg id="704">But the Peacock was not appeased.</seg>
<seg id="704">然而，孔雀仍旧不满足。</seg>
<seg id="705">"What is the use," said he, "of being beautiful, with a voice like mine?"</seg>
<seg id="705">“我的声音那么难听，”孔雀说，“美丽又有什么用呀？”</seg>
<seg id="706">Then Juno replied, with a shade of sternness in her tones, "Fate has allotted to all their destined gifts: to yourself beauty, to the eagle strength, to the nightingale song, and so on to all the rest in their degree;</seg>
<seg id="706">朱诺接着回答说：“命运赋予了每个人不同的礼物——赋予了你无比的美丽，赋予了老鹰强大的力量，赋予了夜莺优美的歌声，以此类推下去，所有生命都有着各自的特征，</seg>
<seg id="707">but you alone are dissatisfied with your portion.</seg>
<seg id="707">而你却不满足于自己所拥有的。</seg>
<seg id="708">Make, then, no more complaints.</seg>
<seg id="708">不要再抱怨了，</seg>
<seg id="709">For, if your present wish were granted, you would quickly find cause for fresh discontent."</seg>
<seg id="709">因为如果你当下的愿望得到了满足，很快你又会找到另一个不满足的借口。”</seg>
<seg id="710">THE BEAR AND THE FOX</seg>
<seg id="710">熊与狐狸</seg>
<seg id="711">A Bear was once bragging about his generous feelings, and saying how refined he was compared with other animals.</seg>
<seg id="711">有一只熊曾经大肆鼓吹自己多么仁慈，与其它动物相比，自己是多么文雅。</seg>
<seg id="712">(There is, in fact, a tradition that a Bear will never touch a dead body.)</seg>
<seg id="712">（其实，绝不碰死人是熊的一贯传统。）</seg>
<seg id="713">A Fox, who heard him talking in this strain, smiled and said, "My friend, when you are hungry, I only wish you would confine your attention to the dead and leave the living alone."</seg>
<seg id="713">一只狐狸听到这些话，面带微笑地对熊说：“我的朋友，当你饥饿难耐时，我希望你也能将注意力集中在死人身上，不再吃活人了！”</seg>
<seg id="714">A hypocrite deceives no one but himself.</seg>
<seg id="714">骗子只会掩耳盗铃似的欺骗自己。</seg>
<seg id="715">THE ASS AND THE OLD PEASANT</seg>
<seg id="715">驴和老农夫</seg>
<seg id="716">An old Peasant was sitting in a meadow watching his Ass, which was grazing close by, when all of a sudden he caught sight of armed men stealthily approaching.</seg>
<seg id="716">一位老农民正坐在草地上看驴，驴被紧紧盯着。突然农民看到全副武装的人们走近，</seg>
<seg id="717">He jumped up in a moment, and begged the Ass to fly with him as fast as he could,</seg>
<seg id="717">便立刻跳了起来，恳请驴跟他一起尽快飞走。</seg>
<seg id="718">"Or else," said he, "we shall both be captured by the enemy."</seg>
<seg id="718">“否则，”他说，“我们便会被敌人逮住。”</seg>
<seg id="719">But the Ass just looked round lazily and said, "And if so, do you think they'll make me carry heavier loads than I have to now?"</seg>
<seg id="719">驴只是懒懒地看了看，便说：“如果这样的话，你不认为他们会让我驮更重的东西？”</seg>
<seg id="720">"No," said his master.</seg>
<seg id="720">“不，”主人说。</seg>
<seg id="721">"Oh, well, then," said the Ass, "I don't mind if they do take me, for I shan't be any worse off."</seg>
<seg id="721">“哦，那么，”驴说，“我不介意他们把我抓走，我再也不会比现在更糟了。”</seg>
<seg id="722">THE OX AND THE FROG</seg>
<seg id="722">牛和青蛙</seg>
<seg id="723">Two little Frogs were playing about at the edge of a pool when an Ox came down to the water to drink, and by accident trod on one of them and crushed the life out of him.</seg>
<seg id="723">两只小青蛙在池塘边玩耍时，一头公牛走到水边去喝水，结果不小心踩扁了其中一只小青蛙，使其当场毙命。</seg>
<seg id="724">When the old Frog missed him, she asked his brother where he was.</seg>
<seg id="724">青蛙妈妈发现小青蛙不见了，便问另一只小青蛙，他的兄弟到哪里去了。</seg>
<seg id="725">"He is dead, mother," said the little Frog;</seg>
<seg id="725">“妈妈，他死了。”小青蛙说，</seg>
<seg id="726">"an enormous big creature with four legs came to our pool this morning and trampled him down in the mud."</seg>
<seg id="726">“今天上午有一个长着四只脚的巨型怪物来到水塘边，把我的兄弟踩进了泥巴里。”</seg>
<seg id="727">"Enormous, was he?</seg>
<seg id="727">“巨型兽？</seg>
<seg id="728">Was he as big as this?" said the Frog, puffing herself out to look as big as possible.</seg>
<seg id="728">是不是这么大？”青蛙妈妈一边问，一边尽力鼓气，让自己尽量变大一些。</seg>
<seg id="729">"Oh! yes, much bigger," was the answer.</seg>
<seg id="729">“嗯，是的，比这还要大。”小青蛙说。</seg>
<seg id="730">The Frog puffed herself out still more. "Was he as big as this?" said she.</seg>
<seg id="730">青蛙妈妈再鼓了鼓气，问道：“是不是这般大小呢？”</seg>
<seg id="731">"Oh! yes, yes, mother, MUCH bigger," said the little Frog.</seg>
<seg id="731">“对，妈妈，比这个还要再大一些。”小青蛙说。</seg>
<seg id="732">And yet again she puffed and puffed herself out till she was almost as round as a ball.</seg>
<seg id="732">于是，青蛙妈妈又使劲鼓气，几乎快成了一个圆球。</seg>
<seg id="733">"As big as...?" she began--but then she burst.</seg>
<seg id="733">“有这么大……”还没等她说完，就把肚子胀破了。</seg>
<seg id="734">THE MAN AND THE IMAGE</seg>
<seg id="734">人和神像</seg>
<seg id="735">A poor Man had a wooden Image of a god, to which he used to pray daily for riches.</seg>
<seg id="735">一个穷人在家里供奉了一尊木头神像，天天对着神像祈祷让自己发财。</seg>
<seg id="736">He did this for a long time, but remained as poor as ever, till one day he caught up the Image in disgust and hurled it with all his strength against the wall.</seg>
<seg id="736">持续了相当一段时间后，他依旧像过去那样贫穷。有一天，这个人带着极度的愤怒抓起神像，用尽全力冲着墙壁扔过去。</seg>
<seg id="737">The force of the blow split open the head and a quantity of gold coins fell out upon the floor.</seg>
<seg id="737">强大的撞击力打破了神像的头，一些金币纷纷掉在了地板上。</seg>
<seg id="738">The Man gathered them up greedily, and said, "O you old fraud, you!</seg>
<seg id="738">这个人贪婪地抓起金币，说：“哦，你这个大骗子！</seg>
<seg id="739">When I honoured you, you did me no good whatever: but no sooner do I treat you to insults and violence than you make a rich man of me!"</seg>
<seg id="739">我好好供奉你的时候，你却什么都不给我；等我用暴力对待你的时候，你却让我成了富翁！”</seg>
<seg id="740">HERCULES AND THE WAGGONER</seg>
<seg id="740">赫刺克勒斯和车夫</seg>
<seg id="741">A Waggoner was driving his team along a muddy lane with a full load behind them, when the wheels of his waggon sank so deep in the mire that no efforts of his horses could move them.</seg>
<seg id="741">有一个车夫驾着一辆载着货物的马车，正当他沿着乡间小路前进时，车轮突然深陷入泥坑中，拉车的马无论如何也挪不出车轮来。</seg>
<seg id="742">As he stood there, looking helplessly on, and calling loudly at intervals upon Hercules for assistance, the god himself appeared, and said to him, "Put your shoulder to the wheel, man, and goad on your horses, and then you may call on Hercules to assist you.</seg>
<seg id="742">车夫站在那里，无助地四处观望，大声呼喊着大力神前来帮忙。大力神赫刺克勒斯终于出现了，对他说：“先用你的肩膀顶住车轮，再用鞭子赶你的马，试着这样做了之后，再来祈求我的帮助。</seg>
<seg id="743">If you won't lift a finger to help yourself, you can't expect Hercules or any one else to come to your aid."</seg>
<seg id="743">如果你不能先自助，就不能期望大力神或其他人来帮你了。”</seg>
<seg id="744">Heaven helps those who help themselves.</seg>
<seg id="744">自助者，天助之。</seg>
<seg id="745">THE POMEGRANATE, THE APPLE-TREE, AND THE BRAMBLE</seg>
<seg id="745">石榴树、苹果树和野蔷薇</seg>
<seg id="746">A Pomegranate and an Apple-tree were disputing about the quality of their fruits, and each claimed that its own was the better of the two.</seg>
<seg id="746">石榴树与苹果树为谁的果实质量最好而争吵不休，双方都认为自己的更好。</seg>
<seg id="747">High words passed between them, and a violent quarrel was imminent, when a Bramble impudently poked its head out of a neighbouring hedge and said, "There, that's enough, my friends;</seg>
<seg id="747">愤怒的话语相继从他们的嘴里脱口而出，激烈的争吵马上就要升级了，这时，野蔷薇嬉皮笑脸地从隔壁篱笆丛中探出头来，说：“够了，朋友们，</seg>
<seg id="748">don't let us quarrel."</seg>
<seg id="748">我们不要再争吵了。”</seg>
<seg id="749">THE LION, THE BEAR, AND THE FOX</seg>
<seg id="749">狮子、熊和狐狸</seg>
<seg id="750">A Lion and a Bear were fighting for possession of a kid, which they had both seized at the same moment.</seg>
<seg id="750">狮子和熊同时抓到了一只小羊羔，他们俩为争夺小羊羔凶狠地打了起来。</seg>
<seg id="751">The battle was long and fierce, and at length both of them were exhausted, and lay upon the ground severely wounded and gasping for breath.</seg>
<seg id="751">经过一场苦斗，双方都受了重伤，有气无力地躺在地上。</seg>
<seg id="752">A Fox had all the time been prowling round and watching the fight: and when he saw the combatants lying there too weak to move, he slipped in and seized the kid, and ran off with it.</seg>
<seg id="752">一只狐狸早已躲在远处观望着，一见他们俩都直挺挺地躺在地上虚弱地一动不动，他便溜过去抓起羊羔，一溜烟地跑掉了。</seg>
<seg id="753">They looked on helplessly, and one said to the other, "Here we've been mauling each other all this while, and no one the better for it except the Fox!"</seg>
<seg id="753">狮子和熊眼睁睁地看着狐狸抢走了小羊羔，却也毫无办法，只能唉声叹气地说：“我们俩斗得两败俱伤，却让狐狸得到了好处！”</seg>
<seg id="754">THE TWO SOLDIERS AND THE ROBBER</seg>
<seg id="754">两个士兵和强盗</seg>
<seg id="755">Two Soldiers travelling together were set upon by a Robber.</seg>
<seg id="755">两个士兵一起赶路，途中被一个强盗所劫。</seg>
<seg id="756">One of them ran away, but the other stood his ground, and laid about him so lustily with his sword that the Robber was fain to fly and leave him in peace.</seg>
<seg id="756">其中一个士兵马上逃跑了，另一个则勇敢地握着剑立在原地，强盗不得不弃他而逃。</seg>
<seg id="757">When the coast was clear the timid one ran back, and, flourishing his weapon, cried in a threatening voice, "Where is he?</seg>
<seg id="757">这时，那个胆小的士兵跑过来，抽出剑，壮着胆大喝一声：“他去哪里了？</seg>
<seg id="758">Let me get at him, and I'll soon let him know whom he's got to deal with."</seg>
<seg id="758">让我来对付他，我要让他知道面对的是什么人。”</seg>
<seg id="759">But the other replied, "You are a little late, my friend:</seg>
<seg id="759">然而，那名勇敢的士兵说：“你来晚了，我的朋友。</seg>
<seg id="760">I only wish you had backed me up just now, even if you had done no more than speak, for I should have been encouraged, believing your words to be true.</seg>
<seg id="760">要是你刚才能来帮我就好了，即便只是嘴上这样说也好，因为我会受到你这番话的鼓舞，并且相信这些话都是真的。</seg>
<seg id="761">As it is, calm yourself, and put up your sword: there is no further use for it.</seg>
<seg id="761">而现在，还是请你把剑收好，已经没有必要再用它了。</seg>
<seg id="762">You may delude others into thinking you're as brave as a lion:</seg>
<seg id="762">你只能欺骗其他人，让人们以为你像雄狮一样勇敢；</seg>
<seg id="763">but I know that, at the first sign of danger, you run away like a hare."</seg>
<seg id="763">而我却知道，在遇到危险时，你会像兔子一样落荒而逃。”</seg>
<seg id="764">THE LION AND THE WILD ASS</seg>
<seg id="764">狮子和野驴</seg>
<seg id="765">A Lion and a Wild Ass went out hunting together:</seg>
<seg id="765">一只狮子和一头野驴联合外出觅食——</seg>
<seg id="766">the latter was to run down the prey by his superior speed, and the former would then come up and despatch it.</seg>
<seg id="766">野驴能以超快的速度追赶猎物，而狮子则能迅速赶来捕获猎物。</seg>
<seg id="767">They met with great success;</seg>
<seg id="767">他们成功地抓获了猎物，</seg>
<seg id="768">and when it came to sharing the spoil the Lion divided it all into three equal portions.</seg>
<seg id="768">然后，狮子把猎物分成了三份。</seg>
<seg id="769">"I will take the first," said he, "because I am King of the beasts;</seg>
<seg id="769">“我来拿第一份，”狮子说，“因为我是百兽之王；</seg>
<seg id="770">I will also take the second, because, as your partner, I am entitled to half of what remains;</seg>
<seg id="770">第二份也归我，因为作为你的合作者，我理应分享剩下的一半；</seg>
<seg id="771">and as for the third--well, unless you give it up to me and take yourself off pretty quick, the third, believe me, will make you feel very sorry for yourself!"</seg>
<seg id="771">至于这第三份，除非你自愿让给我，然后乖乖地滚开，否则你一定会为此而抱憾终身！”</seg>
<seg id="772">Might makes right.</seg>
<seg id="772">强者为王。</seg>
<seg id="773">THE MAN AND THE SATYR</seg>
<seg id="773">人与森林之神萨堤罗斯</seg>
<seg id="774">A Man and a Satyr became friends, and determined to live together.</seg>
<seg id="774">从前，有个人与森林之神萨堤罗斯成了朋友，他们决定一起生活。</seg>
<seg id="775">All went well for a while, until one day in winter-time the Satyr saw the Man blowing on his hands.</seg>
<seg id="775">在一段时间内，一切都很顺利，直到冬季里的一天，萨堤罗斯看到那个人把手放到嘴边不断地呵气。</seg>
<seg id="776">"Why do you do that?" he asked.</seg>
<seg id="776">“你为什么要这样做？”他问道。</seg>
<seg id="777">"To warm my hands," said the Man.</seg>
<seg id="777">“为了暖和我的手呀。”那人回答道。</seg>
<seg id="778">That same day, when they sat down to supper together, they each had a steaming hot bowl of porridge, and the Man raised his bowl to his mouth and blew on it.</seg>
<seg id="778">就在同一天，他们坐下来一起吃饭，每人面前都摆着一碗热气腾腾的粥，那人举起碗来对着嘴又开始吹气。</seg>
<seg id="779">"Why do you do that?" asked the Satyr.</seg>
<seg id="779">“你为什么要这样做？”森林之神又问他。</seg>
<seg id="780">"To cool my porridge," said the Man.</seg>
<seg id="780">“为了让粥凉下来。”他说。</seg>
<seg id="781">The Satyr got up from the table.</seg>
<seg id="781">森林之神立刻站起来，说：</seg>
<seg id="782">"Good-bye," said he, "I'm going:</seg>
<seg id="782">“再见，朋友！</seg>
<seg id="783">I can't be friends with a man who blows hot and cold with the same breath."</seg>
<seg id="783">我要走了，我无法和你这样的人交朋友，因为你的嘴里一会儿吹热气，一会儿又吹冷气。”</seg>
<seg id="784">THE IMAGE-SELLER</seg>
<seg id="784">卖神像的人</seg>
<seg id="785">A certain man made a wooden Image of Mercury, and exposed it for sale in the market.</seg>
<seg id="785">有个人用木头雕刻了墨丘利的像，拿到市场上去卖。</seg>
<seg id="786">As no one offered to buy it, however, he thought he would try to attract a purchaser by proclaiming the virtues of the Image.</seg>
<seg id="786">因为没有一个买主前来光顾，他便认为自己应该大声叫喊，以此吸引人前来购买。</seg>
<seg id="787">So he cried up and down the market, "A god for sale! a god for sale!</seg>
<seg id="787">于是，他冲着市场里大喊：“卖神像了！卖神像了！</seg>
<seg id="788">One who'll bring you luck and keep you lucky!"</seg>
<seg id="788">一个能给你带来好运并维持好运的神像！”</seg>
<seg id="789">Presently one of the bystanders stopped him and said, "If your god is all you make him out to be, how is it you don't keep him and make the most of him yourself?"</seg>
<seg id="789">这时，旁边的一个人对他说：“喂，朋友，如果你的神像真如你所说，那你为何不自己留下他，好好享受他给你的好运呢？”</seg>
<seg id="790">"I'll tell you why," replied he; "he brings gain, it is true, but he takes his time about it; whereas I want money at once."</seg>
<seg id="790">“告诉你吧，”这个人回答道，“他的确能让你有所收获，这是真的，但是需要时间，而我则希望能马上得到钱。”</seg>
<seg id="791">THE EAGLE AND THE ARROW</seg>
<seg id="791">老鹰与箭</seg>
<seg id="792">An Eagle sat perched on a lofty rock, keeping a sharp look-out for prey.</seg>
<seg id="792">鹰站在一块高高的岩石上，用锐利的目光观察着猎物。</seg>
<seg id="793">A huntsman, concealed in a cleft of the mountain and on the watch for game, spied him there and shot an Arrow at him.</seg>
<seg id="793">一个猎人躲藏在山间的裂缝中观察情况，看到鹰之后，一箭射中了他。</seg>
<seg id="794">The shaft struck him full in the breast and pierced him through and through.</seg>
<seg id="794">那箭直插入鹰的前胸，并且破膛而出。</seg>
<seg id="795">As he lay in the agonies of death, he turned his eyes upon the Arrow.</seg>
<seg id="795">受着死亡苦痛折磨的老鹰，转眼又看到了带着鹰毛的箭翎。</seg>
<seg id="796">"Ah! cruel fate!" he cried, "that I should perish thus:</seg>
<seg id="796">“啊！命运真残酷！”他哭喊着，“竟然让我这样死去，</seg>
<seg id="797">but oh! fate more cruel still, that the Arrow which kills me should be winged with an Eagle's feathers!"</seg>
<seg id="797">不过，更为残酷的是，杀死我的箭上竟然还插着鹰的羽毛！”</seg>
<seg id="798">THE RICH MAN AND THE TANNER</seg>
<seg id="798">富人和制皮匠</seg>
<seg id="799">A Rich Man took up his residence next door to a Tanner, and found the smell of the tan-yard so extremely unpleasant that he told him he must go.</seg>
<seg id="799">一个富人与制皮匠比邻而居，发现皮匠院子里传出的气味实在让人受不了，便告诉皮匠请他搬家。</seg>
<seg id="800">The Tanner delayed his departure, and the Rich Man had to speak to him several times about it; and every time the Tanner said he was making arrangements to move very shortly.</seg>
<seg id="800">制皮匠一直在拖延，富人重复说了好多次让他快点搬家，皮匠每次总是说马上就搬，却老是不采取行动。</seg>
<seg id="801">This went on for some time, till at last the Rich Man got so used to the smell that he ceased to mind it, and troubled the Tanner with his objections no more.</seg>
<seg id="801">就这样持续了一段时间，富人已经闻惯了皮革的臭气，也就不再非难制皮匠了。</seg>
<seg id="802">THE WOLF, THE MOTHER, AND HER CHILD</seg>
<seg id="802">狼、妈妈和孩子</seg>
<seg id="803">A hungry Wolf was prowling about in search of food.</seg>
<seg id="803">一只饥饿的狼四处寻觅食物。</seg>
<seg id="804">By and by, attracted by the cries of a Child, he came to a cottage.</seg>
<seg id="804">走着走着，他被小孩子的哭声吸引，来到了一个农舍。</seg>
<seg id="805">As he crouched beneath the window, he heard the Mother say to the Child, "Stop crying, do! or I'll throw you to the Wolf."</seg>
<seg id="805">他在窗下屏息而立，只听到母亲对小孩子说：“别哭了，不然我就把你扔出去喂狼。”</seg>
<seg id="806">Thinking she really meant what she said, he waited there a long time in the expectation of satisfying his hunger.</seg>
<seg id="806">狼信以为真，以为她真会这样做，便站在门外等着，期待着快点能满足自己的食欲。</seg>
<seg id="807">In the evening he heard the Mother fondling her Child and saying, "If the naughty Wolf comes, he shan't get my little one:</seg>
<seg id="807">直到傍晚来临，他又听见母亲在哄小孩子：“要是狼真的来了，</seg>
<seg id="808">Daddy will kill him."</seg>
<seg id="808">爸爸就会杀死他的。”</seg>
<seg id="809">The Wolf got up in much disgust and walked away:</seg>
<seg id="809">狼听了这话后，气愤地赶紧跑开了，</seg>
<seg id="810">"As for the people in that house," said he to himself, "you can't believe a word they say."</seg>
<seg id="810">他边跑边想：“那个房子里的人说的话，一句也不能信。”</seg>
<seg id="811">THE OLD WOMAN AND THE WINE-JAR</seg>
<seg id="811">老太婆和酒瓶</seg>
<seg id="812">An old Woman picked up an empty Wine-jar which had once contained a rare and costly wine, and which still retained some traces of its exquisite bouquet.</seg>
<seg id="812">一个老太婆捡到一个空酒瓶，这个瓶子曾经装过价格不菲的稀世美酒，依然还带着浓浓的酒香。</seg>
<seg id="813">She raised it to her nose and sniffed at it again and again.</seg>
<seg id="813">她把酒瓶放在鼻孔处，一次又一次贪婪地吸着酒香，</seg>
<seg id="814">"Ah," she cried, "how delicious must have been the liquid which has left behind so ravishing a smell."</seg>
<seg id="814">并说：“啊，多么甜美！连装过酒的空瓶都能留下这样甘美难忘的香味，那瓶子里的酒还真不知道会多么甘美醇香呢。”</seg>
<seg id="815">THE LIONESS AND THE VIXEN</seg>
<seg id="815">母狮与雌狐</seg>
<seg id="816">A Lioness and a Vixen were talking together about their young, as mothers will, and saying how healthy and well-grown they were, and what beautiful coats they had, and how they were the image of their parents.</seg>
<seg id="816">一头母狮与一只狐狸在闲聊自己的孩子，出于母亲的美好愿望，她们都在说自己的孩子多么健康，多么茁壮，多么美丽，多么像自己的父母。</seg>
<seg id="817">"My litter of cubs is a joy to see," said the Fox;</seg>
<seg id="817">“看到我产下的小幼崽，真让人高兴，”狐狸说，</seg>
<seg id="818">and then she added, rather maliciously, "But I notice you never have more than one."</seg>
<seg id="818">接着她又不怀好意地说，“但是我注意到你从未生过两胎或更多的幼崽。”</seg>
<seg id="819">"No," said the Lioness grimly, "but that one's a lion."</seg>
<seg id="819">“没有，”母狮面无表情地回答道，“可我生下的毕竟是一只狮子。”</seg>
<seg id="820">Quality, not quantity.</seg>
<seg id="820">注重质量，而非数量。</seg>
<seg id="821">THE VIPER AND THE FILE</seg>
<seg id="821">毒蛇和锉刀</seg>
<seg id="822">A Viper entered a carpenter's shop, and went from one to another of the tools, begging for something to eat.</seg>
<seg id="822">有条毒蛇爬进铁匠铺里，从一个工具到另一个工具，祈求能给他点可以吃的东西。</seg>
<seg id="823">Among the rest, he addressed himself to the File, and asked for the favour of a meal.</seg>
<seg id="823">其中，他向锉刀请求施舍，给他一顿饱餐。</seg>
<seg id="824">The File replied in a tone of pitying contempt, "What a simpleton you must be if you imagine you will get anything from me, who invariably take from every one and never give anything in return."</seg>
<seg id="824">可是，锉刀却带着不屑的语气说：“你若想从我这里得到东西，那你真是太傻了，我历来只会索取，不会回报。”</seg>
<seg id="825">The covetous are poor givers.</seg>
<seg id="825">贪婪之人是最小气的施予者。</seg>
<seg id="826">THE CAT AND THE COCK</seg>
<seg id="826">猫和公鸡</seg>
<seg id="827">A Cat pounced on a Cock, and cast about for some good excuse for making a meal off him, for Cats don't as a rule eat Cocks, and she knew she ought not to.</seg>
<seg id="827">一只猫抓到一只公鸡，并想方设法找出一个借口好吃掉他，因为不吃鸡是猫的一贯传统，而她也知道自己不应该吃鸡。</seg>
<seg id="828">At last she said, "You make a great nuisance of yourself at night by crowing and keeping people awake:</seg>
<seg id="828">最后，猫说：“你总在夜晚打鸣，让人们不能好好睡觉，</seg>
<seg id="829">so I am going to make an end of you."</seg>
<seg id="829">所以，我要吃掉你。”</seg>
<seg id="830">But the Cock defended himself by saying that he crowed in order that men might wake up and set about the day's work in good time, and that they really couldn't very well do without him.</seg>
<seg id="830">但是，公鸡却辩解说，自己为了人们的利益而叫醒他们，可使人们按时起床工作，若是没有了鸡，人们就无法准时起床工作了。</seg>
<seg id="831">"That may be," said the Cat, "but whether they can or not, I'm not going without my dinner";</seg>
<seg id="831">“有点道理，”猫回答说，“不过，不管他们能不能准时开始工作，我总不能没有饭吃。”</seg>
<seg id="832">and she killed and ate him.</seg>
<seg id="832">于是，猫就吃掉了公鸡。</seg>
<seg id="833">The want of a good excuse never kept a villain from crime.</seg>
<seg id="833">带有好借口的欲望，永远不会让坏人免于恶行。</seg>
<seg id="834">THE HARE AND THE TORTOISE</seg>
<seg id="834">野兔与乌龟</seg>
<seg id="835">A Hare was one day making fun of a Tortoise for being so slow upon his feet.</seg>
<seg id="835">有一天，兔子嘲笑乌龟用脚爬得太慢了。</seg>
<seg id="836">"Wait a bit," said the Tortoise;</seg>
<seg id="836">“那又怎么了，”乌龟说，</seg>
<seg id="837">"I'll run a race with you, and I'll wager that I win."</seg>
<seg id="837">“总有一天我会和你赛跑，并且还能赢了你。”</seg>
<seg id="838">"Oh, well," replied the Hare, who was much amused at the idea, "let's try and see";</seg>
<seg id="838">“噢，好吧，”兔子回答，认为乌龟的这个想法太搞笑了，“我们比比看”。</seg>
<seg id="839">and it was soon agreed that the fox should set a course for them, and be the judge.</seg>
<seg id="839">他们很快便商定好了比赛的时间和地点，并且让狐狸来设定比赛过程，兼做裁判。</seg>
<seg id="840">When the time came both started off together, but the Hare was soon so far ahead that he thought he might as well have a rest:</seg>
<seg id="840">比赛一开始，兔子很快就跑到了前面，他觉着自己应该休息一下，</seg>
<seg id="841">so down he lay and fell fast asleep.</seg>
<seg id="841">于是便躺在路旁睡着了。</seg>
<seg id="842">Meanwhile the Tortoise kept plodding on, and in time reached the goal.</seg>
<seg id="842">此时，乌龟正不停地朝前奔跑，并且最后还实现了自己的目标。</seg>
<seg id="843">At last the Hare woke up with a start, and dashed on at his fastest, but only to find that the Tortoise had already won the race.</seg>
<seg id="843">兔子醒来后，用最快的速度猛劲向前跑，可是却发现乌龟已经取得了比赛胜利。</seg>
<seg id="844">Slow and steady wins the race.</seg>
<seg id="844">慢而稳健，这才是制胜法宝。</seg>
<seg id="845">THE SOLDIER AND HIS HORSE</seg>
<seg id="845">士兵和战马</seg>
<seg id="846">A Soldier gave his Horse a plentiful supply of oats in time of war, and tended him with the utmost care, for he wished him to be strong to endure the hardships of the field, and swift to bear his master, when need arose, out of the reach of danger.</seg>
<seg id="846">战争期间，一个士兵用充足的燕麦精心喂养他的马，希望身强体壮的马能够在需要时，驮着主人在地形艰险的战场上快速奔跑，从而免于危险。</seg>
<seg id="847">But when the war was over he employed him on all sorts of drudgery, bestowing but little attention upon him, and giving him, moreover, nothing but chaff to eat.</seg>
<seg id="847">然而，战争一结束，战马便被拉去服苦役，不仅得不到主人的关爱，而且除了糟糠之外，再也没有其它饲料了。</seg>
<seg id="848">The time came when war broke out again, and the Soldier saddled and bridled his Horse, and, having put on his heavy coat of mail, mounted him to ride off and take the field.</seg>
<seg id="848">不久，战争又爆发了，士兵备好马鞍、套上缰绳、穿上厚重的铠甲，全副武装地准备骑着马去迎敌。</seg>
<seg id="849">But the poor half-starved beast sank down under his weight, and said to his rider, "You will have to go into battle on foot this time.</seg>
<seg id="849">这时，马却毫无力气，不断摔倒，他对主人说：“这次，你可要亲自跑着赶赴战场了，</seg>
<seg id="850">Thanks to hard work and bad food, you have turned me from a Horse into an ass;</seg>
<seg id="850">都是因为繁重的劳役和廉价的饲料，让我从一匹战马变成了一头驴，</seg>
<seg id="851">and you cannot in a moment turn me back again into a Horse."</seg>
<seg id="851">你怎么还能把我当战马骑呢？”</seg>
<seg id="852">THE OXEN AND THE BUTCHERS</seg>
<seg id="852">公牛和屠夫</seg>
<seg id="853">Once upon a time the Oxen determined to be revenged upon the Butchers for the havoc they wrought in their ranks, and plotted to put them to death on a given day.</seg>
<seg id="853">有一次，公牛想报复屠夫，因为他们在屠夫那里遭受蹂躏，被分成若干等级，并且等待着某一日被屠宰。</seg>
<seg id="854">They were all gathered together discussing how best to carry out the plan, and the more violent of them were engaged in sharpening their horns for the fray, when an old Ox got up upon his feet and said, "My brothers, you have good reason, I know, to hate these Butchers, but, at any rate, they understand their trade and do what they have to do without causing unnecessary pain.</seg>
<seg id="854">他们聚集在一起商讨如何执行报复计划，其中那些比较暴躁的公牛为了这场战争已经磨好了自己的尖角，准备战斗。这时，一头年长的老公牛站起来，说：“兄弟们，我知道，大家确实有理由憎恨屠夫，但是从某种程度上讲，他们明白自己的职责，已经尽可能地减少了我们的痛苦。</seg>
<seg id="855">But if we kill them, others, who have no experience, will be set to slaughter us, and will by their bungling inflict great sufferings upon us.</seg>
<seg id="855">然而，倘若我们杀死了屠夫，就会让那些没有经验的人来宰杀我们，给我们增添更多痛苦。</seg>
<seg id="856">For you may be sure that, even though all the Butchers perish, mankind will never go without their beef."</seg>
<seg id="856">你们要知道，即便所有的屠夫都死了，但人类总是要吃牛肉的。”</seg>
<seg id="857">THE WOLF AND THE LION</seg>
<seg id="857">狼和狮子</seg>
<seg id="858">A wolf stole a lamb from the flock, and was carrying it off to devour it at his leisure when he met a Lion, who took his prey away from him and walked off with it.</seg>
<seg id="858">一次，狼从羊群中抢走一只羊，正叼着小羊往回走时，碰上了一只狮子。狮子立刻从狼口里抢走羊，大摇大摆地走了。</seg>
<seg id="859">He dared not resist, but when the Lion had gone some distance he said, "It is most unjust of you to take what's mine away from me like that."</seg>
<seg id="859">狼不敢反抗，只好乖乖等着狮子走远了，才说：“你抢走属于我的猎物，太不正当了。”</seg>
<seg id="860">The Lion laughed and called out in reply, "It was justly yours, no doubt!</seg>
<seg id="860">狮子笑着说：“那么，这东西是你正当获得的吗，</seg>
<seg id="861">The gift of a friend, perhaps, eh?"</seg>
<seg id="861">无疑是朋友送给你的，对吗？”</seg>
<seg id="862">THE SHEEP, THE WOLF, AND THE STAG</seg>
<seg id="862">鹿、狼和羊</seg>
<seg id="863">A Stag once asked a Sheep to lend him a measure of wheat, saying that his friend the Wolf would be his surety.</seg>
<seg id="863">一只鹿跑去请求羊借给他一斗麦子，并说他的朋友——狼可以作担保。</seg>
<seg id="864">The Sheep, however, was afraid that they meant to cheat her;</seg>
<seg id="864">然而，羊担心他们俩合伙欺骗自己，</seg>
<seg id="865">so she excused herself, saying, "The Wolf is in the habit of seizing what he wants and running off with it without paying, and you, too, can run much faster than I.</seg>
<seg id="865">便找了个借口，说：“狼有个坏习惯，抢完他想要的东西后便跑了，从不归还；而你则跑得比我快多了，</seg>
<seg id="866">So how shall I be able to come up with either of you when the debt falls due?"</seg>
<seg id="866">所以等到你们该还账时，我怎么能追得上你们呀？”</seg>
<seg id="867">Two blacks do not make a white.</seg>
<seg id="867">两黑不等于一白。</seg>
<seg id="868">THE LION AND THE THREE BULLS</seg>
<seg id="868">狮子和三头公牛</seg>
<seg id="869">Three Bulls were grazing in a meadow, and were watched by a Lion, who longed to capture and devour them, but who felt that he was no match for the three so long as they kept together.</seg>
<seg id="869">三头公牛住在一个草场里，窥探已久的一只狮子想要吃掉他们，可是只要公牛团结一致，狮子就无法得逞。</seg>
<seg id="870">So he began by false whispers and malicious hints to foment jealousies and distrust among them.</seg>
<seg id="870">于是，狮子便在公牛之中煽风点火，不怀好意地挑拨离间，令他们产生冲突和愤恨。</seg>
<seg id="871">This stratagem succeeded so well that ere long the Bulls grew cold and unfriendly, and finally avoided each other and fed each one by himself apart.</seg>
<seg id="871">狮子的计谋终于得逞了，三头公牛不如以前那么友好了，相互之间很冷淡，随后互不相见，各自到草场里吃草。</seg>
<seg id="872">No sooner did the Lion see this than he fell upon them one by one and killed them in turn.</seg>
<seg id="872">这时，狮子轻而易举地依次吃掉了三头公牛。</seg>
<seg id="873">The quarrels of friends are the opportunities of foes.</seg>
<seg id="873">朋友间的争吵，就是在给敌人制造机会。</seg>
<seg id="874">THE HORSE AND HIS RIDER</seg>
<seg id="874">马和骑手</seg>
<seg id="875">A Young Man, who fancied himself something of a horseman, mounted a Horse which had not been properly broken in, and was exceedingly difficult to control.</seg>
<seg id="875">一个年轻人自诩为骑师，爬上了一匹并没有受过良好训练的马，而且这匹马极其难以驾驭。</seg>
<seg id="876">No sooner did the Horse feel his weight in the saddle than he bolted, and nothing would stop him.</seg>
<seg id="876">马一感受到背上的重量，就狂奔起来，什么也挡不住他。</seg>
<seg id="877">A friend of the Rider's met him in the road in his headlong career, and called out, "Where are you off to in such a hurry?"</seg>
<seg id="877">骑手的一个朋友在路上遇见了他，大声叫道：“你这是急着去哪里呀？”</seg>
<seg id="878">To which he, pointing to the Horse, replied, "I've no idea: ask him."</seg>
<seg id="878">骑手指着马回答说：“我也不知道，你问他吧。”</seg>
<seg id="879">THE GOAT AND THE VINE</seg>
<seg id="879">母山羊与葡萄藤</seg>
<seg id="880">A Goat was straying in a vineyard, and began to browse on the tender shoots of a Vine which bore several fine bunches of grapes.</seg>
<seg id="880">一只母山羊在葡萄园里闲逛，她看到一株刚刚长出几串葡萄的葡萄藤，就过去吃起了它的嫩叶。</seg>
<seg id="881">"What have I done to you," said the Vine, "that you should harm me thus?</seg>
<seg id="881">葡萄藤对母山羊说：“我做过什么对不起你的事吗？</seg>
<seg id="882">Isn't there grass enough for you to feed on?</seg>
<seg id="882">难道地上没有青草吃了？</seg>
<seg id="883">All the same, even if you eat up every leaf I have, and leave me quite bare, I shall produce wine enough to pour over you when you are led to the altar to be sacrificed."</seg>
<seg id="883">即便你吃光了我所有的叶子，让我变成光秃秃的藤，当你被放在祭坛上作为祭祀品时，浇灌到你身上的葡萄酒也全是我产出来的。”</seg>
<seg id="884">THE TWO POTS</seg>
<seg id="884">两口锅</seg>
<seg id="885">Two Pots, one of earthenware and the other of brass, were carried away down a river in flood.</seg>
<seg id="885">两口锅被洪水冲进了河里，一口是瓦锅，另一口是铜锅。</seg>
<seg id="886">The Brazen Pot urged his companion to keep close by his side, and he would protect him.</seg>
<seg id="886">铜锅催促同伴靠近他一些，这样才能保护他。</seg>
<seg id="887">The other thanked him, but begged him not to come near him on any account:</seg>
<seg id="887">可是，瓦锅却多谢铜锅的好意，并求他不要靠近自己。</seg>
<seg id="888">"For that," he said, "is just what I am most afraid of.</seg>
<seg id="888">瓦锅说：“这正是我最担心的事情。</seg>
<seg id="889">One touch from you and I should be broken in pieces."</seg>
<seg id="889">只要你一碰我，我必定会粉身碎骨。”</seg>
<seg id="890">Equals make the best friends.</seg>
<seg id="890">水平相当的两者，才会成为好朋友。</seg>
<seg id="891">THE OLD HOUND</seg>
<seg id="891">老猎狗</seg>
<seg id="892">A Hound who had served his master well for years, and had run down many a quarry in his time, began to lose his strength and speed owing to age.</seg>
<seg id="892">一条老猎狗已经尽心尽力为主人服务了很多年，现在已经衰老了，也失去了年轻力壮时的力气和速度。</seg>
<seg id="893">One day, when out hunting, his master started a powerful wild boar and set the Hound at him.</seg>
<seg id="893">有一天，当他们出去狩猎时，主人盯上了一头野猪，让老猎狗扑上去咬他。</seg>
<seg id="894">The latter seized the beast by the ear, but his teeth were gone and he could not retain his hold; so the boar escaped.</seg>
<seg id="894">老猎狗咬住了野猪的耳朵，可是由于他的牙齿已经脱落，根本无法牢牢地咬住野猪，于是，野猪侥幸逃跑了。</seg>
<seg id="895">His master began to scold him severely, but the Hound interrupted him with these words: "My will is as strong as ever, master, but my body is old and feeble.</seg>
<seg id="895">主人严厉地痛骂了他一顿，老猎狗打断主人的斥骂，说：“主人呀，我倒是也想像以前一样强壮，但我的身体已经衰老无力了。</seg>
<seg id="896">You ought to honour me for what I have been instead of abusing me for what I am."</seg>
<seg id="896">想一想从前我为你所付出的一切，你理应称赞我，而不应该责备我。”</seg>
<seg id="897">THE CLOWN AND THE COUNTRYMAN</seg>
<seg id="897">小丑和乡下人</seg>
<seg id="898">A Nobleman announced his intention of giving a public entertainment in the theatre, and offered splendid prizes to all who had any novelty to exhibit at the performance.</seg>
<seg id="898">一个富翁对外宣称要在剧场搞一次公开表演，并且还说，要重重奖励那些表演新戏法的人。</seg>
<seg id="899">The announcement attracted a crowd of conjurers, jugglers, and acrobats, and among the rest a Clown, very popular with the crowd, who let it be known that he was going to give an entirely new turn.</seg>
<seg id="899">这个公告吸引了一群魔术师、杂耍艺人和杂技演员，其中，一个广受欢迎的小丑说他要在台上表演一个全新的把戏。</seg>
<seg id="900">When the day of the performance came, the theatre was filled from top to bottom some time before the entertainment began.</seg>
<seg id="900">到了公开表演的那一天，还没开场，整个剧场就已被围得水泄不通。</seg>
<seg id="901">Several performers exhibited their tricks, and then the popular favourite came on empty-handed and alone.</seg>
<seg id="901">几个演员表演了他们的特技之后，小丑接着就两手空空地独自一人出现在舞台上。</seg>
<seg id="902">At once there was a hush of expectation:</seg>
<seg id="902">观众因为太期待看他的表演，全场立刻鸦雀无声。</seg>
<seg id="903">and he, letting his head fall upon his breast, imitated the squeak of a pig to such perfection that the audience insisted on his producing the animal, which, they said, he must have somewhere concealed about his person.</seg>
<seg id="903">而小丑突然把头俯到胸前，学小猪叫，他叫的声音逼真得使人惊叹，以至于大家都说，他一定是把猪藏在什么地方了。</seg>
<seg id="904">He, however, convinced them that there was no pig there, and then the applause was deafening.</seg>
<seg id="904">然而，他却说服观众，并没有藏起猪来，接着，全场掌声雷鸣。</seg>
<seg id="905">Among the spectators was a Countryman, who disparaged the Clown's performance and announced that he would give a much superior exhibition of the same trick on the following day.</seg>
<seg id="905">场下有一位观众是个乡下人，看完小丑的表演后，他就宣称自己明天也要表演同样的把戏，一定会比小丑的更好。</seg>
<seg id="906">Again the theatre was filled to overflowing, and again the Clown gave his imitation amidst the cheers of the crowd.</seg>
<seg id="906">第二天，剧场里又挤满了人，小丑照样以他的模仿秀赢得了观众的欢呼和喜爱。</seg>
<seg id="907">The Countryman, meanwhile, before going on the stage, had secreted a young porker under his smock;</seg>
<seg id="907">同时站在舞台上的乡下人，早已在上台前，将一只小猪藏到了衣服里，</seg>
<seg id="908">and when the spectators derisively bade him do better if he could, he gave it a pinch in the ear and made it squeal loudly.</seg>
<seg id="908">就在观众嘲弄他是否能表演得更精彩时，他揪了一下小猪的耳朵，让他大声叫起来。</seg>
<seg id="909">But they all with one voice shouted out that the Clown's imitation was much more true to life.</seg>
<seg id="909">然而，观众们都大喊小丑的叫声更逼真。</seg>
<seg id="910">Thereupon he produced the pig from under his smock and said sarcastically, "There, that shows what sort of judges you are!"</seg>
<seg id="910">于是，乡下人便从衣服里拿出小猪来，讽刺地说：“请看这里，你们到底是什么样的裁判呀！”</seg>
<seg id="911">THE LARK AND THE FARMER</seg>
<seg id="911">百灵鸟和农夫</seg>
<seg id="912">A Lark nested in a field of corn, and was rearing her brood under cover of the ripening grain.</seg>
<seg id="912">一只百灵鸟在绿油油的麦田里做了巢，在成熟的麦穗掩映下，正哺育着一窝小百灵鸟。</seg>
<seg id="913">One day, before the young were fully fledged, the Farmer came to look at the crop, and, finding it yellowing fast, he said, "I must send round word to my neighbours to come and help me reap this field."</seg>
<seg id="913">虽然小百灵鸟们的羽翼还未完全丰满，但有一天，农夫来田里看庄稼，发现麦子已经变黄了，便说：“我得去告诉邻居们，帮我到田里来收割庄稼。”</seg>
<seg id="914">One of the young Larks overheard him, and was very much frightened, and asked her mother whether they hadn't better move house at once.</seg>
<seg id="914">一只小百灵鸟听到了这番话，心里非常害怕，便赶忙问妈妈是否应该立刻搬家。</seg>
<seg id="915">"There's no hurry," replied she;</seg>
<seg id="915">“不用着急，”百灵鸟说，</seg>
<seg id="916">"a man who looks to his friends for help will take his time about a thing."</seg>
<seg id="916">“孩子，请朋友来帮忙是需要时间的。”</seg>
<seg id="917">In a few days the Farmer came by again, and saw that the grain was overripe and falling out of the ears upon the ground.</seg>
<seg id="917">过了几天，农夫又到田里来了，看到麦子早已熟透，几乎快掉下来了，</seg>
<seg id="918">"I must put it off no longer," he said;</seg>
<seg id="918">便心急火燎地说：“不能再拖了，</seg>
<seg id="919">"This very day I'll hire the men and set them to work at once."</seg>
<seg id="919">我今天就得雇人，立刻开始收割。”</seg>
<seg id="920">The Lark heard him and said to her young, "Come, my children, we must be off:</seg>
<seg id="920">百灵鸟听到这话后，便对小鸟们说：“我的孩子们，现在我们必须要搬家了，</seg>
<seg id="921">he talks no more of his friends now, but is going to take things in hand himself."</seg>
<seg id="921">因为他没有再提到请朋友帮忙，而是要自己亲自动手了。”</seg>
<seg id="922">Self-help is the best help.</seg>
<seg id="922">自助是最好的帮助。</seg>
<seg id="923">THE LION AND THE ASS</seg>
<seg id="923">狮子和驴</seg>
<seg id="924">A Lion and an Ass set up as partners and went a-hunting together.</seg>
<seg id="924">一只狮子和一头驴合作外出打猎。</seg>
<seg id="925">In course of time they came to a cave in which there were a number of wild goats.</seg>
<seg id="925">走了一会儿，他们来到几只野山羊居住的洞口。</seg>
<seg id="926">The Lion took up his stand at the mouth of the cave, and waited for them to come out;</seg>
<seg id="926">狮子守在洞口等着野山羊出来，</seg>
<seg id="927">while the Ass went inside and brayed for all he was worth in order to frighten them out into the open.</seg>
<seg id="927">驴则跑进洞里，为了把山羊赶出去而乱喊乱跳，吓唬他们。</seg>
<seg id="928">The Lion struck them down one by one as they appeared;</seg>
<seg id="928">守候在洞口的狮子将跑出洞来的野山羊依次抓获了，</seg>
<seg id="929">and when the cave was empty the Ass came out and said, "Well, I scared them pretty well, didn't I?"</seg>
<seg id="929">等到洞里空无一只羊之后，驴跑出洞来，说：“怎么样，我把他们都吓出来了，干得不错吧？”</seg>
<seg id="930">"I should think you did," said the Lion: "why, if I hadn't known you were an Ass, I should have turned and run myself."</seg>
<seg id="930">“我认为你干得很好，”狮子说，“如果我不知道你是一头驴，也许就会转身走了。”</seg>
<seg id="931">THE PROPHET</seg>
<seg id="931">算命人</seg>
<seg id="932">A Prophet sat in the market-place and told the fortunes of all who cared to engage his services.</seg>
<seg id="932">一个专门给人算命的人，坐在市场里靠给人算卦来谋生。</seg>
<seg id="933">Suddenly there came running up one who told him that his house had been broken into by thieves, and that they had made off with everything they could lay hands on.</seg>
<seg id="933">忽然，有一个人跑来告诉他，他家被强盗撬门而入，家里所有的东西几乎都被偷走了。</seg>
<seg id="934">He was up in a moment, and rushed off, tearing his hair and calling down curses on the miscreants.</seg>
<seg id="934">算命的人大吃一惊，立刻气得跳了起来，唉声叹气地赶回家中。</seg>
<seg id="935">The bystanders were much amused, and one of them said, "Our friend professes to know what is going to happen to others, but it seems he's not clever enough to perceive what's in store for himself."</seg>
<seg id="935">旁观者都被逗笑了，其中一个人说道：“这位朋友声称自己能预知将来，可是看上去他并不聪明，怎么连自己的事都没预料到呢？”</seg>
<seg id="936">THE HOUND AND THE HARE</seg>
<seg id="936">猎狗和野兔</seg>
<seg id="937">A young Hound started a Hare, and, when he caught her up, would at one moment snap at her with his teeth as though he were about to kill her, while at another he would let go his hold and frisk about her, as if he were playing with another dog.</seg>
<seg id="937">一只小猎狗去抓一只野兔，就在抓兔子的过程中，猎狗一会儿用牙咬他，仿佛要咬死他；一会儿又让他挣脱出去，在周围乱蹦乱跳，仿佛在和另一只狗玩耍。</seg>
<seg id="938">At last the Hare said, "I wish you would show yourself in your true colours!</seg>
<seg id="938">最后，野兔对猎狗说：“我希望你能表现出你的真实面目来！</seg>
<seg id="939">If you are my friend, why do you bite me?</seg>
<seg id="939">如果你是我的朋友，为什么要咬我？</seg>
<seg id="940">If you are my enemy, why do you play with me?"</seg>
<seg id="940">如果你是我的敌人，为什么还跟我玩？”</seg>
<seg id="941">He is no friend who plays double.</seg>
<seg id="941">两面派可不是你的朋友。</seg>
<seg id="942">THE LION, THE MOUSE, AND THE FOX</seg>
<seg id="942">狮子、老鼠和狐狸</seg>
<seg id="943">A Lion was lying asleep at the mouth of his den when a Mouse ran over his back and tickled him so that he woke up with a start and began looking about everywhere to see what it was that had disturbed him.</seg>
<seg id="943">一只狮子躺在自己的洞口睡着了，这时，一只老鼠跑到他的背后搔他痒，好让他赶快从梦中醒来，寻找究竟是谁在骚扰他。</seg>
<seg id="944">A Fox, who was looking on, thought he would have a joke at the expense of the Lion; so he said, "Well, this is the first time I've seen a Lion afraid of a Mouse."</seg>
<seg id="944">在旁观察的狐狸见后，心想可以和狮子开个玩笑，便开口说道：“我可是第一次看见狮子惧怕老鼠。”</seg>
<seg id="945">"Afraid of a Mouse?" said the Lion testily: "not I!</seg>
<seg id="945">“害怕一只小老鼠？”狮子说，“我才不怕老鼠呢！</seg>
<seg id="946">It's his bad manners I can't stand."</seg>
<seg id="946">只是无法忍受他的无礼。”</seg>
<seg id="947">THE TRUMPETER TAKEN PRISONER</seg>
<seg id="947">被捕的号兵</seg>
<seg id="948">A Trumpeter marched into battle in the van of the army and put courage into his comrades by his warlike tunes.</seg>
<seg id="948">有一个号兵，在战役中总是冲在大部队的前面，利用吹响号角为同志们加油。</seg>
<seg id="949">Being captured by the enemy, he begged for his life, and said, "Do not put me to death;</seg>
<seg id="949">在被敌人抓获后，他说：“不要杀死我，</seg>
<seg id="950">I have killed no one:</seg>
<seg id="950">我从没杀过任何人，</seg>
<seg id="951">indeed, I have no weapons, but carry with me only my trumpet here."</seg>
<seg id="951">实际上，我没有任何武器，只有这把铜号。”</seg>
<seg id="952">But his captors replied, "That is only the more reason why we should take your life;</seg>
<seg id="952">然而，敌人却对他说道：“那你就更应当被处死了，</seg>
<seg id="953">for, though you do not fight yourself, you stir up others to do so."</seg>
<seg id="953">因为你自己虽然没去打仗，可你却召集其他人来攻打我们。”</seg>
<seg id="954">THE WOLF AND THE CRANE</seg>
<seg id="954">狼与鹤</seg>
<seg id="955">A Wolf once got a bone stuck in his throat.</seg>
<seg id="955">有一次，一只狼的喉咙被骨头哽住了，</seg>
<seg id="956">So he went to a Crane and begged her to put her long bill down his throat and pull it out.</seg>
<seg id="956">便去找鹤，求她将长喙伸进自己的喉咙，取出那块骨头。</seg>
<seg id="957">"I'll make it worth your while," he added.</seg>
<seg id="957">随后，他又补充了一句：“我会好好犒劳你的。”</seg>
<seg id="958">The Crane did as she was asked, and got the bone out quite easily.</seg>
<seg id="958">鹤按照狼的吩咐做了，很轻松地取出了那块骨头。</seg>
<seg id="959">The Wolf thanked her warmly, and was just turning away, when she cried, "What about that fee of mine?"</seg>
<seg id="959">狼热情地感谢了她，然后转身就走了。这时，鹤大喊道：“你说好的报酬呢？”</seg>
<seg id="960">"Well, what about it?" snapped the Wolf, baring his teeth as he spoke;</seg>
<seg id="960">“你说什么？”狼龇牙咧嘴地说，</seg>
<seg id="961">"you can go about boasting that you once put your head into a Wolf's mouth and didn't get it bitten off.</seg>
<seg id="961">“你可以大肆宣传自己的头曾经伸到一只狼的嘴巴里，并且安全地拔出来了，</seg>
<seg id="962">What more do you want?"</seg>
<seg id="962">这难道不就是给你的奖赏吗？”</seg>
<seg id="963">THE EAGLE, THE CAT, AND THE WILD SOW</seg>
<seg id="963">鹰、猫和野猪</seg>
<seg id="964">An Eagle built her nest at the top of a high tree;</seg>
<seg id="964">一只老鹰在一棵大橡树的高枝上安了家；</seg>
<seg id="965">a Cat with her family occupied a hollow in the trunk half-way down;</seg>
<seg id="965">一只猫和她的孩子们在这棵树的树干上霸占了一个树洞；</seg>
<seg id="966">and a Wild Sow and her young took up their quarters at the foot.</seg>
<seg id="966">一只野猪则带着小猪崽住进了树根处的洞里。</seg>
<seg id="967">They might have got on very well as neighbours had it not been for the evil cunning of the Cat.</seg>
<seg id="967">若不是猫诡计多端，他们可能会成为很好的邻居。</seg>
<seg id="968">Climbing up to the Eagle's nest she said to the Eagle, "You and I are in the greatest possible danger.</seg>
<seg id="968">猫先爬到老鹰的巢边，说：“你和我都很危险呀！</seg>
<seg id="969">That dreadful creature, the Sow, who is always to be seen grubbing away at the foot of the tree, means to uproot it, that she may devour your family and mine at her ease."</seg>
<seg id="969">树下那头野猪，天天在树根处挖土，怕是想把这棵树连根拔掉，好轻而易举地吃掉我们的孩子。”</seg>
<seg id="970">Having thus driven the Eagle almost out of her senses with terror, the Cat climbed down the tree, and said to the Sow, "I must warn you against that dreadful bird, the Eagle.</seg>
<seg id="970">猫用这番话吓唬了老鹰之后，又爬下来对野猪说：“我必须要警告你，小心那只可怕的老鹰。</seg>
<seg id="971">She is only waiting her chance to fly down and carry off one of your little pigs when you take them out, to feed her brood with."</seg>
<seg id="971">她可是一直在伺机飞下来抓走你的孩子们，去喂小鹰。”</seg>
<seg id="972">She succeeded in frightening the Sow as much as the Eagle.</seg>
<seg id="972">猫也像吓唬老鹰那样，狠狠地吓唬了野猪一番。</seg>
<seg id="973">Then she returned to her hole in the trunk, from which, feigning to be afraid, she never came forth by day.</seg>
<seg id="973">然后，她假装自己也很害怕，躲进了自己的树洞，当日再也没出来。</seg>
<seg id="974">Only by night did she creep out unseen to procure food for her kittens.</seg>
<seg id="974">到了晚上，她则偷偷地跑出去为孩子们寻找食物。</seg>
<seg id="975">The Eagle, meanwhile was afraid to stir from her nest, and the Sow dared not leave her home among the roots:</seg>
<seg id="975">老鹰吓得不敢离开自己的巢，野猪也吓得不敢走出洞来。</seg>
<seg id="976">so that in time both they and their families perished of hunger, and their dead bodies supplied the Cat with ample food for her growing family.</seg>
<seg id="976">就这样，老鹰和野猪以及他们的孩子都饿死了，而猫则用老鹰、野猪及其幼崽的尸体养大了自己的孩子。</seg>
<seg id="977">THE WOLF AND THE SHEEP</seg>
<seg id="977">狼和绵羊</seg>
<seg id="978">A Wolf was worried and badly bitten by dogs, and lay a long time for dead.</seg>
<seg id="978">一只狼被狗咬了，伤势很严重，他非常担心，昏倒在地上很长时间。</seg>
<seg id="979">By and by he began to revive, and, feeling very hungry, called out to a passing Sheep and said, "Would you kindly bring me some water from the stream close by?</seg>
<seg id="979">不久，他苏醒过来，感觉饿了，正好看见一只羊从此经过，便说：“你能发发善心，帮我到旁边的小河里取一点水来吗？</seg>
<seg id="980">I can manage about meat, if only I could get something to drink."</seg>
<seg id="980">如果你能给我一点水解渴，我就能去找点肉吃了。”</seg>
<seg id="981">But this Sheep was no fool.</seg>
<seg id="981">可是，这只羊并不傻。</seg>
<seg id="982">"I can quite understand", said he, "that if I brought you the water, you would have no difficulty about the meat.</seg>
<seg id="982">“我完全明白，”他回答说，“要是我给你送来水，那你就能毫不费力地找到肉吃了。”</seg>
<seg id="983">Good-morning."</seg>
<seg id="983">[无]</seg>
<seg id="984">THE TUNNY-FISH AND THE DOLPHIN</seg>
<seg id="984">金枪鱼和海豚</seg>
<seg id="985">A Tunny-fish was chased by a Dolphin and splashed through the water at a great rate, but the Dolphin gradually gained upon him, and was just about to seize him when the force of his flight carried the Tunny on to a sandbank.</seg>
<seg id="985">一条金枪鱼在水中急速穿行，而追赶他的海豚一直在后面穷追不舍，眼看着就要被海豚捉住了，金枪鱼猛然一跳，不料用劲太猛，让自己在岸边搁浅了。</seg>
<seg id="986">In the heat of the chase the Dolphin followed him, and there they both lay out of the water, gasping for dear life.</seg>
<seg id="986">紧追不舍的海豚因为惯性也跟着金枪鱼一跳，同样搁浅在岸边。</seg>
<seg id="987">When the Tunny saw that his enemy was doomed like himself, he said, "I don't mind having to die now:</seg>
<seg id="987">这时，金枪鱼看到敌人也像自己一样奄奄一息，便说：“现在，死对我来说已经无所谓了，</seg>
<seg id="988">for I see that he who is the cause of my death is about to share the same fate."</seg>
<seg id="988">因为我已亲眼看到，那个引我致死的家伙也与我一起同归于尽了。”</seg>
<seg id="989">THE THREE TRADESMEN</seg>
<seg id="989">三个工匠</seg>
<seg id="990">The citizens of a certain city were debating about the best material to use in the fortifications which were about to be erected for the greater security of the town.</seg>
<seg id="990">某个城镇中的居民在讨论什么样的好材料才能用于对抗敌人的进攻，从而可以确保全城人的安全。</seg>
<seg id="991">A Carpenter got up and advised the use of wood, which he said was readily procurable and easily worked.</seg>
<seg id="991">一个木匠挺身而出，主张用木头作为防御材料，既随手可得又操作简单；</seg>
<seg id="992">A Stone-mason objected to wood on the ground that it was so inflammable, and recommended stones instead.</seg>
<seg id="992">一个石匠毅然反对，他说木头容易被点燃，太不安全了，而他则提议用石头。</seg>
<seg id="993">Then a Tanner got on his legs and said, "In my opinion there's nothing like leather."</seg>
<seg id="993">接着，一个皮匠站起来，说：“依我看来，没有什么能比皮子更适合做防御工事的材料了。”</seg>
