<seg id="994">Every man for himself.</seg>
<seg id="994">人们都习惯于从自身角度考虑问题，总认为自己所熟悉的东西是最好的。</seg>
<seg id="995">THE MOUSE AND THE BULL</seg>
<seg id="995">老鼠和公牛</seg>
<seg id="996">A Bull gave chase to a Mouse which had bitten him in the nose:</seg>
<seg id="996">一头公牛被老鼠咬了鼻子，到处追赶老鼠。</seg>
<seg id="997">but the Mouse was too quick for him and slipped into a hole in a wall.</seg>
<seg id="997">但是，老鼠可比公牛跑得快多了，一下就溜进了墙边的洞里。</seg>
<seg id="998">The Bull charged furiously into the wall again and again until he was tired out, and sank down on the ground exhausted with his efforts.</seg>
<seg id="998">气得公牛一次又一次地撞墙，最后累得筋疲力尽，一下就瘫在了地上。</seg>
<seg id="999">When all was quiet, the Mouse darted out and bit him again.</seg>
<seg id="999">这时，小老鼠一听没了动静，又跑出来再咬公牛。</seg>
<seg id="1000">Beside himself with rage he started to his feet, but by that time the Mouse was back in his hole again, and he could do nothing but bellow and fume in helpless anger.</seg>
<seg id="1000">公牛狂怒，又开始用脚踢墙，而此时小老鼠早已跑回到洞里去了。除了大吼和无用的生闷气之外，公牛一筹莫展。</seg>
<seg id="1001">Presently he heard a shrill little voice say from inside the wall, "You big fellows don't always have it your own way, you see: sometimes we little ones come off best."</seg>
<seg id="1001">不久，他听到一个微弱的声音从墙壁里传出来：“你这个大家伙也不能总逞强吧，你看，有时我们这样的小不点也会占上风的。”</seg>
<seg id="1002">The battle is not always to the strong.</seg>
<seg id="1002">强者并非总是战争的胜方。</seg>
<seg id="1003">THE HARE AND THE HOUND</seg>
<seg id="1003">野兔和猎狗</seg>
<seg id="1004">A Hound started a Hare from her form, and pursued her for some distance;</seg>
<seg id="1004">一条猎狗在追赶兔子，从兔窝边一直追出去好远。</seg>
<seg id="1005">but as she gradually gained upon him, he gave up the chase.</seg>
<seg id="1005">眼看着要追上兔子时，猎狗却放弃了。</seg>
<seg id="1006">A rustic who had seen the race met the Hound as he was returning, and taunted him with his defeat.</seg>
<seg id="1006">一个农民关注了整个过程，在路上遇见往回走的猎狗时，讥笑它是个失败者。</seg>
<seg id="1007">"The little one was too much for you," said he.</seg>
<seg id="1007">“那个小家伙可比你强多了，”农民说。</seg>
<seg id="1008">"Ah, well," said the Hound, "don't forget it's one thing to be running for your dinner, but quite another to be running for your life."</seg>
<seg id="1008">“噢，是吗？”猎狗说，“不要忘了，一个是仅为一顿饭在跑，而另一个则是为了一条命在跑。”</seg>
<seg id="1009">THE TOWN MOUSE AND THE COUNTRY MOUSE</seg>
<seg id="1009">城市鼠和乡下鼠</seg>
<seg id="1010">A Town Mouse and a Country Mouse were acquaintances, and the Country Mouse one day invited his friend to come and see him at his home in the fields.</seg>
<seg id="1010">一只住在城里的老鼠和一只住在乡下的老鼠是好朋友。有一天，乡下鼠邀请城市老鼠到他的家里来玩，看看他那田地里的家。</seg>
<seg id="1011">The Town Mouse came, and they sat down to a dinner of barleycorns and roots, the latter of which had a distinctly earthy flavour.</seg>
<seg id="1011">城里鼠如约而至，他们坐下来分享了以大麦粒和树根为主的晚餐，那些树根还带着一种独特的泥土气息。</seg>
<seg id="1012">The fare was not much to the taste of the guest, and presently he broke out with "My poor dear friend, you live here no better than the ants.</seg>
<seg id="1012">这些食物显然不太对客人的胃口，最后，客人忍不住脱口而出：“可怜的朋友，你在这里生活，比蚂蚁好不到哪里去。</seg>
<seg id="1013">Now, you should just see how I fare!</seg>
<seg id="1013">你真应该去看看我都吃些什么！</seg>
<seg id="1014">My larder is a regular horn of plenty.</seg>
<seg id="1014">我的储藏室里可都是好东西，</seg>
<seg id="1015">You must come and stay with me, and I promise you you shall live on the fat of the land."</seg>
<seg id="1015">你一定得来和我一起生活，我保证你一定会过上锦衣玉食的日子！”</seg>
<seg id="1016">So when he returned to town he took the Country Mouse with him, and showed him into a larder containing flour and oatmeal and figs and honey and dates.</seg>
<seg id="1016">于是，城里鼠带着乡下鼠回到了城里，还让他欣赏了装满面粉、燕麦、无花果、蜂蜜和大枣的储藏室。</seg>
<seg id="1017">The Country Mouse had never seen anything like it, and sat down to enjoy the luxuries his friend provided:</seg>
<seg id="1017">乡下鼠从未见过这么多的美食，坐下来好好欣赏着朋友提供的这些佳肴，</seg>
<seg id="1018">but before they had well begun, the door of the larder opened and some one came in.</seg>
<seg id="1018">就在他们正要开始吃的时候，储藏室的门被打开了，有人走了进来。</seg>
<seg id="1019">The two Mice scampered off and hid themselves in a narrow and exceedingly uncomfortable hole.</seg>
<seg id="1019">两只老鼠立刻惊慌而逃，赶紧钻进了一个窄小的鼠洞。</seg>
<seg id="1020">Presently, when all was quiet, they ventured out again;</seg>
<seg id="1020">不久，储藏室里又恢复了平静，他们接着跑出来，</seg>
<seg id="1021">but some one else came in, and off they scuttled again.</seg>
<seg id="1021">不过，接着又有人进屋来拿东西。</seg>
<seg id="1022">This was too much for the visitor.</seg>
<seg id="1022">乡下来的客人可不习惯这种躲躲藏藏的生活方式。</seg>
<seg id="1023">"Good-bye," said he, "I'm off.</seg>
<seg id="1023">“再见了，朋友！”他说，“我要走了。</seg>
<seg id="1024">You live in the lap of luxury, I can see, but you are surrounded by dangers;</seg>
<seg id="1024">你的确是过着锦衣玉食的日子，我已经看到了，但是你却时刻处在危险之中，</seg>
<seg id="1025">whereas at home I can enjoy my simple dinner of roots and corn in peace."</seg>
<seg id="1025">而我还是回家去平平安安地享受那简单的树根和大麦吧。”</seg>
<seg id="1026">THE LION AND THE BULL</seg>
<seg id="1026">狮子和公牛</seg>
<seg id="1027">A Lion saw a fine fat Bull pasturing among a herd of cattle and cast about for some means of getting him into his clutches;</seg>
<seg id="1027">狮子看见牛群中有一头体态肥硕的公牛在吃草，便思忖着用什么方法能让公牛受骗上当。</seg>
<seg id="1028">so he sent him word that he was sacrificing a sheep, and asked if he would do him the honour of dining with him.</seg>
<seg id="1028">于是，狮子对公牛说自己杀了一只羊，并问他是否愿意赏光，和自己共同分享这只羊。</seg>
<seg id="1029">The Bull accepted the invitation, but, on arriving at the Lion's den, he saw a great array of saucepans and spits, but no sign of a sheep; so he turned on his heel and walked quietly away.</seg>
<seg id="1029">公牛接受了邀请，但是当公牛向着狮子的巢穴走时，只看到了炖锅和水，根本没看见羊的痕迹。于是，他一声不吭地转身走了。</seg>
<seg id="1030">The Lion called after him in an injured tone to ask the reason, and the Bull turned round and said, "I have reason enough.</seg>
<seg id="1030">狮子在他身后大喊，带着受伤的语气询问原因，而公牛则转身说：“我的理由很充分，</seg>
<seg id="1031">When I saw all your preparations it struck me at once that the victim was to be a Bull and not a sheep."</seg>
<seg id="1031">一看到你准备的那些东西，我就惊呆了，那个受害者可能不是一只羊，而是一头公牛。”</seg>
<seg id="1032">The net is spread in vain in sight of the bird.</seg>
<seg id="1032">网虽然张开，但对心知肚明的鸟来说，却是徒劳。</seg>
<seg id="1033">THE WOLF, THE FOX, AND THE APE</seg>
<seg id="1033">狼、狐狸和猿猴</seg>
<seg id="1034">A Wolf charged a Fox with theft, which he denied, and the case was brought before an Ape to be tried.</seg>
<seg id="1034">一只狼指责狐狸偷了他的东西，而狐狸却根本不承认，于是，他们请猿猴来裁决。</seg>
<seg id="1035">When he had heard the evidence on both sides, the Ape gave judgment as follows: "I do not think," he said, "that you, O Wolf, ever lost what you claim;</seg>
<seg id="1035">他们双方各自陈述了理由后，猿猴给出了如下裁决：“狼，我认为你没有丢失什么东西；</seg>
<seg id="1036">but all the same I believe that you, Fox, are guilty of the theft, in spite of all your denials."</seg>
<seg id="1036">但同时我也相信，狐狸即使偷过东西，也死不承认。”</seg>
<seg id="1037">The dishonest get no credit, even if they act honestly.</seg>
<seg id="1037">不诚实的人，即使行为端正，也没有信用。</seg>
<seg id="1038">THE EAGLE AND THE COCKS</seg>
<seg id="1038">老鹰和公鸡</seg>
<seg id="1039">There were two Cocks in the same farmyard, and they fought to decide who should be master.</seg>
<seg id="1039">两只公鸡生活在同一个场院里，为争当主人而打了起来。</seg>
<seg id="1040">When the fight was over, the beaten one went and hid himself in a dark corner;</seg>
<seg id="1040">战争结束后，落败的一方躲进了一个黑暗的角落；</seg>
<seg id="1041">while the victor flew up on to the roof of the stables and crowed lustily.</seg>
<seg id="1041">而胜者则飞到棚顶上兴奋地大喊大叫。</seg>
<seg id="1042">But an Eagle espied him from high up in the sky, and swooped down and carried him off.</seg>
<seg id="1042">然而，一只鹰突然从天而降，冲下来抓走了他。</seg>
<seg id="1043">Forthwith the other Cock came out of his corner and ruled the roost without a rival.</seg>
<seg id="1043">这时，那只被打败的公鸡立刻从角落里跑出来，独自占领了整个鸡窝。</seg>
<seg id="1044">Pride comes before a fall.</seg>
<seg id="1044">骄兵必败。</seg>
<seg id="1045">THE ESCAPED JACKDAW</seg>
<seg id="1045">逃跑的寒鸦</seg>
<seg id="1046">A Man caught a Jackdaw and tied a piece of string to one of its legs, and then gave it to his children for a pet.</seg>
<seg id="1046">有人捕捉到一只寒鸦，并用麻绳绑住了他的一只脚，然后给孩子当宠物玩。</seg>
<seg id="1047">But the Jackdaw didn't at all like having to live with people;</seg>
<seg id="1047">可是，寒鸦很不愿意与人一起生活。</seg>
<seg id="1048">so, after a while, when he seemed to have become fairly tame and they didn't watch him so closely, he slipped away and flew back to his old haunts.</seg>
<seg id="1048">过了一段时间后，当他看上去似乎已经被驯服了时，人们便不再密切监视他了。于是，寒鸦趁机逃出去，飞回了自己的老巢。</seg>
<seg id="1049">Unfortunately, the string was still on his leg, and before long it got entangled in the branches of a tree and the Jackdaw couldn't get free, try as he would.</seg>
<seg id="1049">不幸的是，他的腿上依然还绑着那根绳子，很快便被树枝缠住再也飞不起来了。</seg>
<seg id="1050">He saw it was all up with him, and cried in despair, "Alas, in gaining my freedom I have lost my life."</seg>
<seg id="1050">看到自己性命无保，寒鸦绝望地哭喊道：“唉，为了获得自由，我竟丢失了性命。”</seg>
<seg id="1051">THE FARMER AND THE FOX</seg>
<seg id="1051">农夫和狐狸</seg>
<seg id="1052">A Farmer was greatly annoyed by a Fox, which came prowling about his yard at night and carried off his fowls.</seg>
<seg id="1052">有个农夫受到了狐狸无尽的骚扰，因为狐狸经常在夜里到他的院子里偷鸡。</seg>
<seg id="1053">So he set a trap for him and caught him;</seg>
<seg id="1053">于是，他设置了一个捕获狐狸的圈套。</seg>
<seg id="1054">and in order to be revenged upon him, he tied a bunch of tow to his tail and set fire to it and let him go.</seg>
<seg id="1054">为了能狠狠地报复一下狐狸，农夫在狐狸的尾巴上绑了一捆麻绳，然后点上火，让狐狸在院子里上蹿下跳。</seg>
<seg id="1055">As ill-luck would have it, however, the Fox made straight for the fields where the corn was standing ripe and ready for cutting.</seg>
<seg id="1055">然而，厄运却降临了，狐狸径直跑到农夫的田地里，</seg>
<seg id="1056">It quickly caught fire and was all burnt up, and the Farmer lost all his harvest.</seg>
<seg id="1056">正待收割的庄稼地迅即成了一片火海。最终，农夫颗粒无收。</seg>
<seg id="1057">Revenge is a two-edged sword.</seg>
<seg id="1057">复仇是把双刃剑。</seg>
<seg id="1058">VENUS AND THE CAT</seg>
<seg id="1058">维纳斯和猫</seg>
<seg id="1059">A Cat fell in love with a handsome young man, and begged the goddess Venus to change her into a woman.</seg>
<seg id="1059">一只母猫爱上了一个英俊的青年男子，请求爱神维纳斯将自己变成一个女人。</seg>
<seg id="1060">Venus was very gracious about it, and changed her at once into a beautiful maiden, whom the young man fell in love with at first sight and shortly afterwards married.</seg>
<seg id="1060">仁慈的爱神维纳斯同意了她的请求，立即将她变成了一个美丽的少女。青年男子对她一见钟情，很快两人就结婚了。</seg>
<seg id="1061">One day Venus thought she would like to see whether the Cat had changed her habits as well as her form;</seg>
<seg id="1061">有一天，维纳斯想去看看那只变身后的猫是否也改变了以往的习性，</seg>
<seg id="1062">so she let a mouse run loose in the room where they were.</seg>
<seg id="1062">便将一只老鼠放进了他们的房子里。</seg>
<seg id="1063">Forgetting everything, the young woman had no sooner seen the mouse than up she jumped and was after it like a shot:</seg>
<seg id="1063">年轻女子把现在的身份忘得一干二净，一见到老鼠，便立刻跳下床去追。</seg>
<seg id="1064">at which the goddess was so disgusted that she changed her back again into a Cat.</seg>
<seg id="1064">爱神见此十分气愤，又将母猫变回了原来的模样。</seg>
<seg id="1065">THE CROW AND THE SWAN</seg>
<seg id="1065">乌鸦和天鹅</seg>
<seg id="1066">A Crow was filled with envy on seeing the beautiful white plumage of a Swan, and thought it was due to the water in which the Swan constantly bathed and swam.</seg>
<seg id="1066">一只乌鸦非常妒忌白天鹅那美丽的羽翼，以为那一身漂亮的白色羽毛是由于经常在水中游泳和洗浴而得来的。</seg>
<seg id="1067">So he left the neighbourhood of the altars, where he got his living by picking up bits of the meat offered in sacrifice, and went and lived among the pools and streams.</seg>
<seg id="1067">于是，乌鸦便离开了靠着肉类祭祀品而赖以谋生的祭坛，前往池塘和溪流中居住。</seg>
<seg id="1068">But though he bathed and washed his feathers many times a day, he didn't make them any whiter, and at last died of hunger into the bargain.</seg>
<seg id="1068">可是，尽管他日日勤于在水中梳洗自己的羽毛，却总也不能使其变成白色，反而因忍饥挨饿而死去。</seg>
<seg id="1069">You may change your habits, but not your nature.</seg>
<seg id="1069">你可以改变习惯，却很难改变本质。</seg>
<seg id="1070">THE STAG WITH ONE EYE</seg>
<seg id="1070">独眼鹿</seg>
<seg id="1071">A Stag, blind of one eye, was grazing close to the sea-shore and kept his sound eye turned towards the land, so as to be able to perceive the approach of the hounds, while the blind eye he turned towards the sea, never suspecting that any danger would threaten him from that quarter.</seg>
<seg id="1071">有一只瞎了一只眼的鹿，在靠近海边的草场游荡，他用那只好眼睛注视着陆地，以防备猎人的攻击，而用那只瞎了的眼对着大海，以为海上不会对他有什么危险。</seg>
<seg id="1072">As it fell out, however, some sailors, coasting along the shore, spied him and shot an arrow at him, by which he was mortally wounded.</seg>
<seg id="1072">然而，正从海上经过此处的几个水手看见了这头鹿，一箭射倒了他。</seg>
<seg id="1073">As he lay dying, he said to himself, "Wretch that I am!</seg>
<seg id="1073">鹿受了致命重伤，将要咽气的时候，他自言自语地说：“我真是不幸！</seg>
<seg id="1074">I bethought me of the dangers of the land, whence none assailed me:</seg>
<seg id="1074">我确信地上会有危险，可是却什么也没发生；</seg>
<seg id="1075">but I feared no peril from the sea, yet thence has come my ruin."</seg>
<seg id="1075">而我以为大海这面没什么危险，但是却要了我的命。”</seg>
<seg id="1076">Misfortune often assails us from an unexpected quarter.</seg>
<seg id="1076">不幸经常从出人意料的地方攻击我们。</seg>
<seg id="1077">THE FLY AND THE DRAUGHT-MULE</seg>
<seg id="1077">苍蝇和拉车的骡子</seg>
<seg id="1078">A Fly sat on one of the shafts of a cart and said to the Mule who was pulling it, "How slow you are!</seg>
<seg id="1078">一只苍蝇坐在马车的车轴上，对拉车的骡子说：“你走得太慢了！</seg>
<seg id="1079">Do mend your pace, or I shall have to use my sting as a goad."</seg>
<seg id="1079">再走快一点，不然我就要咬你一下，来刺激你了。”</seg>
<seg id="1080">The Mule was not in the least disturbed.</seg>
<seg id="1080">骡子丝毫没有感到不安。</seg>
<seg id="1081">"Behind me, in the cart," said he, "sits my master.</seg>
<seg id="1081">“主人正坐在我身后的马车上，”骡子说，</seg>
<seg id="1082">He holds the reins, and flicks me with his whip, and him I obey, but I don't want any of your impertinence.</seg>
<seg id="1082">“他握着缰绳，而且还会用鞭子来抽打我。我只遵从他的命令，不需要你来指指点点。</seg>
<seg id="1083">I know when I may dawdle and when I may not."</seg>
<seg id="1083">我很清楚什么时候该快，什么时候该慢。”</seg>
<seg id="1084">THE COCK AND THE JEWEL</seg>
<seg id="1084">公鸡和宝石</seg>
<seg id="1085">A Cock, scratching the ground for something to eat, turned up a Jewel that had by chance been dropped there.</seg>
<seg id="1085">一只公鸡在田野里觅食，突然发现了一块宝玉，不知是谁不小心掉在这里了。</seg>
<seg id="1086">"Ho!" said he, "a fine thing you are, no doubt, and, had your owner found you, great would his joy have been.</seg>
<seg id="1086">公鸡说道：“哇，你可真漂亮，要是你的主人找到了你，肯定会喜出望外。</seg>
<seg id="1087">But for me! give me a single grain of corn before all the jewels in the world."</seg>
<seg id="1087">不过，对我来说，你却毫无用处。与其得到世界上的所有珠宝，还不如得到一颗麦子更好。”</seg>
<seg id="1088">THE WOLF AND THE SHEPHERD</seg>
<seg id="1088">狼和牧羊人</seg>
<seg id="1089">A Wolf hung about near a flock of sheep for a long time, but made no attempt to molest them.</seg>
<seg id="1089">一只狼跟在羊群后面很长时间了，但是却没有打扰他们。</seg>
<seg id="1090">The Shepherd at first kept a sharp eye on him, for he naturally thought he meant mischief:</seg>
<seg id="1090">起先，牧羊人一直提心吊胆地盯着狼，因为他本能地以为狼是个坏蛋。</seg>
<seg id="1091">but as time went by and the Wolf showed no inclination to meddle with the flock, he began to look upon him more as a protector than as an enemy:</seg>
<seg id="1091">可是随着时间的推移，狼却丝毫没有要攻击羊群的迹象，牧羊人便以为这是一个保护者，而非敌对者。</seg>
<seg id="1092">and when one day some errand took him to the city, he felt no uneasiness at leaving the Wolf with the sheep.</seg>
<seg id="1092">终于有一天，牧羊人要进城办事，便把羊群留给狼守护。</seg>
<seg id="1093">But as soon as his back was turned the Wolf attacked them and killed the greater number.</seg>
<seg id="1093">然而，就在牧羊人刚转身走开时，狼就袭击了羊群，并且杀死了大部分羊。</seg>
<seg id="1094">When the Shepherd returned and saw the havoc he had wrought, he cried, "It serves me right for trusting my flock to a Wolf."</seg>
<seg id="1094">牧羊人回来后，见此情景十分后悔，哭喊道：“我竟然把羊群托付给一只狼，真是活该呀！”</seg>
<seg id="1095">THE FARMER AND THE STORK</seg>
<seg id="1095">农夫和鹳</seg>
<seg id="1096">A Farmer set some traps in a field which he had lately sown with corn, in order to catch the cranes which came to pick up the seed.</seg>
<seg id="1096">为了捉住那些前来偷吃种子的鹤，农夫在刚刚播种的田里布下许多陷阱。</seg>
<seg id="1097">When he returned to look at his traps he found several cranes caught, and among them a Stork, which begged to be let go, and said, "You ought not to kill me:</seg>
<seg id="1097">等农夫再来检查陷阱时，发现几只鹤被捉住了，其中还有一只鹳。鹳哀求农夫放了自己，他说：“你不应该杀了我，</seg>
<seg id="1098">I am not a crane, but a Stork, as you can easily see by my feathers, and I am the most honest and harmless of birds."</seg>
<seg id="1098">因为我又不是鹤，而是一只鹳，你仔细看看我的羽毛，就明白我与鹤完全不同了。我是最诚实的鸟儿，从不伤害别人。”</seg>
<seg id="1099">But the Farmer replied, "It's nothing to me what you are:</seg>
<seg id="1099">然而，农夫却说：“你究竟是什么，对我来说并不重要，</seg>
<seg id="1100">I find you among these cranes, who ruin my crops, and, like them, you shall suffer."</seg>
<seg id="1100">但是我在网中发现了你，那你就得和这些毁了庄稼的鹤一起受苦了。”</seg>
<seg id="1101">If you choose bad companions no one will believe that you are anything but bad yourself.</seg>
<seg id="1101">如果你选择与坏人为伍，没有人会相信你是好人。</seg>
<seg id="1102">THE CHARGER AND THE MILLER</seg>
<seg id="1102">战马和磨坊主</seg>
<seg id="1103">A Horse, who had been used to carry his rider into battle, felt himself growing old and chose to work in a mill instead.</seg>
<seg id="1103">一匹曾经驮着主人驰骋沙场的战马，感到自己年事已高，便选择离开战场，到一个磨坊里去工作。</seg>
<seg id="1104">He now no longer found himself stepping out proudly to the beating of the drums, but was compelled to slave away all day grinding the corn.</seg>
<seg id="1104">他发现自己再也无法在听到战鼓雷鸣时昂头挺胸地前进了，只能被迫埋头于终日磨谷子的劳作之中。</seg>
<seg id="1105">Bewailing his hard lot, he said one day to the Miller, "Ah me! I was once a splendid war-horse, gaily caparisoned, and attended by a groom whose sole duty was to see to my wants.</seg>
<seg id="1105">战马垂头丧气地哀叹着自己的命运，有一天，他对磨坊主说：“唉，我曾经可是一匹光彩照人的战马，不仅披着华丽的战袍，而且还有专门的马倌照顾我。</seg>
<seg id="1106">How different is my present condition!</seg>
<seg id="1106">现如今，我这是什么下场呀！</seg>
<seg id="1107">I wish I had never given up the battlefield for the mill."</seg>
<seg id="1107">真希望我当初没有离开战场，为什么要到这个磨坊来呀。”</seg>
<seg id="1108">The Miller replied with asperity, "It's no use your regretting the past.</seg>
<seg id="1108">磨坊主粗暴地回答说：“不必追悔过去，</seg>
<seg id="1109">Fortune has many ups and downs: you must just take them as they come."</seg>
<seg id="1109">命运总会有所起伏，随缘而安就好了。”</seg>
<seg id="1110">THE GRASSHOPPER AND THE OWL</seg>
<seg id="1110">蚂蚱和猫头鹰</seg>
<seg id="1111">An Owl, who lived in a hollow tree, was in the habit of feeding by night and sleeping by day;</seg>
<seg id="1111">栖息在一棵枯树上的猫头鹰，习惯于晚上觅食、白天睡觉。</seg>
<seg id="1112">but her slumbers were greatly disturbed by the chirping of a Grasshopper, who had taken up his abode in the branches.</seg>
<seg id="1112">可是，她白天却也睡不好，一只早已在树丛间做窝的蚂蚱总发出啁啾声，吵得她无法入睡。</seg>
<seg id="1113">She begged him repeatedly to have some consideration for her comfort, but the Grasshopper, if anything, only chirped the louder.</seg>
<seg id="1113">猫头鹰不断地请求蚂蚱考虑一下她的情况，可蚂蚱却仍然大声叫个不停。</seg>
<seg id="1114">At last the Owl could stand it no longer, but determined to rid herself of the pest by means of a trick.</seg>
<seg id="1114">最后，猫头鹰再也受不了了，决定设计除掉蚂蚱。</seg>
<seg id="1115">Addressing herself to the Grasshopper, she said in her pleasantest manner, "As I cannot sleep for your song, which, believe me, is as sweet as the notes of Apollo's lyre, I have a mind to taste some nectar, which Minerva gave me the other day.</seg>
<seg id="1115">于是，猫头鹰装出一副高兴样，对蚂蚱说：“尽管我被你的歌声惊扰，睡不着觉，但是请相信我，你的歌声如同阿波罗神的七弦琴一样动听。我正想喝一点美味琼浆，这可是密涅瓦（智慧女神，即希腊神话中的雅典娜）送给我的。</seg>
<seg id="1116">Won't you come in and join me?"</seg>
<seg id="1116">你要不要上来和我一起享用呢？”</seg>
<seg id="1117">The Grasshopper was flattered by the praise of his song, and his mouth, too, watered at the mention of the delicious drink, so he said he would be delighted.</seg>
<seg id="1117">蚂蚱正得意于猫头鹰对自己歌声的奉承，一听到有琼浆玉液，嘴巴里就开始流口水了，所以，他很高兴地接受了邀请。</seg>
<seg id="1118">No sooner had he got inside the hollow where the Owl was sitting than she pounced upon him and ate him up.</seg>
<seg id="1118">待他刚一飞上去，猫头鹰就从树洞中冲出来，扑过去抓住蚂蚱，吃掉了他。</seg>
<seg id="1119">THE GRASSHOPPER AND THE ANTS</seg>
<seg id="1119">蚂蚱和蚂蚁</seg>
<seg id="1120">One fine day in winter some Ants were busy drying their store of corn, which had got rather damp during a long spell of rain.</seg>
<seg id="1120">冬天一个温暖如春的日子里，蚂蚁们正忙着晒干自己存储的粮食。由于下了很长时间的雨，粮食已经非常潮湿了。</seg>
<seg id="1121">Presently up came a Grasshopper and begged them to spare her a few grains,</seg>
<seg id="1121">这时，来了一只蚂蚱，向他们乞讨一点粮食。</seg>
<seg id="1122">"For," she said, "I'm simply starving."</seg>
<seg id="1122">“因为，”蚂蚱说，“我实在是饿坏了。”</seg>
<seg id="1123">The Ants stopped work for a moment, though this was against their principles.</seg>
<seg id="1123">尽管有点违背原则，但蚂蚁们还是停下了手头的工作。</seg>
<seg id="1124">"May we ask," said they, "what you were doing with yourself all last summer?</seg>
<seg id="1124">“我们能问你一下吗？”他们说，“整个夏天你都在做些什么呢？</seg>
<seg id="1125">Why didn't you collect a store of food for the winter?"</seg>
<seg id="1125">为什么不为冬天储存一些粮食呢？”</seg>
<seg id="1126">"The fact is," replied the Grasshopper, "I was so busy singing that I hadn't the time."</seg>
<seg id="1126">“实际上，”蚂蚱回答道，“我一直在忙着唱歌，根本没有时间存储粮食。”</seg>
<seg id="1127">"If you spent the summer singing," replied the Ants, "you can't do better than spend the winter dancing."</seg>
<seg id="1127">“如果你整个夏天都在唱歌，”蚂蚁们回答道，“那么，你最好在冬天就忙着跳舞吧。”</seg>
<seg id="1128">And they chuckled and went on with their work.</seg>
<seg id="1128">他们哈哈大笑起来，继续忙于各自的工作。</seg>
<seg id="1129">THE FARMER AND THE VIPER</seg>
<seg id="1129">农夫与蛇</seg>
<seg id="1130">One winter a Farmer found a Viper frozen and numb with cold, and out of pity picked it up and placed it in his bosom.</seg>
<seg id="1130">在一个冬日，农夫发现了一条冻僵了的蛇，出于同情心，农夫便把蛇放在自己怀里。</seg>
<seg id="1131">The Viper was no sooner revived by the warmth than it turned upon its benefactor and inflicted a fatal bite upon him;</seg>
<seg id="1131">蛇感觉到一点温暖苏醒过来，立刻就冲着恩人咬了一大口，使他受到了致命的伤害。</seg>
<seg id="1132">and as the poor man lay dying, he cried, "I have only got what I deserved, for taking compassion on so villainous a creature."</seg>
<seg id="1132">这个可怜的农夫在临死前说：“这是我应得的报应，竟然会怜悯一个罪大恶极的生灵。”</seg>
<seg id="1133">Kindness is thrown away upon the evil.</seg>
<seg id="1133">在邪恶面前，仁慈应被抛开。</seg>
<seg id="1134">THE TWO FROGS</seg>
<seg id="1134">两只青蛙</seg>
<seg id="1135">Two Frogs were neighbours.</seg>
<seg id="1135">两只青蛙比邻而居。</seg>
<seg id="1136">One lived in a marsh, where there was plenty of water, which frogs love:</seg>
<seg id="1136">一只住在青蛙们钟爱的湿地里，</seg>
<seg id="1137">the other in a lane some distance away, where all the water to be had was that which lay in the ruts after rain.</seg>
<seg id="1137">另一只却住在稍微远一点的一条小路上，只有下过雨后，那里才能形成一个小水洼。</seg>
<seg id="1138">The Marsh Frog warned his friend and pressed him to come and live with him in the marsh, for he would find his quarters there far more comfortable and--what was still more important--more safe.</seg>
<seg id="1138">住在湿地里的青蛙提醒并督促自己的朋友，尽快搬到湿地这边来住，因为这里十分舒适，更重要的是，这里更安全。</seg>
<seg id="1139">But the other refused, saying that he could not bring himself to move from a place to which he had become accustomed.</seg>
<seg id="1139">可是，另一只青蛙却拒绝了，说自己不想离开已经习惯了的地方。</seg>
<seg id="1140">A few days afterwards a heavy waggon came down the lane, and he was crushed to death under the wheels.</seg>
<seg id="1140">结果，没过几天，一辆载着重物的货车经过小路，而这只青蛙不幸被车轮碾死了。</seg>
<seg id="1141">THE COBBLER TURNED DOCTOR</seg>
<seg id="1141">修鞋匠行医</seg>
<seg id="1142">A very unskilful Cobbler, finding himself unable to make a living at his trade, gave up mending boots and took to doctoring instead.</seg>
<seg id="1142">一个手艺不怎么样的鞋匠发现自己无法靠修鞋来维持生计，便放弃了补鞋的活，改行做起了医生。</seg>
<seg id="1143">He gave out that he had the secret of a universal antidote against all poisons, and acquired no small reputation, thanks to his talent for puffing himself.</seg>
<seg id="1143">他对外宣称自己有一个可祛百毒的解药秘方，因为出色的吹牛本领，他骗取了人们的信任，赢得了好名声。</seg>
<seg id="1144">One day, however, he fell very ill;</seg>
<seg id="1144">然而，有一天，他自己得了重病。</seg>
<seg id="1145">and the King of the country bethought him that he would test the value of his remedy.</seg>
<seg id="1145">国王想借此试验一下他的药效，</seg>
<seg id="1146">Calling, therefore, for a cup, he poured out a dose of the antidote, and, under pretence of mixing poison with it, added a little water, and commanded him to drink it.</seg>
<seg id="1146">因此便叫人拿来一个杯子，倒了一点他的解药，然后加了些水，谎称这是毒药，随后又命令他喝下去。</seg>
<seg id="1147">Terrified by the fear of being poisoned, the Cobbler confessed that he knew nothing about medicine, and that his antidote was worthless.</seg>
<seg id="1147">补鞋匠担心会中毒，便承认自己并不懂什么医药知识，而那个解药也一无是处。</seg>
<seg id="1148">Then the King summoned his subjects and addressed them as follows: "What folly could be greater than yours?</seg>
<seg id="1148">国王便召集起所有臣民，对他们说：“你们简直都愚笨至极，</seg>
<seg id="1149">Here is this Cobbler to whom no one will send his boots to be mended, and yet you have not hesitated to entrust him with your lives!"</seg>
<seg id="1149">这就是那个没人愿意让他给补靴子的修鞋匠，而你们竟然毫不犹豫地将自己的性命托付给他！”</seg>
<seg id="1150">THE ASS, THE COCK, AND THE LION</seg>
<seg id="1150">驴、公鸡和狮子</seg>
<seg id="1151">An Ass and a Cock were in a cattle-pen together.</seg>
<seg id="1151">一头驴和一只公鸡在牛圈里一起生活。</seg>
<seg id="1152">Presently a Lion, who had been starving for days, came along and was just about to fall upon the Ass and make a meal of him when the Cock, rising to his full height and flapping his wings vigorously, uttered a tremendous crow.</seg>
<seg id="1152">不久，一只饿了好几天的狮子走过来，想要逮一头驴当饭吃。这时，公鸡站起来，扑腾着翅膀大叫了起来。</seg>
<seg id="1153">Now, if there is one thing that frightens a Lion, it is the crowing of a Cock:</seg>
<seg id="1153">假如真有什么东西能使狮子害怕的话，那一定是公鸡扑腾着翅膀的大叫声。</seg>
<seg id="1154">and this one had no sooner heard the noise than he fled.</seg>
<seg id="1154">[无]</seg>
<seg id="1155">The Ass was mightily elated at this, and thought that, if the Lion couldn't face a Cock, he would be still less likely to stand up to an Ass:</seg>
<seg id="1155">而驴却因此而洋洋自得，心想如果狮子都不敢面对一只小公鸡，那就更不敢面对一头驴了。</seg>
<seg id="1156">so he ran out and pursued him.</seg>
<seg id="1156">于是，他立即跑出去追赶狮子。</seg>
<seg id="1157">But when the two had got well out of sight and hearing of the Cock, the Lion suddenly turned upon the Ass and ate him up.</seg>
<seg id="1157">然而，等他们跑远了，听不到公鸡的叫声时，狮子猛然转过身来，把驴吃掉了。</seg>
<seg id="1158">False confidence often leads to disaster.</seg>
<seg id="1158">盲目的自信通常会导致失败。</seg>
<seg id="1159">THE BELLY AND THE MEMBERS</seg>
<seg id="1159">胃和体内的各器官</seg>
<seg id="1160">The Members of the Body once rebelled against the Belly.</seg>
<seg id="1160">有一次，人体内的各个器官集体抗议胃。</seg>
<seg id="1161">"You," they said to the Belly, "live in luxury and sloth, and never do a stroke of work;</seg>
<seg id="1161">他们说：“你过着享受的日子，又很懒惰，从来没有干过什么活，</seg>
<seg id="1162">while we not only have to do all the hard work there is to be done, but are actually your slaves and have to minister to all your wants.</seg>
<seg id="1162">而我们不仅要承担繁重的必要工作，还得甘当你的奴隶，为满足你的各种欲望而服务。</seg>
<seg id="1163">Now, we will do so no longer, and you can shift for yourself for the future."</seg>
<seg id="1163">从现在起，我们什么也不做了，你自力更生吧。”</seg>
<seg id="1164">They were as good as their word, and left the Belly to starve.</seg>
<seg id="1164">他们的确说到做到了，胃只得一直挨饿。</seg>
<seg id="1165">The result was just what might have been expected: the whole Body soon began to fail, and the Members and all shared in the general collapse.</seg>
<seg id="1165">而结果可能是他们早已预料到的——整个身体很快就虚弱下来，体内的各个器官也跟着一起衰弱下来。</seg>
<seg id="1166">And then they saw too late how foolish they had been.</seg>
<seg id="1166">他们这才悔恨自己的愚蠢，可为时已晚了。</seg>
<seg id="1167">THE BALD MAN AND THE FLY</seg>
<seg id="1167">秃子和苍蝇</seg>
<seg id="1168">A Fly settled on the head of a Bald Man and bit him.</seg>
<seg id="1168">一只苍蝇落在一个秃顶的男人头上，还咬了他一口。</seg>
<seg id="1169">In his eagerness to kill it, he hit himself a smart slap.</seg>
<seg id="1169">带着想杀死它的迫切心情，男人猛打了自己一下。</seg>
<seg id="1170">But the Fly escaped, and said to him in derision, "You tried to kill me for just one little bite;</seg>
<seg id="1170">但是，苍蝇却逃脱了，并且嘲笑他说：“就因为我小小地咬了你一口，你就想杀死我。</seg>
<seg id="1171">what will you do to yourself now, for the heavy smack you have just given yourself?"</seg>
<seg id="1171">看看你现在都干了些什么，反倒狠狠地打了自己。”</seg>
<seg id="1172">"Oh, for that blow I bear no grudge," he replied, "for I never intended myself any harm;</seg>
<seg id="1172">“噢，我打自己倒不怨恨，”那个人答道，“因为我从来没有想过伤害自己，</seg>
<seg id="1173">but as for you, you contemptible insect, who live by sucking human blood, I'd have borne a good deal more than that for the satisfaction of dashing the life out of you!"</seg>
<seg id="1173">而你却是一个以吸吮人类鲜血为生的卑鄙家伙，要了你的命，才会让我舒服点！”</seg>
<seg id="1174">THE ASS AND THE WOLF</seg>
<seg id="1174">驴和狼</seg>
<seg id="1175">An Ass was feeding in a meadow, and, catching sight of his enemy the Wolf in the distance, pretended to be very lame and hobbled painfully along.</seg>
<seg id="1175">一头驴正在牧场里吃草，看见远处有一只狼向他跑来，便装出瘸腿的样子，独自徐徐前行。</seg>
<seg id="1176">When the Wolf came up, he asked the Ass how he came to be so lame, and the Ass replied that in going through a hedge he had trodden on a thorn, and he begged the Wolf to pull it out with his teeth,</seg>
<seg id="1176">狼走过来，问驴为何一瘸一拐，驴则回答说自己在越过篱笆时脚掌被刺扎伤，并且还请求狼用牙齿帮他拔掉刺。</seg>
<seg id="1177">"In case," he said, "when you eat me, it should stick in your throat and hurt you very much."</seg>
<seg id="1177">“只是以防万一，”驴说，“你吃我的时候，这根刺有可能会卡在你的喉咙里，会弄疼你的。”</seg>
<seg id="1178">The Wolf said he would, and told the Ass to lift up his foot, and gave his whole mind to getting out the thorn.</seg>
<seg id="1178">狼信以为真，便让驴抬起腿来，好让他全力拨出那根刺。</seg>
<seg id="1179">But the Ass suddenly let out with his heels and fetched the Wolf a fearful kick in the mouth, breaking his teeth;</seg>
<seg id="1179">然而，驴突然抬腿用脚后跟对准狼的嘴使劲一蹬，踢碎了狼的牙齿，接着便全速跑开了。</seg>
<seg id="1180">and then he galloped off at full speed.</seg>
<seg id="1180">[无]</seg>
<seg id="1181">As soon as he could speak the Wolf growled to himself, "It serves me right:</seg>
<seg id="1181">刚能开口讲话，狼就咆哮道：“我真活该！</seg>
<seg id="1182">my father taught me to kill, and I ought to have stuck to that trade instead of attempting to cure."</seg>
<seg id="1182">爸爸教我要杀死它，我真应该乖乖听话，怎么还想去救他呢？”</seg>
<seg id="1183">THE MONKEY AND THE CAMEL</seg>
<seg id="1183">猴子和骆驼</seg>
<seg id="1184">At a gathering of all the beasts the Monkey gave an exhibition of dancing and entertained the company vastly.</seg>
<seg id="1184">在一次百兽集会上，猴子兴奋地载歌载舞，大获赞赏。</seg>
<seg id="1185">There was great applause at the finish, which excited the envy of the Camel and made him desire to win the favour of the assembly by the same means.</seg>
<seg id="1185">待表演完后，百兽个个为之喝彩。骆驼十分嫉妒猴子，就想用同样的方式也赢得大家的喝彩。</seg>
<seg id="1186">So he got up from his place and began dancing, but he cut such a ridiculous figure as he plunged about, and made such a grotesque exhibition of his ungainly person, that the beasts all fell upon him with ridicule and drove him away.</seg>
<seg id="1186">于是，他站了起来，开始显示自己的舞技，他那怪异的姿态真是洋相百出。结果，因为这不雅的表演，百兽们哄他下台，并把他赶跑了。</seg>
<seg id="1187">THE SICK MAN AND THE DOCTOR</seg>
<seg id="1187">病人和医生</seg>
<seg id="1188">A Sick Man received a visit from his Doctor, who asked him how he was.</seg>
<seg id="1188">有个人生了病，请医生来看病，医生问他感觉如何。</seg>
<seg id="1189">"Fairly well, Doctor," said he, "but I find I sweat a great deal."</seg>
<seg id="1189">“还好，医生，”他说，“就是发现有点出汗过多。”</seg>
<seg id="1190">"Ah," said the Doctor, "that's a good sign."</seg>
<seg id="1190">医生说：“这是好事。”</seg>
<seg id="1191">On his next visit he asked the same question, and his patient replied, "I'm much as usual, but I've taken to having shivering fits, which leave me cold all over."</seg>
<seg id="1191">第二次来看病人时，医生又问他同样的问题，他回答说：“和以前差不多，就是有点发抖，总感觉冷。”</seg>
<seg id="1192">"Ah," said the Doctor, "that's a good sign too."</seg>
<seg id="1192">医生又说：“这也是好现象。”</seg>
<seg id="1193">When he came the third time and inquired as before about his patient's health, the Sick Man said that he felt very feverish.</seg>
<seg id="1193">医生第三次来看他，又询问他的健康状况时，病人说感觉自己在发烧。</seg>
<seg id="1194">"A very good sign," said the Doctor;</seg>
<seg id="1194">“非常好的现象，”医生说，</seg>
<seg id="1195">"you are doing very nicely indeed."</seg>
<seg id="1195">“其实，你的身体很正常。”</seg>
<seg id="1196">Afterwards a friend came to see the invalid, and on asking him how he did, received this reply: "My dear friend, I'm dying of good signs."</seg>
<seg id="1196">随后，病人的一个朋友来看他，并且问他感觉如何，他说：“我就要因为这些好现象而丧命了。”</seg>
<seg id="1197">THE TRAVELLERS AND THE PLANE-TREE</seg>
<seg id="1197">旅人和法国梧桐树</seg>
<seg id="1198">Two Travellers were walking along a bare and dusty road in the heat of a summer's day.</seg>
<seg id="1198">夏季里的一天，正值中午酷热难耐时，两个行人走在空旷且尘土飞扬的马路上。</seg>
<seg id="1199">Coming presently to a Plane-tree, they joyfully turned aside to shelter from the burning rays of the sun in the deep shade of its spreading branches.</seg>
<seg id="1199">不久，他们来到一棵梧桐树下，躺在茂密树叶遮蔽的阴凉地里休息，从而躲避太阳的毒晒。</seg>
<seg id="1200">As they rested, looking up into the tree, one of them remarked to his companion, "What a useless tree the Plane is!</seg>
<seg id="1200">在休息时，他们抬头看着枝叶四散的大树，其中一人对同伴说：“这棵树没什么用处呀！</seg>
<seg id="1201">It bears no fruit and is of no service to man at all."</seg>
<seg id="1201">它没有结果，对人类没有什么好处。”</seg>
<seg id="1202">The Plane-tree interrupted him with indignation.</seg>
<seg id="1202">梧桐树生气地打断了他们的谈话。</seg>
<seg id="1203">"You ungrateful creature!" it cried:</seg>
<seg id="1203">“你们这些不知好歹的家伙！”它吼道，</seg>
<seg id="1204">"you come and take shelter under me from the scorching sun, and then, in the very act of enjoying the cool shade of my foliage, you abuse me and call me good for nothing!"</seg>
<seg id="1204">“你们走过来在这里寻找遮挡太阳的避难所，一边享受着我的树叶带来的阴凉，一边还骂我，说我是无用之材！”</seg>
<seg id="1205">Many a service is met with ingratitude.</seg>
<seg id="1205">好心提供帮助，却遇上了忘恩负义之徒。</seg>
<seg id="1206">THE FLEA AND THE OX</seg>
<seg id="1206">跳蚤和公牛</seg>
<seg id="1207">A Flea once said to an Ox, "How comes it that a big strong fellow like you is content to serve mankind, and do all their hard work for them, while I, who am no bigger than you see, live on their bodies and drink my fill of their blood, and never do a stroke for it all?"</seg>
<seg id="1207">有一次，跳蚤问公牛：“像你这般高大强壮的家伙，竟然满足于终日为人类服务，为他们付出辛勤的劳动；而像我这样连你都看不清楚的小虫子，却在人类的肉体上生活，毫无顾忌地吸他们的鲜血，什么劳动也不用付出，你怎么会受得了呢？”</seg>
<seg id="1208">To which the Ox replied, "Men are very kind to me, and so I am grateful to them:</seg>
<seg id="1208">公牛回答说：“人类对我很好，所以我很感激他们。</seg>
<seg id="1209">they feed and house me well, and every now and then they show their fondness for me by patting me on the head and neck."</seg>
<seg id="1209">他们给我吃的，给我住的，还经常抚摸、拍打我的头和脖子，以示喜爱。”</seg>
<seg id="1210">"They'd pat me, too," said the Flea, "if I let them:</seg>
<seg id="1210">“他们也打我，”跳蚤说，“如果我愿意挨打的话，</seg>
<seg id="1211">but I take good care they don't, or there would be nothing left of me."</seg>
<seg id="1211">可是，我很小心地不让他们打我，否则，我的小命可就保不住了。”</seg>
<seg id="1212">THE BIRDS, THE BEASTS, AND THE BAT</seg>
<seg id="1212">鸟、兽和蝙蝠</seg>
<seg id="1213">The Birds were at war with the Beasts, and many battles were fought with varying success on either side.</seg>
<seg id="1213">鸟类和野兽开战了，双方各有胜负，都没占到什么便宜。</seg>
<seg id="1214">The Bat did not throw in his lot definitely with either party, but when things went well for the Birds he was found fighting in their ranks;</seg>
<seg id="1214">蝙蝠显然没有明确地加入到任何一方之中，而总是依附强的一方。</seg>
<seg id="1215">when, on the other hand, the Beasts got the upper hand, he was to be found among the Beasts.</seg>
<seg id="1215">当鸟类占上风时，就会发现他在鸟群中；而当兽类占上风时，他又跑到了兽群之中。</seg>
<seg id="1216">No one paid any attention to him while the war lasted:</seg>
<seg id="1216">在战争过程中，谁也没有注意到他。</seg>
<seg id="1217">but when it was over, and peace was restored, neither the Birds nor the Beasts would have anything to do with so double-faced a traitor, and so he remains to this day a solitary outcast from both.</seg>
<seg id="1217">然而，战争一结束，鸟和兽宣告和平相处时，都不想要蝙蝠这样的两面派。所以，从此以后，蝙蝠总在白天躲起来，让双方都看不到他。</seg>
<seg id="1218">THE EAGLE, THE JACKDAW, AND THE SHEPHERD</seg>
<seg id="1218">老鹰、寒鸦和牧羊人</seg>
<seg id="1219">One day a Jackdaw saw an Eagle swoop down on a lamb and carry it off in its talons.</seg>
<seg id="1219">有一天，一只寒鸦看到老鹰从高岩上直飞而下，抓起一只羊羔就飞走了。</seg>
<seg id="1220">"My word," said the Jackdaw, "I'll do that myself."</seg>
<seg id="1220">“我的天呀，”寒鸦说，“我也要试试。”</seg>
<seg id="1221">So it flew high up into the air, and then came shooting down with a great whirring of wings on to the back of a big ram.</seg>
<seg id="1221">于是，他飞上高空，接着又扑腾着翅膀俯冲下来，扑通一声猛扑到一只公羊背上。</seg>
<seg id="1222">It had no sooner alighted than its claws got caught fast in the wool, and nothing it could do was of any use:</seg>
<seg id="1222">刚一飞下来，它的爪子就被羊毛缠住了，无论如何也拔不出来。</seg>
<seg id="1223">there it stuck, flapping away, and only making things worse instead of better.</seg>
<seg id="1223">尽管他使劲拍打着翅膀，可仍然被卡在那里，不但于事无补，反倒更加糟糕了。</seg>
<seg id="1224">By and by up came the Shepherd.</seg>
<seg id="1224">不久，牧羊人走过来了。</seg>
<seg id="1225">"Oho," he said, "so that's what you'd be doing, is it?"</seg>
<seg id="1225">“哦，”他说，“这就是你想做的事情，是吗？”</seg>
<seg id="1226">And he took the Jackdaw, and clipped its wings and carried it home to his children.</seg>
<seg id="1226">他拿起寒鸦，剪断了他的翅膀，带回家给孩子玩。</seg>
<seg id="1227">It looked so odd that they didn't know what to make of it.</seg>
<seg id="1227">寒鸦的样子非常奇怪，孩子们都不知道它是什么东西。</seg>
<seg id="1228">"What sort of bird is it, father?" they asked.</seg>
<seg id="1228">“爸爸，这是一种什么鸟呀？”孩子们问道。</seg>
<seg id="1229">"It's a Jackdaw," he replied, "and nothing but a Jackdaw:</seg>
<seg id="1229">牧羊人回答道：“这是一只寒鸦，只不过是一只寒鸦而已，</seg>
<seg id="1230">but it wants to be taken for an Eagle."</seg>
<seg id="1230">可他却想当一只老鹰。”</seg>
<seg id="1231">If you attempt what is beyond your power, your trouble will be wasted and you court not only misfortune but ridicule.</seg>
<seg id="1231">如果你想做些超出自己能力范围之外的事，不但徒劳无功，还会给自己带来不幸和世人的嘲笑。</seg>
<seg id="1232">THE WOLF AND THE BOY</seg>
<seg id="1232">狼和男孩</seg>
<seg id="1233">A Wolf, who had just enjoyed a good meal and was in a playful mood, caught sight of a Boy lying flat upon the ground, and, realising that he was trying to hide, and that it was fear of himself that made him do this, he went up to him and said, "Aha, I've found you, you see;</seg>
<seg id="1233">刚刚饱餐了一顿的狼正欣喜万分，这时，他看见一个男孩平躺在地上，并且意识到男孩正想藏起来，因为男孩害怕狼。他走到男孩跟前，说：“啊哈，你注意到我发现你了，</seg>
<seg id="1234">but if you can say three things to me, the truth of which cannot be disputed, I will spare your life."</seg>
<seg id="1234">不过，如果你能对我说出三件无可争议的事情来，我就饶了你的命。”</seg>
<seg id="1235">The Boy plucked up courage and thought for a moment, and then he said, "First, it is a pity you saw me;</seg>
<seg id="1235">男孩鼓起勇气，想了一会儿，说：“首先，很可惜，你看见了我；</seg>
<seg id="1236">secondly, I was a fool to let myself be seen;</seg>
<seg id="1236">其次，我很傻，竟然被你看见了；</seg>
<seg id="1237">and thirdly, we all hate wolves because they are always making unprovoked attacks upon our flocks."</seg>
<seg id="1237">第三，我们都讨厌狼，因为他们总会无端攻击我们的羊群。”</seg>
<seg id="1238">The Wolf replied, "Well, what you say is true enough from your point of view;</seg>
<seg id="1238">狼回答说：“嗯，从你的角度来看，你所说的都是事实，</seg>
<seg id="1239">so you may go."</seg>
<seg id="1239">所以你可以走了。”</seg>
<seg id="1240">THE MILLER, HIS SON, AND THEIR ASS</seg>
<seg id="1240">父亲、儿子和驴</seg>
<seg id="1241">A Miller, accompanied by his young Son, was driving his Ass to market in hopes of finding a purchaser for him.</seg>
<seg id="1241">磨坊主和小儿子牵着一头驴到邻近的市场上，希望能给驴找到一个新主人。</seg>
<seg id="1242">On the road they met a troop of girls, laughing and talking, who exclaimed, "Did you ever see such a pair of fools?</seg>
<seg id="1242">在路上，他们遇见了几个女孩子，她们笑着说：“你们看见过这样的傻瓜吗，</seg>
<seg id="1243">To be trudging along the dusty road when they might be riding!"</seg>
<seg id="1243">放着驴不骑，却要在尘土飞扬的路上走！”</seg>
<seg id="1244">The Miller thought there was sense in what they said;</seg>
<seg id="1244">磨坊主心想，她们说得有点道理，</seg>
<seg id="1245">so he made his Son mount the Ass, and himself walked at the side.</seg>
<seg id="1245">于是就让儿子骑上驴，自己则牵着驴走。</seg>
<seg id="1246">Presently they met some of his old cronies, who greeted them and said, "You'll spoil that Son of yours, letting him ride while you toil along on foot!</seg>
<seg id="1246">走了一会，他们遇到了几个老朋友，打过招呼后，朋友们说：“你把儿子宠坏了，竟然让他骑在驴上，而你却在地上辛辛苦苦地走！</seg>
<seg id="1247">Make him walk, young lazybones!</seg>
<seg id="1247">让他下来，这个小懒骨头！</seg>
<seg id="1248">It'll do him all the good in the world."</seg>
<seg id="1248">这样才对他有好处。”</seg>
<seg id="1249">The Miller followed their advice, and took his Son's place on the back of the Ass while the boy trudged along behind.</seg>
<seg id="1249">磨坊主听从了他们的建议，便叫儿子下来，自己骑了上去。</seg>
<seg id="1250">They had not gone far when they overtook a party of women and children, and the Miller heard them say, "What a selfish old man!</seg>
<seg id="1250">没走多远，他们又遇到一群妇女和孩子，磨坊主又听他们说：“这个老头可真自私，</seg>
<seg id="1251">He himself rides in comfort, but lets his poor little boy follow as best he can on his own legs!"</seg>
<seg id="1251">自己舒服地骑在驴上，让那可怜的孩子一路跟着跑！”</seg>
<seg id="1252">So he made his Son get up behind him.</seg>
<seg id="1252">于是，磨坊主立刻又叫儿子坐到他后面。</seg>
<seg id="1253">Further along the road they met some travellers, who asked the Miller whether the Ass he was riding was his own property, or a beast hired for the occasion.</seg>
<seg id="1253">又往前走了一段路后，他们又遇到了几个路人，他们问磨坊主胯下的这头驴子是自己的，还是临时租的。</seg>
<seg id="1254">He replied that it was his own, and that he was taking it to market to sell.</seg>
<seg id="1254">磨坊主说是自己的，正要去市场卖掉驴。</seg>
<seg id="1255">"Good heavens!" said they, "with a load like that the poor beast will be so exhausted by the time he gets there that no one will look at him.</seg>
<seg id="1255">“天啊！”他们说，“驮着你们俩一路走来，这个可怜的牲口看上去已经筋疲力尽了，等它到了市场里，估计没人愿意多看它一眼。</seg>
<seg id="1256">Why, you'd do better to carry him!"</seg>
<seg id="1256">也许你们抬着它去市场更好些！”</seg>
<seg id="1257">"Anything to please you," said the old man, "we can but try."</seg>
<seg id="1257">“只要你高兴就好，”磨坊主说，“我们可以试一下。”</seg>
<seg id="1258">So they got off, tied the Ass's legs together with a rope and slung him on a pole, and at last reached the town, carrying him between them.</seg>
<seg id="1258">于是，他和儿子一起跳下驴，用绳子绑好驴的四条腿，并用一根木棍挑起驴，最后父子俩终于抬着驴来到了镇上。</seg>
<seg id="1259">This was so absurd a sight that the people ran out in crowds to laugh at it, and chaffed the Father and Son unmercifully, some even calling them lunatics.</seg>
<seg id="1259">这个场面有点不寻常，很多人围过来看热闹，大家都取笑他们父子俩，说他们太残酷了，甚至还有人说他们是疯子。</seg>
<seg id="1260">They had then got to a bridge over the river, where the Ass, frightened by the noise and his unusual situation, kicked and struggled till he broke the ropes that bound him, and fell into the water and was drowned.</seg>
<seg id="1260">他们接着要穿过河上的一座桥，就在这时，被吵闹声和自己的奇怪姿势吓呆了的驴，用力挣断了绑缚它的绳子，掉到河里被冲走了。</seg>
<seg id="1261">Whereupon the unfortunate Miller, vexed and ashamed, made the best of his way home again, convinced that in trying to please all he had pleased none, and had lost his Ass into the bargain.</seg>
<seg id="1261">不幸的磨坊主又气愤又羞愧，连忙夺路而逃。他终于信服了一个道理——努力取悦所有人，其实等于谁也没取悦到，反倒还丢了自己的驴。</seg>
<seg id="1262">THE STAG AND THE VINE</seg>
<seg id="1262">牡鹿和葡萄藤</seg>
<seg id="1263">A Stag, pursued by the huntsmen, concealed himself under cover of a thick Vine.</seg>
<seg id="1263">一只鹿为了逃避猎人的追捕，躲藏在一棵茂盛的葡萄藤下。</seg>
<seg id="1264">They lost track of him and passed by his hiding-place without being aware that he was anywhere near.</seg>
<seg id="1264">猎人找不到鹿的踪迹了，虽然刚从葡萄藤旁经过，却并没有发现他。</seg>
<seg id="1265">Supposing all danger to be over, he presently began to browse on the leaves of the Vine.</seg>
<seg id="1265">鹿以为躲过了危险，便旁若无人地开始吃那茂盛的葡萄叶子。</seg>
<seg id="1266">The movement drew the attention of the returning huntsmen, and one of them, supposing some animal to be hidden there, shot an arrow at a venture into the foliage.</seg>
<seg id="1266">这个动静吸引了猎人们的注意，他们马上掉回头来，其中一个人认为叶子底下一定躲着什么动物，一箭就射中了鹿。</seg>
<seg id="1267">The unlucky Stag was pierced to the heart, and, as he expired, he said, "I deserve my fate for my treachery in feeding upon the leaves of my protector."</seg>
<seg id="1267">不幸的鹿被箭刺穿了心脏，临死前说道：“我真是活该，因为我恩将仇报，吃了那曾经救过我一命的葡萄藤。”</seg>
<seg id="1268">Ingratitude sometimes brings its own punishment.</seg>
<seg id="1268">恩将仇报有时会受到更严重的惩罚。</seg>
<seg id="1269">THE LAMB CHASED BY A WOLF</seg>
<seg id="1269">被狼追赶的羊羔</seg>
<seg id="1270">A Wolf was chasing a Lamb, which took refuge in a temple.</seg>
<seg id="1270">一只狼正在追赶一只小羊，而羊逃进了一个神庙里。</seg>
<seg id="1271">The Wolf urged it to come out of the precincts, and said, "If you don't, the priest is sure to catch you and offer you up in sacrifice on the altar."</seg>
<seg id="1271">狼为了怂恿小羊出来，便说：“要是你不赶快出来，祭司就会抓住你，把你放到神坛上当祭祀品。”</seg>
<seg id="1272">To which the Lamb replied, "Thanks, I think I'll stay where I am:</seg>
<seg id="1272">小羊则回答说：“谢谢你，我会一直待在这里，</seg>
<seg id="1273">I'd rather be sacrificed any day than be eaten up by a Wolf."</seg>
<seg id="1273">宁愿有一天能成为祭祀品，也比被你吃掉好。”</seg>
<seg id="1274">THE ARCHER AND THE LION</seg>
<seg id="1274">射手和狮子</seg>
<seg id="1275">An Archer went up into the hills to get some sport with his bow, and all the animals fled at the sight of him with the exception of the Lion, who stayed behind and challenged him to fight.</seg>
<seg id="1275">从前，有一个神射手到山里去寻找猎物，森林里的野兽一见到他，全都逃得无影无踪，只有高傲的狮子依然待在原地，向他发出挑战。</seg>
<seg id="1276">But he shot an arrow at the Lion and hit him, and said, "There, you see what my messenger can do:</seg>
<seg id="1276">然而，射手冲狮子射出一箭，说：“这只是给你报个信，</seg>
<seg id="1277">just you wait a moment and I'll tackle you myself."</seg>
<seg id="1277">你等着吧，看看我怎么收拾你。”</seg>
<seg id="1278">The Lion, however, when he felt the sting of the arrow, ran away as fast as his legs could carry him.</seg>
<seg id="1278">狮子感觉到箭伤的疼痛后，竭力地快速逃走了。</seg>
<seg id="1279">A fox, who had seen it all happen, said to the Lion, "Come, don't be a coward:</seg>
<seg id="1279">一只在旁观看的狐狸对狮子说：“别做懦夫呀，</seg>
<seg id="1280">why don't you stay and show fight?"</seg>
<seg id="1280">为什么你不待在原地，展示一下你的斗志呢？”</seg>
<seg id="1281">But the Lion replied, "You won't get me to stay, not you:</seg>
<seg id="1281">可是狮子却回答说：“你可不能让我冒死呀，显示斗志的又不是你。</seg>
<seg id="1282">why, when he sends a messenger like that before him, he must himself be a terrible fellow to deal with."</seg>
<seg id="1282">为什么要跑，他射过来的一支箭都这么厉害，他本人肯定也不是一个好对付的家伙。”</seg>
<seg id="1283">Give a wide berth to those who can do damage at a distance.</seg>
<seg id="1283">要对那些从远处就具杀伤力的人敬而远之。</seg>
<seg id="1284">THE WOLF AND THE GOAT</seg>
<seg id="1284">狼和山羊</seg>
<seg id="1285">A Wolf caught sight of a Goat browsing above him on the scanty herbage that grew on the top of a steep rock; and being unable to get at her, tried to induce her to come lower down.</seg>
<seg id="1285">一只狼看见山羊在陡峭的山崖上啃着稀疏的草，自己根本无法捉到她，便怂恿她赶快下来。</seg>
<seg id="1286">"You are risking your life up there, madam, indeed you are," he called out:</seg>
<seg id="1286">“你站在那里会有生命危险的，女士，你太冒险了，”狼喊道，</seg>
<seg id="1287">"pray take my advice and come down here, where you will find plenty of better food."</seg>
<seg id="1287">“还是听我的话，快点下来吧，这里的草更嫩更多，足够你吃的了。”</seg>
<seg id="1288">The Goat turned a knowing eye upon him. "It's little you care whether I get good grass or bad," said she:</seg>
<seg id="1288">山羊带着精明的眼神看着狼，回答说：“你并非真关心我在吃什么样的草，</seg>
<seg id="1289">"what you want is to eat me."</seg>
<seg id="1289">你不过是想吃掉我而已。”</seg>
<seg id="1290">THE SICK STAG</seg>
<seg id="1290">病鹿</seg>
<seg id="1291">A Stag fell sick and lay in a clearing in the forest, too weak to move from the spot.</seg>
<seg id="1291">一只生了病的鹿躺在森林里的一片空地上，虚弱得无力挪动。</seg>
<seg id="1292">When the news of his illness spread, a number of the other beasts came to inquire after his health, and they one and all nibbled a little of the grass that grew round the invalid till at last there was not a blade within his reach.</seg>
<seg id="1292">鹿生病的消息四散开来，众多野兽纷纷前来探望，他们无一例外都会或多或少地吃一点鹿身边生长着的草。最后，在病鹿周围再也看不到一片小草了。</seg>
<seg id="1293">In a few days he began to mend, but was still too feeble to get up and go in search of fodder;</seg>
<seg id="1293">几天后，鹿的身体虽然开始复原了，但是依然十分虚弱，无法站起来出去找东西吃。</seg>
<seg id="1294">and thus he perished miserably of hunger owing to the thoughtlessness of his friends.</seg>
<seg id="1294">终于，他死了，但并非死于疾病，而是不幸地被饿死了，这都是因为朋友们的不体贴而造成的。</seg>
<seg id="1295">THE ASS AND THE MULE</seg>
<seg id="1295">驴和骡子</seg>
<seg id="1296">A certain man who had an Ass and a Mule loaded them both up one day and set out upon a journey.</seg>
<seg id="1296">某人有一头驴和一头骡子，有一天，他把货物分别放在驴和骡子的背上，就出远门了。</seg>
<seg id="1297">So long as the road was fairly level, the Ass got on very well:</seg>
<seg id="1297">只要在平地上走，驴还能应付，</seg>
<seg id="1298">but by and by they came to a place among the hills where the road was very rough and steep, and the Ass was at his last gasp.</seg>
<seg id="1298">但是一走到大山之间那崎岖不平的山路上，驴就上气不接下气了。</seg>
<seg id="1299">So he begged the Mule to relieve him of a part of his load: but the Mule refused.</seg>
<seg id="1299">于是，驴请求骡子替他分担一部分货物，可是，骡子却拒绝了。</seg>
<seg id="1300">At last, from sheer weariness, the Ass stumbled and fell down a steep place and was killed.</seg>
<seg id="1300">由于极度疲倦，驴一不小心从山上滚下去，摔死了。</seg>
<seg id="1301">The driver was in despair, but he did the best he could: he added the Ass's load to the Mule's, and he also flayed the Ass and put his skin on the top of the double load.</seg>
<seg id="1301">赶驴人非常沮丧，但也只能如此，他把驴身上驮的货物放在了骡子的背上，同时还割下了驴皮，一起放在货物顶上。</seg>
<seg id="1302">The Mule could only just manage the extra weight, and, as he staggered painfully along, he said to himself, "I have only got what I deserved:</seg>
<seg id="1302">骡子也只得忍气吞声默默承担着所有重量，他一边蹒跚着前进，一边自言自语：“我真是活该！</seg>
<seg id="1303">if I had been willing to help the Ass at first, I should not now be carrying his load and his skin into the bargain."</seg>
<seg id="1303">如果我一开始就愿意帮助驴分担重量的话，现在也就不会既驮着本该在他背上的货物，又驮着他的皮了。”</seg>
<seg id="1304">BROTHER AND SISTER</seg>
<seg id="1304">哥哥和妹妹</seg>
<seg id="1305">A certain man had two children, a boy and a girl:</seg>
<seg id="1305">某人有两个孩子，一个儿子和一个女儿。</seg>
<seg id="1306">and the boy was as good-looking as the girl was plain.</seg>
<seg id="1306">儿子长相英俊，而女儿却相貌平平。</seg>
<seg id="1307">One day, as they were playing together in their mother's chamber, they chanced upon a mirror and saw their own features for the first time.</seg>
<seg id="1307">有一天，兄妹俩在妈妈的房间里玩，偶然走到镜子前，第一次看见了自己的真实面目。</seg>
<seg id="1308">The boy saw what a handsome fellow he was, and began to boast to his Sister about his good looks:</seg>
<seg id="1308">哥哥看到自己是个英俊的小伙子，就开始向妹妹鼓吹自己的相貌；</seg>
<seg id="1309">she, on her part, was ready to cry with vexation when she was aware of her plainness, and took his remarks as an insult to herself.</seg>
<seg id="1309">从妹妹的角度来说，她一看到自己相貌平平，都快要哭出来了，就把哥哥的自夸当成了对自己的嘲笑。</seg>
<seg id="1310">Running to her father, she told him of her Brother's conceit, and accused him of meddling with his mother's things.</seg>
<seg id="1310">她便跑到父亲跟前，抱怨说哥哥太自负了，而且还乱动妈妈的东西。</seg>
<seg id="1311">He laughed and kissed them both, and said, "My children, learn from now onwards to make a good use of the glass.</seg>
<seg id="1311">父亲笑着亲吻了两个孩子，并说：“我的好孩子，今后你们可要好好利用这个镜子。</seg>
<seg id="1312">You, my boy, strive to be as good as it shows you to be handsome;</seg>
<seg id="1312">我的儿子，你可要像自己的英俊相貌一样努力出众；</seg>
<seg id="1313">and you, my girl, resolve to make up for the plainness of your features by the sweetness of your disposition."</seg>
<seg id="1313">我的女儿，可以用你的美德来弥补相貌上的不足。”</seg>
<seg id="1314">THE HEIFER AND THE OX</seg>
<seg id="1314">小母牛和公牛</seg>
<seg id="1315">A Heifer went up to an Ox, who was straining hard at the plough, and sympathised with him in a rather patronising sort of way on the necessity of his having to work so hard.</seg>
<seg id="1315">一头小母牛走到一头公牛跟前，看见公牛在辛苦地耕田，便以一种居高临下的方式悲叹公牛天生劳苦的可怜命运。</seg>
<seg id="1316">Not long afterwards there was a festival in the village and every one kept holiday:</seg>
<seg id="1316">不久，村子里要举行节日庆祝仪式，所有的人和动物都放假了。</seg>
<seg id="1317">but, whereas the Ox was turned loose into the pasture, the Heifer was seized and led off to sacrifice.</seg>
<seg id="1317">可是，就在公牛被放逐到牧场吃草时，小母牛却被抓去充当祭祀品。</seg>
<seg id="1318">"Ah," said the Ox, with a grim smile, "I see now why you were allowed to have such an idle time:</seg>
<seg id="1318">这时，公牛冷笑道：“喂，现在我知道你为何这么悠闲自得了，</seg>
<seg id="1319">it was because you were always intended for the altar."</seg>
<seg id="1319">因为你天生就要去当祭祀品。”</seg>
<seg id="1320">THE KINGDOM OF THE LION</seg>
<seg id="1320">狮子的王国</seg>
<seg id="1321">When the Lion reigned over the beasts of the earth he was never cruel or tyrannical, but as gentle and just as a King ought to be.</seg>
<seg id="1321">狮子自从统治了地球上的百兽之后，从未施行过任何凶暴、残忍的手段，而是像国王应有的那样公正、仁慈。</seg>
<seg id="1322">During his reign he called a general assembly of the beasts, and drew up a code of laws under which all were to live in perfect equality and harmony:</seg>
<seg id="1322">在统治百兽期间，他曾经召集所有的动物开大会，拟订一个大家都应遵守的法规，便于让动物们公平、和谐地相处。</seg>
<seg id="1323">the wolf and the lamb, the tiger and the stag, the leopard and the kid, the dog and the hare, all should dwell side by side in unbroken peace and friendship.</seg>
<seg id="1323">狼和羊，老虎和鹿，豹子和小山羊，狗和野兔等，大家都应该按照规定友好和睦地相处。</seg>
<seg id="1324">The hare said, "Oh! how I have longed for this day when the weak take their place without fear by the side of the strong!"</seg>
<seg id="1324">兔子说：“哦！这一天，我期盼已久了！这样一来，弱者再也不用惧怕强者了，终于有了自己的一席之地。”</seg>
<seg id="1325">THE ASS AND HIS DRIVER</seg>
<seg id="1325">驴和赶驴人</seg>
<seg id="1326">An Ass was being driven down a mountain road, and after jogging along for a while sensibly enough he suddenly quitted the track and rushed to the edge of a precipice.</seg>
<seg id="1326">某人赶着驴走在下山的路上，一阵小跑之后，驴突然离开大道，冲到了悬崖边。</seg>
<seg id="1327">He was just about to leap over the edge when his Driver caught hold of his tail and did his best to pull him back:</seg>
<seg id="1327">就在驴即将滑下悬崖时，赶驴的人一把抓住他的尾巴，用劲往回拉。</seg>
<seg id="1328">but pull as he might he couldn't get the Ass to budge from the brink.</seg>
<seg id="1328">可是，无论如何也无法将驴从悬崖边拉上来。</seg>
<seg id="1329">At last he gave up, crying, "All right, then, get to the bottom your own way;</seg>
<seg id="1329">最后，赶驴的人放弃了，说道：“好吧，随你去吧，你愿意掉下悬崖，就掉吧，</seg>
<seg id="1330">but it's the way to sudden death, as you'll find out quick enough."</seg>
<seg id="1330">很快你就会发现，这是一条通向死亡的路。”</seg>
<seg id="1331">THE LION AND THE HARE</seg>
<seg id="1331">狮子和野兔</seg>
<seg id="1332">A Lion found a Hare sleeping in her form, and was just going to devour her when he caught sight of a passing stag.</seg>
<seg id="1332">一只狮子发现一只兔子正在窝里睡觉，便想趁机吃掉她。</seg>
<seg id="1333">Dropping the Hare, he at once made for the bigger game;</seg>
<seg id="1333">这时，他又看见旁边有一只鹿经过。狮子立刻丢下兔子，去追赶个头更大的鹿。</seg>
<seg id="1334">but finding, after a long chase, that he could not overtake the stag, he abandoned the attempt and came back for the Hare.</seg>
<seg id="1334">然而，追了一阵子后，狮子发现根本追不上鹿，于是就放弃了目标，又回过头来找兔子。</seg>
<seg id="1335">When he reached the spot, however, he found she was nowhere to be seen, and he had to go without his dinner.</seg>
<seg id="1335">可是，等他回到兔窝时，却发现兔子早已逃之夭夭。这下，他的晚餐全都泡汤了。</seg>
<seg id="1336">"It serves me right," he said; "I should have been content with what I had got, instead of hankering after a better prize."</seg>
<seg id="1336">狮子说：“我真活该！我应该满足于唾手可得的东西，而不应贪心去追求更大的奖励。”</seg>
<seg id="1337">THE WOLVES AND THE DOGS</seg>
<seg id="1337">一群狼和一群狗</seg>
<seg id="1338">Once upon a time the Wolves said to the Dogs, "Why should we continue to be enemies any longer?</seg>
<seg id="1338">从前，有一群狼对一群狗说：“为什么我们要一直成为敌人呢？</seg>
<seg id="1339">You are very like us in most ways:</seg>
<seg id="1339">从各方面来看，你们和我们都很相像，</seg>
<seg id="1340">the main difference between us is one of training only.</seg>
<seg id="1340">咱们之间唯一的区别仅仅是受驯不同而已。</seg>
<seg id="1341">We live a life of freedom; but you are enslaved to mankind, who beat you, and put heavy collars round your necks, and compel you to keep watch over their flocks and herds for them, and, to crown all, they give you nothing but bones to eat.</seg>
<seg id="1341">我们过着自由自在的日子，而你们却成了人类的奴隶，他们不仅鞭打你们，还给你们套上沉重的颈圈，迫使你们去看守羊群和牲畜。总而言之，除了让你们啃骨头之外，人类什么也没给你们。</seg>
<seg id="1342">Don't put up with it any longer, but hand over the flocks to us, and we will all live on the fat of the land and feast together."</seg>
<seg id="1342">别再忍受他们的折磨了，直接把羊群交给我们，我们一起到肥沃的草场里生活吧，我们一起去享受。”</seg>
<seg id="1343">The Dogs allowed themselves to be persuaded by these words, and accompanied the Wolves into their den.</seg>
<seg id="1343">那群狗被狼的一番话说动了心，跟随狼群来到他们的窝里。</seg>
<seg id="1344">But no sooner were they well inside than the Wolves set upon them and tore them to pieces.</seg>
<seg id="1344">结果，刚一进去，狼群就向狗群发起进攻，杀得他们片甲不留。</seg>
<seg id="1345">Traitors richly deserve their fate.</seg>
<seg id="1345">背叛者通常都没有好下场。</seg>
<seg id="1346">THE BULL AND THE CALF</seg>
<seg id="1346">公牛和小牛</seg>
<seg id="1347">A full-grown Bull was struggling to force his huge bulk through the narrow entrance to a cow-house where his stall was, when a young Calf came up and said to him, "If you'll step aside a moment, I'll show you the way to get through."</seg>
<seg id="1347">一头公牛竭尽全力要挤过一道窄门到牛棚里去，他的牛栏就在棚里。这时，一头小牛犊走了过来，对公牛说：“如果你能闪到一边去，我就告诉你怎么过去。”</seg>
<seg id="1348">The Bull turned upon him an amused look. "I knew that way," said he, "before you were born."</seg>
<seg id="1348">公牛开心地看了他一眼，说：“你还没出世之前，我就早已知道那个办法了。”</seg>
<seg id="1349">THE TREES AND THE AXE</seg>
<seg id="1349">树和斧头</seg>
<seg id="1350">A Woodman went into the forest and begged of the Trees the favour of a handle for his Axe.</seg>
<seg id="1350">一个樵夫走进森林里，请求树给他一根木头做斧柄。</seg>
<seg id="1351">The principal Trees at once agreed to so modest a request, and unhesitatingly gave him a young ash sapling, out of which he fashioned the handle he desired.</seg>
<seg id="1351">树的首领马上就答应了樵夫那温和谦逊的请求，毫不犹豫地给了他一根小树枝。樵夫用小树枝做成了自己想要的斧柄。</seg>
<seg id="1352">No sooner had he done so than he set to work to fell the noblest Trees in the wood.</seg>
<seg id="1352">刚一完成这个任务，他接着就在森林里用斧头砍起其中最贵重的一棵大树。</seg>
<seg id="1353">When they saw the use to which he was putting their gift, they cried, "Alas! alas!</seg>
<seg id="1353">当树看到樵夫用的正是自己给他的礼物时，说：“哎呀，哎呀！</seg>
<seg id="1354">We are undone, but we are ourselves to blame.</seg>
<seg id="1354">我们是自己葬送了自己。</seg>
<seg id="1355">The little we gave has cost us all:</seg>
<seg id="1355">给他的那一根小树枝，竟然葬送了我们大家的命。</seg>
<seg id="1356">had we not sacrificed the rights of the ash, we might ourselves have stood for ages."</seg>
<seg id="1356">要是我们没给它，也许我们还能在这里多站几年。”</seg>
<seg id="1357">THE ASTRONOMER</seg>
<seg id="1357">天文学家</seg>
<seg id="1358">There was once an Astronomer whose habit it was to go out at night and observe the stars.</seg>
<seg id="1358">有一个天文学家养成了晚上出去观察星象的习惯。</seg>
<seg id="1359">One night, as he was walking about outside the town gates, gazing up absorbed into the sky and not looking where he was going, he fell into a dry well.</seg>
<seg id="1359">有一个夜晚，当他走出城门来到郊外后，便聚精会神地观察着天空，一不小心掉进一口枯井里。</seg>
<seg id="1360">As he lay there groaning, some one passing by heard him, and, coming to the edge of the well, looked down and, on learning what had happened, said, "If you really mean to say that you were looking so hard at the sky that you didn't even see where your feet were carrying you along the ground, it appears to me that you deserve all you've got."</seg>
<seg id="1360">当他正坐在井里呻吟时，一个刚好从旁经过的人听到了，便走到井边向下看，待了解了事情经过后，对他说：“如果真如你所说，只是一味地努力向上看，而没有看清楚脚下的路况，那么在我看来，你就活该待在这里。”</seg>
<seg id="1361">THE LABOURER AND THE SNAKE</seg>
<seg id="1361">工人和蛇</seg>
<seg id="1362">A Labourer's little son was bitten by a Snake and died of the wound.</seg>
<seg id="1362">工人的小儿子被一条毒蛇咬了一口，并且死于蛇伤。</seg>
<seg id="1363">The father was beside himself with grief, and in his anger against the Snake he caught up an axe and went and stood close to the Snake's hole, and watched for a chance of killing it.</seg>
<seg id="1363">悲痛气愤之余，工人抓起一把斧头，气冲冲地跑到蛇洞外，等待机会砍死蛇。</seg>
<seg id="1364">Presently the Snake came out, and the man aimed a blow at it, but only succeeded in cutting off the tip of its tail before it wriggled in again.</seg>
<seg id="1364">不久，蛇从洞里出来了，工人立即一斧头砍过去，可是只砍断了它的尾巴尖。</seg>
<seg id="1365">He then tried to get it to come out a second time, pretending that he wished to make up the quarrel.</seg>
<seg id="1365">随后，工人还想再如法炮制，便假装想与蛇和解。</seg>
<seg id="1366">But the Snake said, "I can never be your friend because of my lost tail, nor you mine because of your lost child."</seg>
<seg id="1366">可是，蛇却说：“我永远也无法成为你的朋友，因为我丢了自己的尾巴，而你却丢失了儿子。”</seg>
<seg id="1367">Injuries are never forgotten in the presence of those who caused them.</seg>
<seg id="1367">在造成创伤的双方心里，永远无法忘却伤痛。</seg>
<seg id="1368">THE CAGE-BIRD AND THE BAT</seg>
<seg id="1368">笼子里的鸟与蝙蝠</seg>
<seg id="1369">A Singing-bird was confined in a cage which hung outside a window, and had a way of singing at night when all other birds were asleep.</seg>
<seg id="1369">一只画眉鸟被囚禁在窗外挂着的一个笼子里，当其他鸟儿都酣睡时，她却在夜里歌唱。</seg>
<seg id="1370">One night a Bat came and clung to the bars of the cage, and asked the Bird why she was silent by day and sang only at night.</seg>
<seg id="1370">有一个夜晚，蝙蝠飞过来，抓住鸟笼的栅栏，问她为什么白天默默无声，却在夜间放声歌唱。</seg>
<seg id="1371">"I have a very good reason for doing so," said the Bird:</seg>
<seg id="1371">小鸟回答说：“我这样做是有道理的，</seg>
<seg id="1372">"it was once when I was singing in the daytime that a fowler was attracted by my voice, and set his nets for me and caught me.</seg>
<seg id="1372">曾经有一次，当我在白天唱歌时，一个捕鸟人被我的歌声吸引，就用鸟笼子捉住了我。</seg>
<seg id="1373">Since then I have never sung except by night."</seg>
<seg id="1373">从此我只在夜里唱歌。”</seg>
<seg id="1374">But the Bat replied, "It is no use your doing that now when you are a prisoner:</seg>
<seg id="1374">可是，蝙蝠却说：“你现在这样做根本没用了，因为你已经成为了阶下囚。</seg>
<seg id="1375">if only you had done so before you were caught, you might still have been free."</seg>
<seg id="1375">若是在被捉住之前这样做就好了，那样或许你依然是自由之身！”</seg>
<seg id="1376">Precautions are useless after the event.</seg>
<seg id="1376">待事件发生之后再预防，为时已晚。</seg>
<seg id="1377">THE ASS AND HIS PURCHASER</seg>
<seg id="1377">驴和他的买主</seg>
<seg id="1378">A Man who wanted to buy an Ass went to market, and, coming across a likely-looking beast, arranged with the owner that he should be allowed to take him home on trial to see what he was like.</seg>
<seg id="1378">有个人想买一头驴，于是，他来到市场里。有一群貌似一样的畜生被主人牵着向他走来，他提出应该将驴牵回家，好检验一下驴的状况。</seg>
<seg id="1379">When he reached home, he put him into his stable along with the other asses.</seg>
<seg id="1379">回到家后，他把驴安置在马棚里，里面还混杂着其他牲口。</seg>
<seg id="1380">The newcomer took a look round, and immediately went and chose a place next to the laziest and greediest beast in the stable.</seg>
<seg id="1380">驴环视了一下四周，立刻来到马棚里一头好吃懒做的驴旁边。</seg>
<seg id="1381">When the master saw this he put a halter on him at once, and led him off and handed him over to his owner again.</seg>
<seg id="1381">主人见此，立刻给那头驴套上辔头，牵去还给驴的卖主。</seg>
<seg id="1382">The latter was a good deal surprised to see him back so soon, and said, "Why, do you mean to say you have tested him already?"</seg>
<seg id="1382">看到他们这么快就回来了，卖主很惊讶，就说：“为什么回来了？</seg>
<seg id="1383">"I don't want to put him through any more tests," replied the other:</seg>
<seg id="1383">你已经检验过它了？”那人答道：</seg>
<seg id="1384">"I could see what sort of beast he is from the companion he chose for himself."</seg>
<seg id="1384">“我可不想再做什么检验了，从它选择的同伴来看，我就已经知道它是什么样的牲口了。”</seg>
<seg id="1385">A man is known by the company he keeps.</seg>
<seg id="1385">物以类聚，人以群分。</seg>
<seg id="1386">THE KID AND THE WOLF</seg>
<seg id="1386">小山羊和狼</seg>
<seg id="1387">A Kid strayed from the flock and was chased by a Wolf.</seg>
<seg id="1387">一只从羊群里掉队的小山羊，被狼所追赶。</seg>
<seg id="1388">When he saw he must be caught he turned round and said to the Wolf, "I know, sir, that I can't escape being eaten by you:</seg>
<seg id="1388">当小山羊感觉自己就快被抓住了时，他回过头来，对狼说：“狼啊，我知道逃不掉了，很快就会成为你的盘中餐，</seg>
<seg id="1389">and so, as my life is bound to be short, I pray you let it be as merry as may be.</seg>
<seg id="1389">因为我的生命很短暂，求求你让我尽可能地灿烂一回吧。</seg>
<seg id="1390">Will you not play me a tune to dance to before I die?"</seg>
<seg id="1390">你能在我死之前吹一曲，让我跳一次舞吗？”</seg>
<seg id="1391">The Wolf saw no objection to having some music before his dinner:</seg>
<seg id="1391">狼心想在晚餐前听一支曲子也不错，</seg>
<seg id="1392">so he took out his pipe and began to play, while the Kid danced before him.</seg>
<seg id="1392">于是，他拿出自己的笛子来，开始吹奏，而小山羊则在他面前跳起舞来。</seg>
<seg id="1393">Before many minutes were passed the gods who guarded the flock heard the sound and came up to see what was going on.</seg>
<seg id="1393">还没过几分钟，守护羊群的牧羊犬闻声而至，想探个究竟。</seg>
<seg id="1394">They no sooner clapped eyes on the Wolf than they gave chase and drove him away.</seg>
<seg id="1394">牧羊犬一看到狼，便马上赶走了他。</seg>
<seg id="1395">As he ran off, he turned and said to the Kid, "It's what I thoroughly deserve:</seg>
<seg id="1395">狼一边跑，一边回过头来对小山羊说：“我真活该，</seg>
<seg id="1396">my trade is the butcher's, and I had no business to turn piper to please you."</seg>
<seg id="1396">我本该杀了你，根本没有义务为你吹笛子取悦你呀。”</seg>
<seg id="1397">THE DEBTOR AND HIS SOW</seg>
<seg id="1397">欠债人和母猪</seg>
<seg id="1398">A Man of Athens fell into debt and was pressed for the money by his creditor;</seg>
<seg id="1398">一个雅典人欠了别人的钱，债主三番五次来催他还钱，但他当时根本没有办法还钱，所以请求延期几天。</seg>
<seg id="1399">but he had no means of paying at the time, so he begged for delay.</seg>
<seg id="1399">可是，债主却不答应，让他立刻还钱。</seg>
<seg id="1400">But the creditor refused and said he must pay at once.</seg>
<seg id="1400">迫不得已，欠债人把家中仅有的母猪带到市场上去卖。</seg>
<seg id="1401">Then the Debtor fetched a Sow--the only one he had--and took her to market to offer her for sale.</seg>
<seg id="1401">碰巧，债主也在那个市场里。</seg>
<seg id="1402">It happened that his creditor was there too.</seg>
<seg id="1402">过了一会儿，有一个买主走上前来，问这头猪是否还能下小猪崽。</seg>
<seg id="1403">"Yes," said the Debtor, "very fine ones;</seg>
<seg id="1403">“当然了，”欠债人回答说，“能生下很好的小猪崽，</seg>
<seg id="1404">and the remarkable thing is that she produces females at the Mysteries and males at the Panathenea."</seg>
<seg id="1404">而且更惊人的是，她还能在女神节生下小母猪，在帕纳西尼亚节生下小公猪。”</seg>
<seg id="1405">(Festivals these were: and the Athenians always sacrifice a sow at one, and a boar at the other;</seg>
<seg id="1405">（这是希腊的两个节日，雅典人总是在女神节杀一只小母猪祭祀，在帕纳西尼亚节杀一只小公猪祭祀，</seg>
<seg id="1406">while at the Dionysia they sacrifice a kid.)</seg>
<seg id="1406">而在狂欢节杀一只小山羊做祭祀品。）</seg>
<seg id="1407">At that the creditor, who was standing by, put in, "Don't be surprised, sir;</seg>
<seg id="1407">债主听到他说的话，立刻站出来插话道：“一点都不奇怪，先生，</seg>
<seg id="1408">why, still better, at the Dionysia this Sow has kids!"</seg>
<seg id="1408">为什么呢，因为更厉害的是，在狂欢节时，她还会生下小山羊呢！”</seg>
<seg id="1409">THE BALD HUNTSMAN</seg>
<seg id="1409">秃头的猎人</seg>
<seg id="1410">A Man who had lost all his hair took to wearing a wig, and one day he went out hunting.</seg>
<seg id="1410">有一个人因为所有的头发都掉光了，便戴上了一顶假发。有一天，他出去打猎。</seg>
<seg id="1411">It was blowing rather hard at the time, and he hadn't gone far before a gust of wind caught his hat and carried it off, and his wig too, much to the amusement of the hunt.</seg>
<seg id="1411">突然，一阵狂风吹来，把他头上的帽子和假发一起吹跑了，此事成了狩猎活动中的一大乐事。</seg>
<seg id="1412">But he quite entered into the joke, and said, "Ah, well! the hair that wig is made of didn't stick to the head on which it grew;</seg>
<seg id="1412">然而，他本人说出来的话就更加可笑了：“哈哈，好吧，制成这顶假发的那些头发，早已不能固定在原主人的头上了，</seg>
<seg id="1413">so it's no wonder it won't stick to mine."</seg>
<seg id="1413">所以毫无疑问，它们也无法粘在我的头上。”</seg>
<seg id="1414">THE HERDSMAN AND THE LOST BULL</seg>
<seg id="1414">牧人和丢失的公牛</seg>
<seg id="1415">A Herdsman was tending his cattle when he missed a young Bull, one of the finest of the herd.</seg>
<seg id="1415">一个牧人在给牛喂草时发现丢了一头小公牛，那可是其中最好的一头牛。</seg>
<seg id="1416">He went at once to look for him, but, meeting with no success in his search, he made a vow that, if he should discover the thief, he would sacrifice a calf to Jupiter.</seg>
<seg id="1416">他立刻出去找牛，可是哪里都找不到，便发下誓言，只要让他发现偷牛的贼，他就会杀一头小牛供奉朱庇特。</seg>
<seg id="1417">Continuing his search, he entered a thicket, where he presently espied a lion devouring the lost Bull.</seg>
<seg id="1417">牧人继续去找他的牛，走着走着来到了一个灌木丛中，他忽然看见一只狮子正在津津有味地吃着那头丢失了的小公牛。</seg>
<seg id="1418">Terrified with fear, he raised his hands to heaven and cried, "Great Jupiter, I vowed I would sacrifice a calf to thee if I should discover the thief:</seg>
<seg id="1418">他吓呆了，立刻举起双手向上天祈求说：“伟大的朱庇特，刚才我曾立誓，如果捉到贼，愿意献上一头小牛供奉你；</seg>
<seg id="1419">but now a full-grown Bull I promise thee if only I myself escape unhurt from his clutches."</seg>
<seg id="1419">但是现在，如果我可以安全地脱离狮口，我愿意再奉献一头成熟强壮的牛。”</seg>
<seg id="1420">THE MULE</seg>
<seg id="1420">骡子</seg>
<seg id="1421">One morning a Mule, who had too much to eat and too little to do, began to think himself a very fine fellow indeed, and frisked about saying, "My father was undoubtedly a high-spirited horse and I take after him entirely."</seg>
<seg id="1421">一天清晨，一匹衣食无忧、悠闲自在的骡子，认为自己天生好命，便高兴地自言自语道：“我的父亲一定是一匹能奔善跑的马，我非常像他。”</seg>
<seg id="1422">But very soon afterwards he was put into the harness and compelled to go a very long way with a heavy load behind him.</seg>
<seg id="1422">然而，话音刚落，他就被套上马具，驮着沉重的货物上路了。</seg>
<seg id="1423">At the end of the day, exhausted by his unusual exertions, he said dejectedly to himself, "I must have been mistaken about my father;</seg>
<seg id="1423">一天下来，骡子已被那不同寻常的工作累垮了，他愁眉苦脸地说：“关于父亲的出身，我可能想错了，</seg>
<seg id="1424">he can only have been an ass after all."</seg>
<seg id="1424">他不过是一头苦命的驴而已。”</seg>
<seg id="1425">THE HOUND AND THE FOX</seg>
<seg id="1425">猎狗和狐狸</seg>
<seg id="1426">A Hound, roaming in the forest, spied a lion, and being well used to lesser game, gave chase, thinking he would make a fine quarry.</seg>
<seg id="1426">有一条猎狗，正在森林里闲逛，猛然看见一只狮子，心想这可是一个不错的猎物，便追了上去，想施展一下自己的小伎俩。</seg>
<seg id="1427">Presently the lion perceived that he was being pursued;</seg>
<seg id="1427">很快，狮子觉察到自己被追踪了，</seg>
<seg id="1428">so, stopping short, he rounded on his pursuer and gave a loud roar.</seg>
<seg id="1428">便突然停住，回过头来冲着追捕者大声吼叫。</seg>
<seg id="1429">The Hound immediately turned tail and fled.</seg>
<seg id="1429">猎狗立刻转身逃跑了。</seg>
<seg id="1430">A Fox, seeing him running away, jeered at him and said, "Ho! ho!</seg>
<seg id="1430">一只狐狸见状，便嘲笑起猎狗：“呵呵，</seg>
<seg id="1431">There goes the coward who chased a lion and ran away the moment he roared!"</seg>
<seg id="1431">真是个胆小鬼，竟然还敢追狮子，只要狮子一声吼，你可就落荒而逃了！”</seg>
<seg id="1432">THE FATHER AND HIS DAUGHTERS</seg>
<seg id="1432">父亲和他的女儿</seg>
<seg id="1433">A Man had two Daughters, one of whom he gave in marriage to a gardener, and the other to a potter.</seg>
<seg id="1433">某人有两个女儿，一个嫁给了园丁，另一个嫁给了陶艺人。</seg>
<seg id="1434">After a time he thought he would go and see how they were getting on;</seg>
<seg id="1434">过了些日子，父亲心想应该去看看女儿们的生活如何。</seg>
<seg id="1435">and first he went to the gardener's wife.</seg>
<seg id="1435">于是，他先来到嫁给园丁的女儿家里，</seg>
<seg id="1436">He asked her how she was, and how things were going with herself and her husband.</seg>
<seg id="1436">他问女儿生活过得怎么样，她的丈夫又过得怎么样。</seg>
<seg id="1437">She replied that on the whole they were doing very well:</seg>
<seg id="1437">女儿回答说一切都很好，</seg>
<seg id="1438">"But," she continued, "I do wish we could have some good heavy rain:</seg>
<seg id="1438">“但是，”她又补充道，“我真希望能下场大雨，</seg>
<seg id="1439">the garden wants it badly."</seg>
<seg id="1439">园子里太需要水了。”</seg>
<seg id="1440">Then he went on to the potter's wife and made the same inquiries of her.</seg>
<seg id="1440">接着，他又来到嫁给陶艺人的女儿家里，问了同样的问题。</seg>
<seg id="1441">She replied that she and her husband had nothing to complain of:</seg>
<seg id="1441">女儿说她和丈夫什么都不缺，</seg>
<seg id="1442">"But," she went on, "I do wish we could have some nice dry weather, to dry the pottery."</seg>
<seg id="1442">“可是，”她继续说，“我只希望能有个阳光充足的好天气，好让陶器快点干。”</seg>
<seg id="1443">Her Father looked at her with a humorous expression on his face.</seg>
<seg id="1443">父亲带着滑稽的表情看着女儿，</seg>
<seg id="1444">"You want dry weather," he said, "and your sister wants rain.</seg>
<seg id="1444">对她说：“你希望出太阳，而你的姐姐却盼着下雨，</seg>
<seg id="1445">I was going to ask in my prayers that your wishes should be granted;</seg>
<seg id="1445">我本想祈祷让你的愿望也成真，</seg>
<seg id="1446">but now it strikes me I had better not refer to the subject."</seg>
<seg id="1446">可是现在，我认为自己最好什么也不管了。”</seg>
<seg id="1447">THE THIEF AND THE INNKEEPER</seg>
<seg id="1447">小偷和店主</seg>
<seg id="1448">A Thief hired a room at an inn, and stayed there some days on the look-out for something to steal.</seg>
<seg id="1448">一个小偷在旅馆里租了一间房，一连住了好几天，想要偷一点东西。</seg>
<seg id="1449">No opportunity, however, presented itself, till one day, when there was a festival to be celebrated, the Innkeeper appeared in a fine new coat and sat down before the door of the inn for an airing.</seg>
<seg id="1449">可是，一直没找到机会。直到有一天，人们要庆祝某个节日，老板穿着一件漂亮的新衣坐在门口透气。</seg>
<seg id="1450">The Thief no sooner set eyes upon the coat than he longed to get possession of it.</seg>
<seg id="1450">小偷很快就盯上了那件新衣服，想据为己有。</seg>
<seg id="1451">There was no business doing, so he went and took a seat by the side of the Innkeeper, and began talking to him.</seg>
<seg id="1451">店里也没有什么生意，小偷便走过去坐在老板旁边，与他闲谈起来。</seg>
<seg id="1452">They conversed together for some time, and then the Thief suddenly yawned and howled like a wolf.</seg>
<seg id="1452">聊了一会儿，小偷突然打了一个呵欠，并像狼似的大吼了一声。</seg>
<seg id="1453">The Innkeeper asked him in some concern what ailed him.</seg>
<seg id="1453">旅馆老板关切地问他这是怎么了。</seg>
<seg id="1454">The Thief replied, "I will tell you about myself, sir, but first I must beg you to take charge of my clothes for me, for I intend to leave them with you.</seg>
<seg id="1454">小偷回答说：“我会告诉你有关我的事情，但是首先，请你负责照看一下我的衣服，因为我想把这些都留给你。</seg>
<seg id="1455">Why I have these fits of yawning I cannot tell:</seg>
<seg id="1455">我自己也不知道为什么要这样打呵欠，</seg>
<seg id="1456">maybe they are sent as a punishment for my misdeeds;</seg>
<seg id="1456">可能是对过去所犯恶行的一种惩罚吧。</seg>
<seg id="1457">but, whatever the reason, the facts are that when I have yawned three times I become a ravening wolf and fly at men's throats."</seg>
<seg id="1457">不过，无论是什么原因，实际上，等我第三次打呵欠时，就会变成一只狼，扑向人的喉咙。”</seg>
<seg id="1458">As he finished speaking he yawned a second time and howled again as before.</seg>
<seg id="1458">说完之后，他又打了第二个呵欠，接着就像第一次一样大吼了一声。</seg>
<seg id="1459">The Innkeeper, believing every word he said, and terrified at the prospect of being confronted with a wolf, got up hastily and started to run indoors;</seg>
<seg id="1459">旅馆老板完全信以为真，一想到即将要面对一只狼，心里就很害怕。他立刻站起身来，准备夺门而逃。</seg>
<seg id="1460">but the Thief caught him by the coat and tried to stop him, crying, "Stay, sir, stay, and take charge of my clothes, or else I shall never see them again."</seg>
<seg id="1460">小偷扯住他的外衣，想留下他，并说：“先生，请等一等，拿走我的衣服吧，不然我再也看不到它们了。”</seg>
<seg id="1461">As he spoke he opened his mouth and began to yawn for the third time.</seg>
<seg id="1461">刚一说完，他又张开嘴，准备打第三个呵欠。</seg>
<seg id="1462">The Innkeeper, mad with the fear of being eaten by a wolf, slipped out of his coat, which remained in the other's hands, and bolted into the inn and locked the door behind him;</seg>
<seg id="1462">旅馆老板快被吓疯了，便赶紧从被小偷抓住的外套里溜出来，逃进旅馆里并锁上了门，</seg>
<seg id="1463">and the Thief then quietly stole off with his spoil.</seg>
<seg id="1463">而小偷则带着他夺来的战利品悄悄地溜走了。</seg>
<seg id="1464">THE PACK-ASS AND THE WILD ASS</seg>
<seg id="1464">家驴和野驴</seg>
<seg id="1465">A Wild Ass, who was wandering idly about, one day came upon a Pack-Ass lying at full length in a sunny spot and thoroughly enjoying himself.</seg>
<seg id="1465">有一天，一头无所事事的野驴，看见一头家驴正舒适地躺在阳光充足的地方自娱自乐。</seg>
<seg id="1466">Going up to him, he said, "What a lucky beast you are!</seg>
<seg id="1466">他走了过去，说：“你可真幸运呀！</seg>
<seg id="1467">Your sleek coat shows how well you live:</seg>
<seg id="1467">从你那光滑的皮肤就能看出来，你的日子过得很舒服呀，</seg>
<seg id="1468">how I envy you!"</seg>
<seg id="1468">我真羡慕你！”</seg>
<seg id="1469">Not long after the Wild Ass saw his acquaintance again, but this time he was carrying a heavy load, and his driver was following behind and beating him with a thick stick.</seg>
<seg id="1469">不久，野驴又看见家驴驮着沉重的货物，驴夫还跟在后面不停地用鞭子抽打他，</seg>
<seg id="1470">"Ah, my friend," said the Wild Ass, "I don't envy you any more:</seg>
<seg id="1470">这一次，野驴说：“我的朋友，我不再羡慕你了，</seg>
<seg id="1471">for I see you pay dear for your comforts."</seg>
<seg id="1471">因为我知道你付出了惨痛的代价。”</seg>
<seg id="1472">Advantages that are dearly bought are doubtful blessings.</seg>
<seg id="1472">用昂贵代价换来的优势是令人怀疑的福气。</seg>
<seg id="1473">THE ASS AND HIS MASTERS</seg>
<seg id="1473">驴和他的主人们</seg>
<seg id="1474">A Gardener had an Ass which had a very hard time of it, what with scanty food, heavy loads, and constant beating.</seg>
<seg id="1474">有一头生活在园丁家里的驴，过着艰辛的日子，不仅吃得少、干得多，还经常挨主人的鞭打。</seg>
<seg id="1475">The Ass therefore begged Jupiter to take him away from the Gardener and hand him over to another master.</seg>
<seg id="1475">于是，驴请求朱庇特让他离开园丁，换另外一个主人。</seg>
<seg id="1476">So Jupiter sent Mercury to the Gardener to bid him sell the Ass to a Potter, which he did.</seg>
<seg id="1476">于是朱庇特派墨丘利去找园丁，让他把驴卖给一个陶艺工人，园丁照做了。</seg>
<seg id="1477">But the Ass was as discontented as ever, for he had to work harder than before:</seg>
<seg id="1477">然而，驴仍然像以前一样不满足，因为他现在过得比以前还辛苦。</seg>
<seg id="1478">so he begged Jupiter for relief a second time, and Jupiter very obligingly arranged that he should be sold to a Tanner.</seg>
<seg id="1478">于是，他又请求朱庇特让自己离开第二个主人，再换另外一个。朱庇特又安排第二个主人把他卖给一个皮匠。</seg>
<seg id="1479">But when the Ass saw what his new master's trade was, he cried in despair, "Why wasn't I content to serve either of my former masters, hard as I had to work and badly as I was treated?</seg>
<seg id="1479">可是，当驴一看到新主人的生意，就绝望地哭起来：“为什么我总对以前的主人不满意呀！为什么不满足于自己的辛苦工作和微薄待遇呀？</seg>
<seg id="1480">for they would have buried me decently, but now I shall come in the end to the tanning-vat."</seg>
<seg id="1480">至少，我会慢慢地消耗至死，而现在，我就要在制皮桶里结束性命了。”</seg>
<seg id="1481">Servants don't know a good master till they have served a worse.</seg>
<seg id="1481">到了更坏的主人那里，才知道前主人的好。</seg>
<seg id="1482">THE PACK-ASS, THE WILD ASS, AND THE LION</seg>
<seg id="1482">家驴、野驴和狮子</seg>
<seg id="1483">A Wild Ass saw a Pack-Ass jogging along under a heavy load, and taunted him with the condition of slavery in which he lived, in these words: "What a vile lot is yours compared with mine!</seg>
<seg id="1483">一头野驴看到一头家驴背负着沉重的货物一路小跑，便讥讽他过着奴隶般的生活：“和我相比，你过得多么卑微呀！</seg>
<seg id="1484">I am free as the air, and never do a stroke of work;</seg>
<seg id="1484">我自由自在地享受着大自然，从不下苦力，</seg>
<seg id="1485">and, as for fodder, I have only to go to the hills and there I find far more than enough for my needs.</seg>
<seg id="1485">说到食物，我只需要跑到山上去，就能发现大量吃的东西。</seg>
<seg id="1486">But you!</seg>
<seg id="1486">再看看你！</seg>
<seg id="1487">you depend on your master for food, and he makes you carry heavy loads every day and beats you unmercifully."</seg>
<seg id="1487">只能依靠主人施舍点吃的，他不仅每天都让你驮重物，还无情地鞭打你。”</seg>
<seg id="1488">At that moment a Lion appeared on the scene, and made no attempt to molest the Pack-Ass owing to the presence of the driver;</seg>
<seg id="1488">这时，一只狮子出现在他们视野中，由于驴夫的出现，狮子没有骚扰家驴，</seg>
<seg id="1489">but he fell upon the Wild Ass, who had no one to protect him, and without more ado made a meal of him.</seg>
<seg id="1489">直接扑向了没有保护者的野驴，立即吃掉了野驴。</seg>
<seg id="1490">It is no use being your own master unless you can stand up for yourself.</seg>
<seg id="1490">除非能照顾好自己，否则做自己的主人一点儿用也没有。</seg>
<seg id="1491">THE ANT</seg>
<seg id="1491">蚂蚁</seg>
<seg id="1492">Ants were once men and made their living by tilling the soil.</seg>
<seg id="1492">很久很久以前，蚂蚁本来是人，以耕地为生。</seg>
<seg id="1493">But, not content with the results of their own work, they were always casting longing eyes upon the crops and fruits of their neighbours, which they stole, whenever they got the chance, and added to their own store.</seg>
<seg id="1493">但是，他们不满足于自己的劳动所得，总是盯着邻居的水果和庄稼羡慕不已，只要一有机会，他们就会偷邻居的食物，放在自己的储藏室。</seg>
<seg id="1494">At last their covetousness made Jupiter so angry that he changed them into Ants.</seg>
<seg id="1494">后来，他们的贪婪让朱庇特十分生气，便把他们变成了现在的蚂蚁。</seg>
<seg id="1495">But, though their forms were changed, their nature remained the same:</seg>
<seg id="1495">然而，虽然他们的模样改变了，本性却依然未变。</seg>
