<seg id="1496">and so, to this day, they go about among the cornfields and gather the fruits of others' labour, and store them up for their own use.</seg>
<seg id="1496">直到现在，他们仍然会到别人的田里采集人家的劳动成果，贮存起来留作自己的食物。</seg>
<seg id="1497">You may punish a thief, but his bent remains.</seg>
<seg id="1497">你可以惩罚小偷，但他们的恶习依然如故。</seg>
<seg id="1498">THE FROGS AND THE WELL</seg>
<seg id="1498">青蛙和水井</seg>
<seg id="1499">Two Frogs lived together in a marsh.</seg>
<seg id="1499">两只青蛙住在一片沼泽地里。</seg>
<seg id="1500">But one hot summer the marsh dried up, and they left it to look for another place to live in: for frogs like damp places if they can get them.</seg>
<seg id="1500">在一个炎热的夏季，沼泽地干涸了，他们不得不去寻找另一块湿地，因为他们很喜欢潮湿的地方。</seg>
<seg id="1501">By and by they came to a deep well, and one of them looked down into it, and said to the other, "This looks a nice cool place:</seg>
<seg id="1501">不久，他们找到了一口深井，其中一只青蛙向下看了看，对另一只说：“看上去，这是个凉快的好地方，</seg>
<seg id="1502">let us jump in and settle here."</seg>
<seg id="1502">我们跳进去，就住在这里吧。”</seg>
<seg id="1503">But the other, who had a wiser head on his shoulders, replied, "Not so fast, my friend: supposing this well dried up like the marsh, how should we get out again?"</seg>
<seg id="1503">而另一只青蛙头脑比较聪明，回答说：“别着急，朋友，如果这口井也干了的话，我们可怎么出来呢？”</seg>
<seg id="1504">Think twice before you act.</seg>
<seg id="1504">凡事应三思而后行。</seg>
<seg id="1505">THE CRAB AND THE FOX</seg>
<seg id="1505">螃蟹和狐狸</seg>
<seg id="1506">A Crab once left the sea-shore and went and settled in a meadow some way inland, which looked very nice and green and seemed likely to be a good place to feed in.</seg>
<seg id="1506">有一次，一只螃蟹离开海边，定居在内陆的一块草地上，那里看着很美，有青青的绿草，是个养分充足的好地方。</seg>
<seg id="1507">But a hungry Fox came along and spied the Crab and caught him.</seg>
<seg id="1507">然而，一只饥饿的狐狸走过来，看见螃蟹并捉住了他。</seg>
<seg id="1508">Just as he was going to be eaten up, the Crab said, "This is just what I deserve;</seg>
<seg id="1508">就在狐狸将要吃掉他之前，螃蟹说：“我真是活该！</seg>
<seg id="1509">for I had no business to leave my natural home by the sea and settle here as though I belonged to the land."</seg>
<seg id="1509">我没有理由要离开海边那个天然的家，像陆地栖息的动物一样，偏要到这里来定居。”</seg>
<seg id="1510">Be content with your lot.</seg>
<seg id="1510">知足才能常乐。</seg>
<seg id="1511">THE FOX AND THE GRASSHOPPER</seg>
<seg id="1511">狐狸和蚂蚱</seg>
<seg id="1512">A Grasshopper sat chirping in the branches of a tree.</seg>
<seg id="1512">一只蚂蚱坐在树枝上叽叽喳喳地鸣唱。</seg>
<seg id="1513">A Fox heard her, and, thinking what a dainty morsel she would make, he tried to get her down by a trick.</seg>
<seg id="1513">一只狐狸听到她的叫声，心想这可是一顿美餐呀，便想出了一个诡计诱使蚂蚱下来。</seg>
<seg id="1514">Standing below in full view of her, he praised her song in the most flattering terms, and begged her to descend, saying he would like to make the acquaintance of the owner of so beautiful a voice.</seg>
<seg id="1514">他站在树下一个能完全看见蚂蚱的地方，用尽各种方法赞美蚂蚱的歌声悦耳动听，并劝蚂蚱下来，想要看一看是什么样的动物才能发出如此悦耳的声音。</seg>
<seg id="1515">But she was not to be taken in, and replied, "You are very much mistaken, my dear sir, if you imagine I am going to come down:</seg>
<seg id="1515">可是，蚂蚱识破了他的诡计，回答说：“喂，若是你以为我会飞下来，那就大错特错了。</seg>
<seg id="1516">I keep well out of the way of you and your kind ever since the day when I saw numbers of grasshoppers' wings strewn about the entrance to a fox's earth."</seg>
<seg id="1516">自从那天见到狐狸的洞口四周散布着无数蚂蚱的翅膀之后，我就开始警惕着你和你的同类了。”</seg>
<seg id="1517">THE FARMER, HIS BOY, AND THE ROOKS</seg>
<seg id="1517">农夫、伙计和白嘴鸦</seg>
<seg id="1518">A Farmer had just sown a field of wheat, and was keeping a careful watch over it, for numbers of Rooks and starlings kept continually settling on it and eating up the grain.</seg>
<seg id="1518">一个农夫刚刚播下一片麦种，十分小心地守护着，因为有些秃鼻乌鸦和八哥不断地在耕地上找谷子吃。</seg>
<seg id="1519">Along with him went his Boy, carrying a sling:</seg>
<seg id="1519">农夫的儿子也跟着农夫一起来到田里，手上还拿着一把弹弓，</seg>
<seg id="1520">and whenever the Farmer asked for the sling the starlings understood what he said and warned the Rooks and they were off in a moment.</seg>
<seg id="1520">每当农夫要弹弓时，八哥都能听懂他的话，并警告秃鼻乌鸦赶快飞走。</seg>
<seg id="1521">So the Farmer hit on a trick.</seg>
<seg id="1521">因此，农夫想出一招。</seg>
<seg id="1522">"My lad," said he, "we must get the better of these birds somehow.</seg>
<seg id="1522">“我的孩子，”他说，“我们必须得打败这些鸟。</seg>
<seg id="1523">After this, when I want the sling, I won't say 'sling,' but just 'humph!' and you must then hand me the sling quickly."</seg>
<seg id="1523">以后，等我想要弹弓时，我不会再说弹弓了，而只是“哼”一声，而你必须赶快递给我弹弓。”</seg>
<seg id="1524">Presently back came the whole flock.</seg>
<seg id="1524">不久，鸟群又回来了。</seg>
<seg id="1525">"Humph!" said the Farmer;</seg>
<seg id="1525">“哼！”农夫说，</seg>
<seg id="1526">but the starlings took no notice, and he had time to sling several stones among them, hitting one on the head, another in the legs, and another in the wing, before they got out of range.</seg>
<seg id="1526">不过，这次八哥没注意到，所以农夫有时间弹了多次石头，还没等他们飞走，便击中了一只鸟的头，一只鸟的腿，另一只鸟的翅膀。</seg>
<seg id="1527">As they made all haste away they met some cranes, who asked them what the matter was.</seg>
<seg id="1527">乌鸦和八哥在逃跑的路上遇见了几只鹤，其中一只问他们出了什么事。</seg>
<seg id="1528">"Matter?" said one of the Rooks;</seg>
<seg id="1528">“出事？”一只秃鼻乌鸦喊道，</seg>
<seg id="1529">"it's those rascals, men, that are the matter.</seg>
<seg id="1529">“都是人类那些骗子，他们就是麻烦。</seg>
<seg id="1530">Don't you go near them.</seg>
<seg id="1530">你不要去靠近他们。</seg>
<seg id="1531">They have a way of saying one thing and meaning another which has just been the death of several of our poor friends."</seg>
<seg id="1531">他们嘴里说一套，做的却是另一套，我们几个可怜的朋友刚刚因此而丧命呢！”</seg>
<seg id="1532">THE ASS AND THE DOG</seg>
<seg id="1532">驴和狗</seg>
<seg id="1533">An Ass and a Dog were on their travels together, and, as they went along, they found a sealed packet lying on the ground.</seg>
<seg id="1533">一头驴和一只狗一起外出旅行，走了一段路后，他们发现地上有一封密封好的信。</seg>
<seg id="1534">The Ass picked it up, broke the seal, and found it contained some writing, which he proceeded to read out aloud to the Dog.</seg>
<seg id="1534">驴捡起来，撕开封印，发现上面有写好的字，便大声读给狗听。</seg>
<seg id="1535">As he read on it turned out to be all about grass and barley and hay--in short, all the kinds of fodder that Asses are fond of.</seg>
<seg id="1535">可是，信里提到的几乎全是干草、大麦和糠麸之类驴喜欢的东西。</seg>
<seg id="1536">The Dog was a good deal bored with listening to all this, till at last his impatience got the better of him, and he cried, "Just skip a few pages, friend, and see if there isn't something about meat and bones."</seg>
<seg id="1536">听到这些内容，狗觉着很无聊，终于不耐烦地对驴喊道：“赶紧跳过这些内容，朋友，看看下面有没有提到肉和骨头之类的。”</seg>
<seg id="1537">The Ass glanced all through the packet, but found nothing of the sort, and said so.</seg>
<seg id="1537">驴浏览了一下信的全部内容，没有发现任何狗所想要的东西，就如实说了。</seg>
<seg id="1538">Then the Dog said in disgust, "Oh, throw it away, do: what's the good of a thing like that?"</seg>
<seg id="1538">然后，狗就带着厌恶的表情说：“把它扔了吧，朋友，这封信有什么意思呀？”</seg>
<seg id="1539">THE ASS CARRYING THE IMAGE</seg>
<seg id="1539">背着神像的驴</seg>
<seg id="1540">A certain man put an Image on the back of his Ass to take it to one of the temples of the town.</seg>
<seg id="1540">有个人把神像放在驴的背上，准备运到城里的一座寺庙里。</seg>
<seg id="1541">As they went along the road all the people they met uncovered and bowed their heads out of reverence for the Image;</seg>
<seg id="1541">他们走在路上时，所有遇见他们的人都对着神像顶礼膜拜，</seg>
<seg id="1542">but the Ass thought they were doing it out of respect for himself, and began to give himself airs accordingly.</seg>
<seg id="1542">而驴却以为人们是在向它致敬，逐渐骄傲自满起来。</seg>
<seg id="1543">At last he became so conceited that he imagined he could do as he liked, and, by way of protest against the load he was carrying, he came to a full stop and flatly declined to proceed any further.</seg>
<seg id="1543">最后，自以为是的他竟然幻想着可以肆意妄为，再也不用驮着沉重的货物了，于是，驴停下了脚步，再也不肯往前走。</seg>
<seg id="1544">His driver, finding him so obstinate, hit him hard and long with his stick, saying the while, "Oh, you dunder-headed idiot, do you suppose it's come to this, that men pay worship to an Ass?"</seg>
<seg id="1544">赶驴的人发现他这么固执，便用棍子狠狠地打了他一顿，并且说道：“你这个蠢货，竟然自以为这是在向你致敬，人们会对一头驴这么恭敬吗？”</seg>
<seg id="1545">Rude shocks await those who take to themselves the credit that is due to others.</seg>
<seg id="1545">那些夺走他人荣誉的人，必定会遭受沉重的打击。</seg>
<seg id="1546">THE ATHENIAN AND THE THEBAN</seg>
<seg id="1546">雅典人和底比斯人</seg>
<seg id="1547">An Athenian and a Theban were on the road together, and passed the time in conversation, as is the way of travellers.</seg>
<seg id="1547">一个雅典人和一个底比斯人一同走在路上，就像其他旅行者一样，他们用聊天来打发时间。</seg>
<seg id="1548">After discussing a variety of subjects they began to talk about heroes, a topic that tends to be more fertile than edifying.</seg>
<seg id="1548">聊了一些其他话题之后，他们开始谈起英雄，虽然没有什么教育意义，但这可是一个颇有谈资的内容。</seg>
<seg id="1549">Each of them was lavish in his praises of the heroes of his own city, until eventually the Theban asserted that Hercules was the greatest hero who had ever lived on earth, and now occupied a foremost place among the gods;</seg>
<seg id="1549">一提到赞美各自城市里的英雄，两个人都侃侃而谈。后来，底比斯人断言，赫拉克勒斯是地球上曾经存在过的最伟大的英雄，现在占据了众神之中的首要位置。</seg>
<seg id="1550">while the Athenian insisted that Theseus was far superior, for his fortune had been in every way supremely blessed, whereas Hercules had at one time been forced to act as a servant.</seg>
<seg id="1550">而雅典人则坚持认为，提修斯远远超过了赫拉克勒斯，因为他的命运在各方面都得到了充分的眷顾，而赫拉克勒斯曾一度被迫充当奴隶。</seg>
<seg id="1551">And he gained his point, for he was a very glib fellow, like all Athenians;</seg>
<seg id="1551">他达到了自己的目的，因为他像所有雅典人一样，是一个非常圆滑的家伙。</seg>
<seg id="1552">so that the Theban, who was no match for him in talking, cried at last in some disgust, "All right, have your way;</seg>
<seg id="1552">而底比斯人在谈话中根本不是他的对手，最后有些反感地大吼道：“好吧，随便你。</seg>
<seg id="1553">I only hope that, when our heroes are angry with us, Athens may suffer from the anger of Hercules, and Thebes only from that of Theseus."</seg>
<seg id="1553">我只希望，当我们的英雄对我们生气时，雅典人会从赫拉克勒斯的愤怒中遭殃，而底比斯人则从提修斯的愤怒中受苦。”</seg>
<seg id="1554">THE GOATHERD AND THE GOAT</seg>
<seg id="1554">牧羊人和山羊</seg>
<seg id="1555">A Goatherd was one day gathering his flock to return to the fold, when one of his goats strayed and refused to join the rest.</seg>
<seg id="1555">有一天，牧羊人赶着羊群回到羊圈里，其中有一只山羊失散了，并且拒绝回到羊群中。</seg>
<seg id="1556">He tried for a long time to get her to return by calling and whistling to her, but the Goat took no notice of him at all;</seg>
<seg id="1556">牧羊人费了好长时间叫她回来，既大声喊叫，又冲她吹口哨，但是山羊根本没注意到他。</seg>
<seg id="1557">so at last he threw a stone at her and broke one of her horns.</seg>
<seg id="1557">于是，牧羊人只得冲她扔了一块石头，正巧打断了山羊的一只羊角。</seg>
<seg id="1558">In dismay, he begged her not to tell his master: but she replied, "You silly fellow, my horn would cry aloud even if I held my tongue."</seg>
<seg id="1558">惊慌中，牧羊人肯求山羊不要告诉主人，可山羊却说：“你这个愚蠢的家伙，即使我不说，我的角也会告诉他事实呀。”</seg>
<seg id="1559">It's no use trying to hide what can't be hidden.</seg>
<seg id="1559">竭力掩盖无法隐瞒的事实是没用的。</seg>
<seg id="1560">THE SHEEP AND THE DOG</seg>
<seg id="1560">羊群和狗</seg>
<seg id="1561">Once upon a time the Sheep complained to the shepherd about the difference in his treatment of themselves and his Dog.</seg>
<seg id="1561">从前，有一群羊向牧羊人抱怨自己和狗受到了差别待遇。</seg>
<seg id="1562">"Your conduct," said they, "is very strange and, we think, very unfair.</seg>
<seg id="1562">“你的行为很奇怪，”羊群说，“我们认为非常不公平。</seg>
<seg id="1563">We provide you with wool and lambs and milk and you give us nothing but grass, and even that we have to find for ourselves:</seg>
<seg id="1563">我们为您提供羊毛、羔羊肉和羊奶，你却只给我们吃草，甚至于我们还要自己去找草吃。</seg>
<seg id="1564">but you get nothing at all from the Dog, and yet you feed him with tit-bits from your own table."</seg>
<seg id="1564">你从狗那里什么也没得到，可你却从自己的餐桌上拿些精美的食物喂他。”</seg>
<seg id="1565">Their remarks were overheard by the Dog, who spoke up at once and said, "Yes, and quite right, too:</seg>
<seg id="1565">狗听到了他们的言论，立刻开口说：“是的，的确如此。</seg>
<seg id="1566">where would you be if it wasn't for me?</seg>
<seg id="1566">要不是有我在，你们会在哪里呢？</seg>
<seg id="1567">Thieves would steal you!</seg>
<seg id="1567">小偷早就偷走你们了！</seg>
<seg id="1568">Wolves would eat you!</seg>
<seg id="1568">狼也会吃掉你们！</seg>
<seg id="1569">Indeed, if I didn't keep constant watch over you, you would be too terrified even to graze!"</seg>
<seg id="1569">其实，如果没有我守护着你们，你们可能连吃草都吓得不敢去！”</seg>
<seg id="1570">The Sheep were obliged to acknowledge that he spoke the truth, and never again made a grievance of the regard in which he was held by his master.</seg>
<seg id="1570">羊群不得不承认他说的有道理，便不再提受到主人差别待遇的意见了。</seg>
<seg id="1571">THE SHEPHERD AND THE WOLF</seg>
<seg id="1571">牧羊人和狼</seg>
<seg id="1572">A Shepherd found a Wolf's Cub straying in the pastures, and took him home and reared him along with his dogs.</seg>
<seg id="1572">牧羊人在牧场里捡到一只失散了的小狼崽，于是把它带回家，和狗一起喂养。</seg>
<seg id="1573">When the Cub grew to his full size, if ever a wolf stole a sheep from the flock, he used to join the dogs in hunting him down.</seg>
<seg id="1573">小狼崽长大以后，倘若有狼来偷羊吃，它就会和狗一起去追赶狼。</seg>
<seg id="1574">It sometimes happened that the dogs failed to come up with the thief, and, abandoning the pursuit, returned home.</seg>
<seg id="1574">有一次，狗没追上就回去了，</seg>
<seg id="1575">The Wolf would on such occasions continue the chase by himself, and when he overtook the culprit, would stop and share the feast with him, and then return to the Shepherd.</seg>
<seg id="1575">那只狼却继续追捕，待追上后，他看了看自己的同类，便与其一同分享了羊肉，然后回到牧羊人家里。</seg>
<seg id="1576">But if some time passed without a sheep being carried off by the wolves, he would steal one himself and share his plunder with the dogs.</seg>
<seg id="1576">从此以后，即便有时狼并没有来偷羊，他也会偷偷咬死一只羊，和狗一起分享战利品。</seg>
<seg id="1577">The Shepherd's suspicions were aroused, and one day he caught him in the act;</seg>
<seg id="1577">后来，牧羊人对它产生了怀疑，有一天终于发现了事实真相，</seg>
<seg id="1578">and, fastening a rope round his neck, hung him on the nearest tree.</seg>
<seg id="1578">便用绳子套住狼的脖子，将它吊死在旁边的树上。</seg>
<seg id="1579">What's bred in the bone is sure to come out in the flesh.</seg>
<seg id="1579">江山易改，本性难移。</seg>
<seg id="1580">THE LION, JUPITER, AND THE ELEPHANT</seg>
<seg id="1580">狮子、朱庇特和大象</seg>
<seg id="1581">The Lion, for all his size and strength, and his sharp teeth and claws, is a coward in one thing:</seg>
<seg id="1581">狮子有着健壮魁梧的体魄、锐利的牙齿和四爪，然而有一件事却让他成了懦夫。</seg>
<seg id="1582">he can't bear the sound of a cock crowing, and runs away whenever he hears it.</seg>
<seg id="1582">他受不了公鸡的啼鸣声。只要一听到这个声音，狮子立刻就会逃跑。</seg>
<seg id="1583">He complained bitterly to Jupiter for making him like that;</seg>
<seg id="1583">他痛苦地向朱庇特哭诉，为何把自己造成这样，</seg>
<seg id="1584">but Jupiter said it wasn't his fault:</seg>
<seg id="1584">可朱庇特却说这不是自己的错，</seg>
<seg id="1585">he had done the best he could for him, and, considering this was his only failing, he ought to be well content.</seg>
<seg id="1585">他已经尽可能地把优点都给了狮子，这不过是唯一的缺点，狮子应该知足了。</seg>
<seg id="1586">The Lion, however, wouldn't be comforted, and was so ashamed of his timidity that he wished he might die.</seg>
<seg id="1586">然而，狮子仍然觉着不舒服，为自己的胆小和懦弱羞愧得无地自容。</seg>
<seg id="1587">In this state of mind, he met the Elephant and had a talk with him.</seg>
<seg id="1587">正在这时候，他遇见了大象，便和大象聊起来。</seg>
<seg id="1588">He noticed that the great beast cocked up his ears all the time, as if he were listening for something, and he asked him why he did so.</seg>
<seg id="1588">他看见这头巨兽总是不停地扇动着耳朵，好像在倾听什么，于是便问为什么总这样。</seg>
<seg id="1589">Just then a gnat came humming by, and the Elephant said, "Do you see that wretched little buzzing insect?</seg>
<seg id="1589">恰好，有一只小飞虫在大象耳边嗡嗡地叫，大象回答说：“你看见这些嗡嗡叫的虫子了吗？</seg>
<seg id="1590">I'm terribly afraid of its getting into my ear:</seg>
<seg id="1590">我很担心他们钻进我的耳朵里，</seg>
<seg id="1591">if it once gets in, I'm dead and done for."</seg>
<seg id="1591">一旦让他们飞进去，我就完蛋了。”</seg>
<seg id="1592">The Lion's spirits rose at once when he heard this: "For," he said to himself, "if the Elephant, huge as he is, is afraid of a gnat, I needn't be so much ashamed of being afraid of a cock, who is ten thousand times bigger than a gnat."</seg>
<seg id="1592">一听到这话，狮子立刻打起了精神，自言自语地说：“如果像大象那么大的动物都害怕一只小虫子，我也不必为自己害怕公鸡而羞愧了，公鸡可比虫子大得多了。”</seg>
<seg id="1593">THE PIG AND THE SHEEP</seg>
<seg id="1593">猪和绵羊</seg>
<seg id="1594">A Pig found his way into a meadow where a flock of Sheep were grazing.</seg>
<seg id="1594">有一头猪跑进正在牧场里吃草的羊群中，</seg>
<seg id="1595">The shepherd caught him, and was proceeding to carry him off to the butcher's when he set up a loud squealing and struggled to get free.</seg>
<seg id="1595">牧羊人抓住了他，要把他送到屠夫那里，猪鬼哭狼嚎般拼命挣扎着想逃出来。</seg>
<seg id="1596">The Sheep rebuked him for making such a to-do, and said to him, "The shepherd catches us regularly and drags us off just like that, and we don't make any fuss."</seg>
<seg id="1596">羊群指责他大惊小怪，对猪说：“我们经常被牧羊人抓住，就像刚才那样被拖走，可从来不这样叫喊。”</seg>
<seg id="1597">"No, I dare say not," replied the Pig, "but my case and yours are altogether different:</seg>
<seg id="1597">猪回答说：“我和你们绝对不一样，</seg>
<seg id="1598">he only wants you for wool, but he wants me for bacon."</seg>
<seg id="1598">他抓你是为了你的毛，抓我却是为了吃我的肉呀。”</seg>
<seg id="1599">THE GARDENER AND HIS DOG</seg>
<seg id="1599">花匠和他的狗</seg>
<seg id="1600">A Gardner's Dog fell into a deep well, from which his master used to draw water for the plants in his garden with a rope and a bucket.</seg>
<seg id="1600">花匠的狗掉进了一口深井里，井旁边有绳子和桶，是花匠经常用来打水去浇花的工具，</seg>
<seg id="1601">Failing to get the Dog out by means of these, the Gardener went down into the well himself in order to fetch him up.</seg>
<seg id="1601">可无论用什么办法，他也没能把狗捞上来。于是，为了救小狗，花匠自己跳进了井中。</seg>
<seg id="1602">But the Dog thought he had come to make sure of drowning him;</seg>
<seg id="1602">可是，狗却以为主人下来是要淹死它。</seg>
<seg id="1603">so he bit his master as soon as he came within reach, and hurt him a good deal, with the result that he left the Dog to his fate and climbed out of the well, remarking, "It serves me quite right for trying to save so determined a suicide."</seg>
<seg id="1603">所以，当花匠靠近狗时，狗立刻狠狠地咬了他一口。花匠着实受了重伤，决定让狗自生自灭，不再管它了。花匠一边往上爬，一边说：“我真是活该！为什么要去救一个想要寻死的畜生呢？”</seg>
<seg id="1604">THE RIVERS AND THE SEA</seg>
<seg id="1604">河流和大海</seg>
<seg id="1605">Once upon a time all the Rivers combined to protest against the action of the Sea in making their waters salt.</seg>
<seg id="1605">从前，所有河流都联合起来抵抗大海的行为，不想让水变咸了。</seg>
<seg id="1606">"When we come to you," said they to the Sea, "we are sweet and drinkable:</seg>
<seg id="1606">“当我们流向你时，”河流对大海说，“我们本是甘甜可口的，</seg>
<seg id="1607">but when once we have mingled with you, our waters become as briny and unpalatable as your own."</seg>
<seg id="1607">可一旦与你混合，我们就变得跟你们一样，又咸又涩，一点儿都不好喝了。”</seg>
<seg id="1608">The Sea replied shortly, "Keep away from me and you'll remain sweet."</seg>
<seg id="1608">大海只是简单地回答道：“离我远一点，你们就会一直甘甜可口了。”</seg>
<seg id="1609">THE LION IN LOVE</seg>
<seg id="1609">恋爱的狮子</seg>
<seg id="1610">A Lion fell deeply in love with the daughter of a cottager and wanted to marry her;</seg>
<seg id="1610">一只狮子深深爱上了农夫的女儿，想娶她为妻。</seg>
<seg id="1611">but her father was unwilling to give her to so fearsome a husband, and yet didn't want to offend the Lion;</seg>
<seg id="1611">可是，农夫却不忍心让女儿嫁给一个这么可怕的丈夫，但又不想激怒狮子。</seg>
<seg id="1612">so he hit upon the following expedient.</seg>
<seg id="1612">于是他急中生智，想出一个权宜之计。</seg>
<seg id="1613">He went to the Lion and said, "I think you will make a very good husband for my daughter:</seg>
<seg id="1613">他去找狮子，并说：“我认为你是一个非常出色的丈夫人选，</seg>
<seg id="1614">but I cannot consent to your union unless you let me draw your teeth and pare your nails, for my daughter is terribly afraid of them."</seg>
<seg id="1614">但是我不能同意你们结合，除非先拔掉你的牙齿、剪掉你的指甲，因为我的女儿害怕这些东西。”</seg>
<seg id="1615">The Lion was so much in love that he readily agreed that this should be done.</seg>
<seg id="1615">狮子被爱冲昏了头，毫不犹豫地接受了农夫的要求。</seg>
<seg id="1616">When once, however, he was thus disarmed, the Cottager was afraid of him no longer, but drove him away with his club.</seg>
<seg id="1616">然而，狮子刚被缴械，农夫就不再惧怕狮子了，反而用棍棒赶走了狮子。</seg>
<seg id="1617">THE BEE-KEEPER</seg>
<seg id="1617">养蜂人</seg>
<seg id="1618">A Thief found his way into an apiary when the Bee-keeper was away, and stole all the honey.</seg>
<seg id="1618">趁养蜂人不在家时，一个小偷溜进蜂房，偷走了所有的蜂蜜。</seg>
<seg id="1619">When the Keeper returned and found the hives empty, he was very much upset and stood staring at them for some time.</seg>
<seg id="1619">养蜂人回来后发现蜂箱空了，伤心难过之余，他站在那里盯着看了很长时间。</seg>
<seg id="1620">Before long the bees came back from gathering honey, and, finding their hives overturned and the Keeper standing by, they made for him with their stings.</seg>
<seg id="1620">不久，蜜蜂采完花蜜回来，发现自己的蜂巢空了，而养蜂人又站在一边，便都围住他用尾针刺。</seg>
<seg id="1621">At this he fell into a passion and cried, "You ungrateful scoundrels, you let the thief who stole my honey get off scot-free, and then you go and sting me who have always taken such care of you!"</seg>
<seg id="1621">养蜂人被群蜂围住，痛苦地大喊：“你们这些不知感恩的坏家伙！让那偷蜜的贼逃之夭夭，却一个劲地来刺一直在照顾你们的人！”</seg>
<seg id="1622">When you hit back make sure you have got the right man.</seg>
<seg id="1622">发动反击时，一定要确定自己找对了人。</seg>
<seg id="1623">THE WOLF AND THE HORSE</seg>
<seg id="1623">狼和马</seg>
<seg id="1624">A Wolf on his rambles came to a field of oats, but, not being able to eat them, he was passing on his way when a Horse came along.</seg>
<seg id="1624">一只狼溜达着来到了一个麦田，然而，狼并不吃大麦，看见一匹马走过来，他便让开了。</seg>
<seg id="1625">"Look," said the Wolf, "here's a fine field of oats.</seg>
<seg id="1625">狼对马说：“看吧，这是一块上好的麦田。</seg>
<seg id="1626">For your sake I have left it untouched, and I shall greatly enjoy the sound of your teeth munching the ripe grain."</seg>
<seg id="1626">为了给你留着，我都没敢动。而且，我非常喜欢听你牙齿咀嚼成熟麦穗的声音。”</seg>
<seg id="1627">But the Horse replied, "If wolves could eat oats, my fine friend, you would hardly have indulged your ears at the cost of your belly."</seg>
<seg id="1627">然而，马却回答说：“朋友，如果狼能吃大麦，你就未必喜欢听我吃麦穗的声音了。”</seg>
<seg id="1628">There is no virtue in giving to others what is useless to oneself.</seg>
<seg id="1628">将己所不欲之物施与他人，并无美德可言。</seg>
<seg id="1629">THE BAT, THE BRAMBLE, AND THE SEAGULL</seg>
<seg id="1629">蝙蝠、荆棘和海鸥</seg>
<seg id="1630">A Bat, a Bramble, and a Seagull went into partnership and determined to go on a trading voyage together.</seg>
<seg id="1630">一只蝙蝠、一棵荆棘与一只海鸥，决定合伙出海做一次生意。</seg>
<seg id="1631">The Bat borrowed a sum of money for his venture; the Bramble laid in a stock of clothes of various kinds; and the Seagull took a quantity of lead:</seg>
<seg id="1631">于是，蝙蝠借了一笔钱作为资金，荆棘带来了一包款式不同的衣服，而海鸥带来了一些铅，</seg>
<seg id="1632">and so they set out.</seg>
<seg id="1632">然后，他们起航出发了。</seg>
<seg id="1633">By and by a great storm came on, and their boat with all the cargo went to the bottom, but the three travellers managed to reach land.</seg>
<seg id="1633">不久，一场暴风雨袭来，他们的船和所有货物都沉没了。幸运的是，三个航行者设法回到了岸上。</seg>
<seg id="1634">Ever since then the Seagull flies to and fro over the sea, and every now and then dives below the surface, looking for the lead he's lost;</seg>
<seg id="1634">从此以后，海鸥总是在海面上飞来飞去，即便偶尔钻入水中，也是在寻找丢失的铅；</seg>
<seg id="1635">while the Bat is so afraid of meeting his creditors that he hides away by day and only comes out at night to feed;</seg>
<seg id="1635">蝙蝠则害怕见到债主，所以总是白天藏着，夜里才出来觅食；</seg>
<seg id="1636">and the Bramble catches hold of the clothes of every one who passes by, hoping some day to recognise and recover the lost garments.</seg>
<seg id="1636">而荆棘总爱扯住过路人的衣服，希望有一天能找到丢失的衣服以弥补损失。</seg>
<seg id="1637">All men are more concerned to recover what they lose than to acquire what they lack.</seg>
<seg id="1637">所有人都更希望能弥补损失，而非弥补不足。</seg>
<seg id="1638">THE DOG AND THE WOLF</seg>
<seg id="1638">狗和狼</seg>
<seg id="1639">A Dog was lying in the sun before a farmyard gate when a Wolf pounced upon him and was just going to eat him up;</seg>
<seg id="1639">在阳光照耀下，一条狗躺在农院门前睡着了。一只狼窥见后，冲上去袭击他，正想吃掉他时，</seg>
<seg id="1640">but he begged for his life and said, "You see how thin I am and what a wretched meal I should make you now:</seg>
<seg id="1640">狗乞求狼饶了自己，说：“我现在骨瘦如柴，还不够你塞牙缝的呢。</seg>
<seg id="1641">but if you will only wait a few days my master is going to give a feast.</seg>
<seg id="1641">不过，如果你再多等几天，我的主人就要举办宴会了，</seg>
<seg id="1642">All the rich scraps and pickings will fall to me and I shall get nice and fat:</seg>
<seg id="1642">到时，所有的佳肴美食都会给我吃，而我也会变得肥肥胖胖的，</seg>
<seg id="1643">then will be the time for you to eat me."</seg>
<seg id="1643">然后，你再来吃我，不是更好吗。”</seg>
<seg id="1644">The Wolf thought this was a very good plan and went away.</seg>
<seg id="1644">狼听信了狗的话，便放了他。</seg>
<seg id="1645">Some time afterwards he came to the farmyard again, and found the Dog lying out of reach on the stable roof.</seg>
<seg id="1645">过了几天，狼又来到农院，发现狗躺在他够不到的屋顶上。</seg>
<seg id="1646">"Come down," he called, "and be eaten: you remember our agreement?"</seg>
<seg id="1646">“下来，”狼喊道，“快让我吃了你，你不记得我们的协议了吗？”</seg>
<seg id="1647">But the Dog said coolly, "My friend, if ever you catch me lying down by the gate there again, don't you wait for any feast."</seg>
<seg id="1647">而狗却从容地说：“朋友，要是你上次在门口抓住了躺在地上的我，就不用等待什么宴会了呀。”</seg>
<seg id="1648">Once bitten, twice shy.</seg>
<seg id="1648">一朝被蛇咬，十年怕井绳。</seg>
<seg id="1649">THE WASP AND THE SNAKE</seg>
<seg id="1649">黄蜂和蛇</seg>
<seg id="1650">A Wasp settled on the head of a Snake, and not only stung him several times, but clung obstinately to the head of his victim.</seg>
<seg id="1650">一只黄蜂坐在一条蛇的头上，不仅多次用刺去叮蛇，而且还牢牢地贴在受害者的头上。</seg>
<seg id="1651">Maddened with pain the Snake tried every means he could think of to get rid of the creature, but without success.</seg>
<seg id="1651">蛇疼得快要发疯了，尝试了很多方法想要赶走这个黄蜂，可是都没有成功。</seg>
<seg id="1652">At last he became desperate, and crying, "Kill you I will, even at the cost of my own life,"</seg>
<seg id="1652">最后，蛇绝望了，大喊道：“我要杀了你，即使丢掉我自己的性命也在所不惜。”</seg>
<seg id="1653">he laid his head with the Wasp on it under the wheel of a passing waggon, and they both perished together.</seg>
<seg id="1653">于是，蛇将自己的头伸到一辆从旁经过的马车车轮下，他们同归于尽了。</seg>
<seg id="1654">THE EAGLE AND THE BEETLE</seg>
<seg id="1654">老鹰和甲虫</seg>
<seg id="1655">An Eagle was chasing a hare, which was running for dear life and was at her wits' end to know where to turn for help.</seg>
<seg id="1655">一只鹰正在奋力追一只兔子，而兔子则拼命奔跑，一筹莫展地不知该到哪里寻求帮助。</seg>
<seg id="1656">Presently she espied a Beetle, and begged it to aid her.</seg>
<seg id="1656">这时，她恰巧看见一只甲虫，便向他求救。</seg>
<seg id="1657">So when the Eagle came up the Beetle warned her not to touch the hare, which was under its protection.</seg>
<seg id="1657">于是，当老鹰过来时，甲虫便警告她不要碰那只兔子。</seg>
<seg id="1658">But the Eagle never noticed the Beetle because it was so small, seized the hare and ate her up.</seg>
<seg id="1658">老鹰根本没有把小小的甲虫放在眼里，因为它实在太不起眼了，终于还是抓住兔子并吃了她。</seg>
<seg id="1659">The Beetle never forgot this, and used to keep an eye on the Eagle's nest, and whenever the Eagle laid an egg it climbed up and rolled it out of the nest and broke it.</seg>
<seg id="1659">甲虫一直没有忘记这件事，经常关注着老鹰的巢，只要老鹰一下蛋，他便悄悄地爬上去，把老鹰蛋滚出巢来摔碎它。</seg>
<seg id="1660">At last the Eagle got so worried over the loss of her eggs that she went up to Jupiter, who is the special protector of Eagles, and begged him to give her a safe place to nest in:</seg>
<seg id="1660">后来，老鹰十分担心再丢失自己的蛋，便跑到朱庇特（鹰的特别守护神）那里，请求给自己一个安全的地方生儿育女。</seg>
<seg id="1661">so he let her lay her eggs in his lap.</seg>
<seg id="1661">于是，朱庇特让她在自己的膝上下蛋。</seg>
<seg id="1662">But the Beetle noticed this and made a ball of dirt the size of an Eagle's egg, and flew up and deposited it in Jupiter's lap.</seg>
<seg id="1662">然而，甲虫也注意到了此事，就做了一个和鹰蛋差不多大小的泥球，然后飞上去，把它扔到了朱庇特的膝盖上。</seg>
<seg id="1663">When Jupiter saw the dirt, he stood up to shake it out of his robe, and, forgetting about the eggs, he shook them out too, and they were broken just as before.</seg>
<seg id="1663">朱庇特一看是泥球，马上站起身来抖擞自己的长袍，浑然忘记了膝上还有老鹰下的蛋，无意间把蛋也抖落了，老鹰的蛋像之前那样摔了个粉碎。</seg>
<seg id="1664">Ever since then, they say, Eagles never lay their eggs at the season when Beetles are about.</seg>
<seg id="1664">据说，从那以后，在甲虫出现的时节，老鹰就再也不下蛋了。</seg>
<seg id="1665">The weak will sometimes find ways to avenge an insult, even upon the strong.</seg>
<seg id="1665">即便对手是强者，弱者有时也会想方设法地报仇雪耻。</seg>
<seg id="1666">THE FOWLER AND THE LARK</seg>
<seg id="1666">捕鸟人和百灵鸟</seg>
<seg id="1667">A Fowler was setting his nets for little birds when a Lark came up to him and asked him what he was doing.</seg>
<seg id="1667">一个捕鸟人正在撒网，好让小鸟们自投罗网。这时，一只百灵鸟走过来，问他在干什么。</seg>
<seg id="1668">"I am engaged in founding a city," said he, and with that he withdrew to a short distance and concealed himself.</seg>
<seg id="1668">“我正在建造一座漂亮的城市。”捕鸟人回答道，说完就跑到远处藏起来。</seg>
<seg id="1669">The Lark examined the nets with great curiosity, and presently, catching sight of the bait, hopped on to them in order to secure it, and became entangled in the meshes.</seg>
<seg id="1669">百灵鸟带着极大的好奇心，跑过去想看个究竟，她小心地冲着网中的诱饵跳过去，结果却被缠在网中。</seg>
<seg id="1670">The Fowler then ran up quickly and captured her.</seg>
<seg id="1670">捕鸟人很快跑过来，抓住了她。</seg>
<seg id="1671">"What a fool I was!" said she:</seg>
<seg id="1671">百灵鸟说：“我可真是个傻瓜！</seg>
<seg id="1672">"but at any rate, if that's the kind of city you are founding, it'll be a long time before you find fools enough to fill it."</seg>
<seg id="1672">但无论如何，如果这就是你建造的城市，那么估计要花很长时间才能找到足够多的傻瓜来填补空缺！”</seg>
<seg id="1673">THE FISHERMAN PIPING</seg>
<seg id="1673">吹笛子的渔夫</seg>
<seg id="1674">A Fisherman who could play the flute went down one day to the sea-shore with his nets and his flute;</seg>
<seg id="1674">有一天，一个会吹长笛的渔夫带着笛子和渔网来到海边，</seg>
<seg id="1675">and, taking his stand on a projecting rock, began to play a tune, thinking that the music would bring the fish jumping out of the sea.</seg>
<seg id="1675">他站在一块突出海面的岩石上，开始吹奏曲子，希望用笛声引诱鱼儿跳出海面。</seg>
<seg id="1676">He went on playing for some time, but not a fish appeared:</seg>
<seg id="1676">渔夫弹奏了一会儿，没有一条鱼出来。</seg>
<seg id="1677">so at last he threw down his flute and cast his net into the sea, and made a great haul of fish.</seg>
<seg id="1677">最后，他把长笛放到一边，撒网入海，却捞起满网的鱼。</seg>
<seg id="1678">When they were landed and he saw them leaping about on the shore, he cried, "You rascals!</seg>
<seg id="1678">当渔夫把网拖上岸后，看见鱼儿在岸边不停地跳跃，他便说：“你们这些淘气鬼！</seg>
<seg id="1679">you wouldn't dance when I piped:</seg>
<seg id="1679">我吹笛子时，你们不肯跳；</seg>
<seg id="1680">but now I've stopped, you can do nothing else!"</seg>
<seg id="1680">现在我不吹了，你们却在这里欢蹦乱跳！”</seg>
<seg id="1681">THE WEASEL AND THE MAN</seg>
<seg id="1681">黄鼠狼和人</seg>
<seg id="1682">A Man once caught a Weasel, which was always sneaking about the house, and was just going to drown it in a tub of water, when it begged hard for its life, and said to him, "Surely you haven't the heart to put me to death?</seg>
<seg id="1682">从前，有一个人抓住了一只黄鼠狼，它总是在房子里偷偷摸摸。这人正要用一盆水淹死它时，黄鼠狼苦苦哀求人饶了自己的性命，并且对人说：“你一定不忍心杀了我！</seg>
<seg id="1683">Think how useful I have been in clearing your house of the mice and lizards which used to infest it, and show your gratitude by sparing my life."</seg>
<seg id="1683">想想我对你们家做的贡献吧，我可是一直在清理你家里的老鼠和蜥蜴，为了显示你对我的感激之情，就饶我一命吧。”</seg>
<seg id="1684">"You have not been altogether useless, I grant you," said the Man:</seg>
<seg id="1684">“我也承认，你并非完全无用，”男人说，</seg>
<seg id="1685">"but who killed the fowls?</seg>
<seg id="1685">“但是，是谁杀了鸡？</seg>
<seg id="1686">Who stole the meat?</seg>
<seg id="1686">是谁偷了肉？</seg>
<seg id="1687">No, no!</seg>
<seg id="1687">不，不！</seg>
<seg id="1688">You do much more harm than good, and die you shall."</seg>
<seg id="1688">你做了太多坏事，理应去死。”</seg>
<seg id="1689">THE PLOUGHMAN, THE ASS, AND THE OX</seg>
<seg id="1689">农夫、驴和公牛</seg>
<seg id="1690">A Ploughman yoked his Ox and his Ass together, and set to work to plough his field.</seg>
<seg id="1690">农夫给他的公牛和驴一起套上牛轭，然后赶着它们下地犁田。</seg>
<seg id="1691">It was a poor makeshift of a team, but it was the best he could do, as he had but a single Ox.</seg>
<seg id="1691">这是一个糟糕的临时组合，但农夫已经尽力了，因为他只有一头公牛。</seg>
<seg id="1692">At the end of the day, when the beasts were loosed from the yoke, the Ass said to the Ox, "Well, we've had a hard day: which of us is to carry the master home?"</seg>
<seg id="1692">干了一天活后，牲口被主人从牛轭里解放出来，驴对牛说：“我们可是度过了艰难的一天，我们两个当中，谁载着主人回家呢？”</seg>
<seg id="1693">The Ox looked surprised at the question. "Why," said he, "you, to be sure, as usual."</seg>
<seg id="1693">听了驴的话，牛似乎很惊讶，“怎么这么问呢，”他说，“当然是你，像往常一样。”</seg>
<seg id="1694">DEMADES AND HIS FABLE</seg>
<seg id="1694">狄马德斯和他的寓言</seg>
<seg id="1695">Demades the orator was once speaking in the Assembly at Athens;</seg>
<seg id="1695">有一次，演说家狄马德斯在雅典的一次集会上演讲，</seg>
<seg id="1696">but the people were very inattentive to what he was saying, so he stopped and said, "Gentlemen, I should like to tell you one of Æsop's fables."</seg>
<seg id="1696">但是没有一个人认真听，他便停下来，说：“先生们，我很想告诉你们一个伊索寓言里的故事。”</seg>
<seg id="1697">This made every one listen intently.</seg>
<seg id="1697">这话受到了人们的重视。</seg>
<seg id="1698">Then Demades began: "Demeter, a Swallow, and an Eel were once travelling together, and came to a river without a bridge:</seg>
<seg id="1698">接着，他开始说：“有一次，得墨忒耳（掌管农业、结婚、丰饶的女神）和一只燕子、一条鳗鱼一同出行，他们要穿过一条没有桥的河，</seg>
<seg id="1699">the Swallow flew over it, and the Eel swam across";</seg>
<seg id="1699">燕子飞过去了，鳗鱼游过去了。”</seg>
<seg id="1700">and then he stopped.</seg>
<seg id="1700">讲到这里，他便停下来，不再讲了。</seg>
<seg id="1701">"What happened to Demeter?" cried several people in the audience.</seg>
<seg id="1701">听众中有几个人问他：“那么得墨忒耳怎么过去的呢？”</seg>
<seg id="1702">"Demeter," he replied, "is very angry with you for listening to fables when you ought to be minding public business."</seg>
<seg id="1702">他回答说：“得墨忒耳正在生你们的气呢，因为你们对公共事务毫无兴趣，一心只喜欢听伊索寓言。”</seg>
<seg id="1703">THE MONKEY AND THE DOLPHIN</seg>
<seg id="1703">猴子和海豚</seg>
<seg id="1704">When people go on a voyage they often take with them lap-dogs or monkeys as pets to wile away the time.</seg>
<seg id="1704">人类在出海航行时喜欢带上哈巴狗或猴子之类的宠物，以供消遣。</seg>
<seg id="1705">Thus it fell out that a man returning to Athens from the East had a pet Monkey on board with him.</seg>
<seg id="1705">一个人从东方回到雅典时，就带了一只猴子随行。</seg>
<seg id="1706">As they neared the coast of Attica a great storm burst upon them, and the ship capsized.</seg>
<seg id="1706">当他们靠近阿提卡海岸时，一场风暴突然袭来，船被狂风巨浪打翻了，</seg>
<seg id="1707">All on board were thrown into the water, and tried to save themselves by swimming, the Monkey among the rest.</seg>
<seg id="1707">甲板上的所有人都被抛入水中，人们试着游向岸边，猴子也在其中。</seg>
<seg id="1708">A Dolphin saw him, and, supposing him to be a man, took him on his back and began swimming towards the shore.</seg>
<seg id="1708">一只海豚看见了猴子，以为是人，立即将它驮到背上，游向岸边。</seg>
<seg id="1709">When they got near the Piræus, which is the port of Athens, the Dolphin asked the Monkey if he was an Athenian.</seg>
<seg id="1709">当他们快要到达雅典的珀赖欧斯海港时，海豚问那猴子是不是雅典人。</seg>
<seg id="1710">The Monkey replied that he was, and added that he came of a very distinguished family.</seg>
<seg id="1710">猴子回答说是的，而且还补充说自己出身名门望族。</seg>
<seg id="1711">"Then, of course, you know the Piræus," continued the Dolphin.</seg>
<seg id="1711">“那么，你肯定了解珀赖欧斯了？”海琢接着又问道。</seg>
<seg id="1712">The Monkey thought he was referring to some high official or other, and replied, "Oh, yes, he's a very old friend of mine."</seg>
<seg id="1712">猴子以为海豚说的是某个官员或什么人，便回答说：“他是我的一个老朋友。”</seg>
<seg id="1713">At that, detecting his hypocrisy, the Dolphin was so disgusted that he dived below the surface, and the unfortunate Monkey was quickly drowned.</seg>
<seg id="1713">海豚察觉到了猴子的虚伪，十分气愤，便没入水中，不幸的猴子很快就被淹死了。</seg>
<seg id="1714">THE CROW AND THE SNAKE</seg>
<seg id="1714">乌鸦和蛇</seg>
<seg id="1715">A hungry Crow spied a Snake lying asleep in a sunny spot, and, picking it up in his claws, he was carrying it off to a place where he could make a meal of it without being disturbed, when the Snake reared its head and bit him.</seg>
<seg id="1715">一只饥饿的乌鸦暗中发现一条蛇正在温暖的阳光下熟睡，便猛扑过去用爪子抓住了蛇，带着他飞到一个可以安然享受美食而不受打扰的地方，这时，惊醒的蛇回过头来，咬了乌鸦一大口。</seg>
<seg id="1716">It was a poisonous Snake, and the bite was fatal, and the dying Crow said, "What a cruel fate is mine!</seg>
<seg id="1716">这是一条毒蛇，挨咬的乌鸦受到了致命袭击。将死时，乌鸦说：“我的命运多么不幸呀！</seg>
<seg id="1717">I thought I had made a lucky find, and it has cost me my life!"</seg>
<seg id="1717">我以为自己找到了美食，可是却因此而丢掉了性命。”</seg>
<seg id="1718">THE DOGS AND THE FOX</seg>
<seg id="1718">狗和狐狸</seg>
<seg id="1719">Some Dogs once found a lion's skin, and were worrying it with their teeth.</seg>
<seg id="1719">几条狗发现了一张狮子皮，便使劲用牙齿撕碎了。</seg>
<seg id="1720">Just then a Fox came by, and said, "You think yourselves very brave, no doubt;</seg>
<seg id="1720">碰巧，一只狐狸走过来，说：“显然，你们以为自己很英勇，</seg>
<seg id="1721">but if that were a live lion you'd find his claws a good deal sharper than your teeth."</seg>
<seg id="1721">可如果这是一头活着的狮子，你们就会明白，他的爪子显然要比你们的牙齿更锋利。”</seg>
<seg id="1722">THE NIGHTINGALE AND THE HAWK</seg>
<seg id="1722">夜莺和老鹰</seg>
<seg id="1723">A Nightingale was sitting on a bough of an oak and singing, as her custom was.</seg>
<seg id="1723">夜莺坐在一棵橡树的树枝上，像往常一样在歌唱。</seg>
<seg id="1724">A hungry Hawk presently spied her, and darting to the spot seized her in his talons.</seg>
<seg id="1724">一只饥饿的老鹰看见她后，便猛飞过去用鹰爪抓住了她。</seg>
<seg id="1725">He was just about to tear her in pieces when she begged him to spare her life:</seg>
<seg id="1725">就在老鹰将要撕碎夜莺时，她恳求老鹰饶命：</seg>
<seg id="1726">"I'm not big enough," she pleaded, "to make you a good meal:</seg>
<seg id="1726">“我的个头太小了，不能让你饱餐一顿，</seg>
<seg id="1727">you ought to seek your prey among the bigger birds."</seg>
<seg id="1727">你应当去抓那些个头更大的鸟。”</seg>
<seg id="1728">The Hawk eyed her with some contempt. "You must think me very simple," said he, "if you suppose I am going to give up a certain prize on the chance of a better of which I see at present no signs."</seg>
<seg id="1728">老鹰不屑一顾地看着她，说：“如果你认为我会放弃手中现成的食物，而去追求目前看不见影的东西，那可真是太小看我了。”</seg>
<seg id="1729">THE ROSE AND THE AMARANTH</seg>
<seg id="1729">玫瑰花和苋菜</seg>
<seg id="1730">A Rose and an Amaranth blossomed side by side in a garden, and the Amaranth said to her neighbour, "How I envy you your beauty and your sweet scent!</seg>
<seg id="1730">玫瑰花和苋菜在花园里并排而立，苋菜对自己的邻居——玫瑰花说：“我真羡慕你，有着漂亮的颜色和芬芳的香味！</seg>
<seg id="1731">No wonder you are such a universal favourite."</seg>
<seg id="1731">毫无疑问，你是世上最美丽的花朵！”</seg>
<seg id="1732">But the Rose replied with a shade of sadness in her voice, "Ah, my dear friend, I bloom but for a time:</seg>
<seg id="1732">玫瑰花却回答说：“亲爱的朋友，我只开一季而已。</seg>
<seg id="1733">my petals soon wither and fall, and then I die.</seg>
<seg id="1733">我的花瓣很快就会枯萎凋谢，然后我就死去了。</seg>
<seg id="1734">But your flowers never fade, even if they are cut; for they are everlasting."</seg>
<seg id="1734">而你的花却永不褪色，即使被割断了，它们依然能够常绿、不褪色。”</seg>
<seg id="1735">THE MAN, THE HORSE, THE OX, AND THE DOG</seg>
<seg id="1735">人、马、牛、狗</seg>
<seg id="1736">One winter's day, during a severe storm, a Horse, an Ox, and a Dog came and begged for shelter in the house of a Man.</seg>
<seg id="1736">冬日里的一天，一场强烈风暴过后，马、牛、狗纷纷来到人居住的房子里，乞求得到庇护。</seg>
<seg id="1737">He readily admitted them, and, as they were cold and wet, he lit a fire for their comfort:</seg>
<seg id="1737">人爽快地接纳了他们。因为他们又湿又冷，人便生火取暖，让他们舒服一些。</seg>
<seg id="1738">and he put oats before the Horse, and hay before the Ox, while he fed the Dog with the remains of his own dinner.</seg>
<seg id="1738">不仅如此，人还把燕麦放到马的面前，把干草放到牛的面前，把自己吃剩的饭放在狗的面前。</seg>
<seg id="1739">When the storm abated, and they were about to depart, they determined to show their gratitude in the following way.</seg>
<seg id="1739">风暴减弱后，他们准备离开人的房子，决定以某种方式来表示自己的感激之情。</seg>
<seg id="1740">They divided the life of Man among them, and each endowed one part of it with the qualities which were peculiarly his own.</seg>
<seg id="1740">他们将人的一生分成几个阶段，然后在每个阶段分别赋予自己的某种特殊品质。</seg>
<seg id="1741">The Horse took youth, and hence young men are high-mettled and impatient of restraint;</seg>
<seg id="1741">马取走了年轻阶段，因此，年轻人奋发向上但不受约束；</seg>
<seg id="1742">the Ox took middle age, and accordingly men in middle life are steady and hard-working;</seg>
<seg id="1742">牛取走了中年阶段，因此，中年人踏实稳定且埋头苦干；</seg>
<seg id="1743">while the Dog took old age, which is the reason why old men are so often peevish and ill-tempered, and, like dogs, attached chiefly to those who look to their comfort, while they are disposed to snap at those who are unfamiliar or distasteful to them.</seg>
<seg id="1743">而狗则接受了老年阶段，这正是老年人经常脾气暴躁的原因之一，他们也像狗那样，主要依赖那些能给他们带来温暖和舒适的人，而厉声呵斥那些陌生或令其不悦的人。</seg>
<seg id="1744">THE WOLVES, THE SHEEP, AND THE RAM</seg>
<seg id="1744">狼群、羊群和公羊</seg>
<seg id="1745">The Wolves sent a deputation to the Sheep with proposals for a lasting peace between them, on condition of their giving up the sheep-dogs to instant death.</seg>
<seg id="1745">狼群派了一个使者到羊群那里去送一份缔结永久和平的建议书，其中提出，只要羊群放弃牧羊犬的看护，并把他处死，狼群便愿意与羊群和平相处。</seg>
<seg id="1746">The foolish Sheep agreed to the terms;</seg>
<seg id="1746">愚蠢的羊群同意了狼群的提议，</seg>
<seg id="1747">but an old Ram, whose years had brought him wisdom, interfered and said, "How can we expect to live at peace with you?</seg>
<seg id="1747">但是一只上了年纪的公羊因年长而颇具智慧，他说：“即便眼前有狗在保护我们，我们尚且不能平安地逃出你们的魔爪，</seg>
<seg id="1748">Why, even with the dogs at hand to protect us, we are never secure from your murderous attacks!"</seg>
<seg id="1748">还怎么敢期望着与你们和平相处呢？”</seg>
<seg id="1749">THE SWAN</seg>
<seg id="1749">天鹅</seg>
<seg id="1750">The Swan is said to sing but once in its life--when it knows that it is about to die.</seg>
<seg id="1750">据说，天鹅一生只唱一次歌，只有在他死期临近时才唱。</seg>
<seg id="1751">A certain man, who had heard of the song of the Swan, one day saw one of these birds for sale in the market, and bought it and took it home with him.</seg>
<seg id="1751">一个曾经听过天鹅那优美歌声的人，偶然在市场上看到几只天鹅正待出售，便买了一只带回家。</seg>
<seg id="1752">A few days later he had some friends to dinner, and produced the Swan, and bade it sing for their entertainment: but the Swan remained silent.</seg>
<seg id="1752">几天后，他邀请了几个朋友来吃饭，并介绍了自己的天鹅，让他唱首歌来助兴。可是，天鹅却始终保持沉默。</seg>
<seg id="1753">In course of time, when it was growing old, it became aware of its approaching end and broke into a sweet, sad song.</seg>
<seg id="1753">后来，终于有一天，天鹅慢慢老了，他知道自己死期将至，便展开歌喉，唱出了一曲甜美哀婉的歌。</seg>
<seg id="1754">When its owner heard it, he said angrily, "If the creature only sings when it is about to die, what a fool I was that day I wanted to hear its song!</seg>
<seg id="1754">主人听到后，生气地说：“如果你真是在临死前才肯唱歌，那我多么愚蠢呀！</seg>
<seg id="1755">I ought to have wrung its neck instead of merely inviting it to sing."</seg>
<seg id="1755">我真应该在那天就拧断你的脖子，而不仅仅是让你唱歌了。”</seg>
<seg id="1756">THE SNAKE AND JUPITER</seg>
<seg id="1756">蛇和朱庇特</seg>
<seg id="1757">A Snake suffered a good deal from being constantly trodden upon by man and beast, owing partly to the length of his body and partly to his being unable to raise himself above the surface of the ground:</seg>
<seg id="1757">一条蛇因为人类和其他野兽的践踏常常生活在水深火热之中，部分原因是他的身体过长，另一部分原因是他无法离开地面。</seg>
<seg id="1758">so he went and complained to Jupiter about the risks to which he was exposed.</seg>
<seg id="1758">于是，他便跑去向朱庇特抱怨自己所暴露出的危险。</seg>
<seg id="1759">But Jupiter had little sympathy for him.</seg>
<seg id="1759">可是，朱庇特却不怎么同情他。</seg>
<seg id="1760">"I dare say," said he, "that if you had bitten the first that trod on you, the others would have taken more trouble to look where they put their feet."</seg>
<seg id="1760">朱庇特说：“如果你咬了第一个践踏你的人，其他人就不再敢冒险这样做了。”</seg>
<seg id="1761">THE WOLF AND HIS SHADOW</seg>
<seg id="1761">狼和他的影子</seg>
<seg id="1762">A Wolf, who was roaming about on the plain when the sun was getting low in the sky, was much impressed by the size of his shadow, and said to himself, "I had no idea I was so big.</seg>
<seg id="1762">一只狼在日落时漫步于平原上，看到自己的影子那么长，他得意洋洋地自言自语道：“我还不知道自己的身体居然有这么大。</seg>
<seg id="1763">Fancy my being afraid of a lion!</seg>
<seg id="1763">难以想象我竟然还怕一只狮子！</seg>
<seg id="1764">Why, I, not he, ought to be King of the beasts";</seg>
<seg id="1764">不，我不应该害怕他，我应该做百兽之王。”</seg>
<seg id="1765">and, heedless of danger, he strutted about as if there could be no doubt at all about it.</seg>
<seg id="1765">他沉醉于其中，忽视了身边的危险。</seg>
<seg id="1766">Just then a lion sprang upon him and began to devour him.</seg>
<seg id="1766">这时，一只狮子向他扑来，开始撕咬他。</seg>
<seg id="1767">"Alas," he cried, "had I not lost sight of the facts, I shouldn't have been ruined by my fancies."</seg>
<seg id="1767">“哎呀！”狼大声喊道，“若不是沉醉于虚幻之中，我就不会被自己的幻想毁了呀。”</seg>
<seg id="1768">THE PLOUGHMAN AND THE WOLF</seg>
<seg id="1768">农夫和狼</seg>
<seg id="1769">A Ploughman loosed his oxen from the plough, and led them away to the water to drink.</seg>
<seg id="1769">农夫松开牛脖子上挂着的牛轭，牵着它们到水边去喝水。</seg>
<seg id="1770">While he was absent a half-starved Wolf appeared on the scene, and went up to the plough and began chewing the leather straps attached to the yoke.</seg>
<seg id="1770">这时，一只饿得半死的狼出现了，他走到犁旁边，开始咀嚼牛轭上的皮套。</seg>
<seg id="1771">As he gnawed away desperately in the hope of satisfying his craving for food, he somehow got entangled in the harness, and, taking fright, struggled to get free, tugging at the traces as if he would drag the plough along with him.</seg>
<seg id="1771">为了能够填饱肚子，狼拼命地啃那皮套，不知不觉就将头伸进了牛轭中，惊慌中的狼拼命挣扎着想重获自由，结果只好拉着犁跑，就像要去田里耕地似的。</seg>
<seg id="1772">Just then the Ploughman came back, and seeing what was happening, he cried, "Ah, you old rascal, I wish you would give up thieving for good and take to honest work instead."</seg>
<seg id="1772">恰巧农夫回来了，看到眼前发生的一切，便说：“啊，你这个可恶的东西，但愿你弃恶从善，干点正经事。”</seg>
<seg id="1773">MERCURY AND THE MAN BITTEN BY AN ANT</seg>
<seg id="1773">墨丘利和被蚂蚁所咬的人</seg>
<seg id="1774">A Man once saw a ship go down with all its crew, and commented severely on the injustice of the gods.</seg>
<seg id="1774">一个人在海边看见一艘船遇难，船上的人全都被淹死了，他便愤愤不平地抱怨上帝。</seg>
<seg id="1775">"They care nothing for a man's character," said he, "but let the good and the bad go to their deaths together."</seg>
<seg id="1775">“唉，上帝都不考虑一个人的品格，”他说，“竟然让好人和坏人一起死了。”</seg>
<seg id="1776">There was an ant-heap close by where he was standing, and, just as he spoke, he was bitten in the foot by an Ant.</seg>
<seg id="1776">这个人当时正站在一个蚂蚁窝旁，当他说这番话时，被爬到脚上的一只蚂蚁咬了一口。</seg>
<seg id="1777">Turning in a temper to the ant-heap he stamped upon it and crushed hundreds of unoffending ants.</seg>
<seg id="1777">他立刻冲着身旁的蚂蚁窝撒起火来，碾死了许多并没有伤害他的蚂蚁。</seg>
<seg id="1778">Suddenly Mercury appeared, and belaboured him with his staff, saying as he did so, "You villain, where's your nice sense of justice now?"</seg>
<seg id="1778">这时，墨丘利出现了，用棍棒痛打了他一顿，而且还重复着那人刚才所说的话：“你这个恶棍，现在你的正义感又去哪里了呢？”</seg>
<seg id="1779">THE WILY LION</seg>
<seg id="1779">狡猾的狮子</seg>
<seg id="1780">A Lion watched a fat Bull feeding in a meadow, and his mouth watered when he thought of the royal feast he would make, but he did not dare to attack him, for he was afraid of his sharp horns.</seg>
<seg id="1780">一只狮子看见一头肥壮的公牛正在吃草，一想到这是一顿美味佳肴，口水禁不住就流了出来，可是他又畏惧公牛的尖角，不敢轻易发起进攻。</seg>
<seg id="1781">Hunger, however, presently compelled him to do something:</seg>
<seg id="1781">然而，饥饿促使他一定要做点什么。</seg>
<seg id="1782">and as the use of force did not promise success, he determined to resort to artifice.</seg>
<seg id="1782">单凭武力，他肯定无法成功，于是狮子决定用诡计智取。</seg>
<seg id="1783">Going up to the Bull in friendly fashion, he said to him, "I cannot help saying how much I admire your magnificent figure.</seg>
<seg id="1783">他带着友好的姿态走到公牛身旁，对公牛说：“简直无法用语言来表达我对您那魔鬼般的身材有多羡慕，</seg>
<seg id="1784">What a fine head!</seg>
<seg id="1784">这是多么漂亮的头呀，</seg>
<seg id="1785">What powerful shoulders and thighs!</seg>
<seg id="1785">多么宽阔结实的肩膀和大腿呀！</seg>
<seg id="1786">But, my dear friend, what in the world makes you wear those ugly horns?</seg>
<seg id="1786">不过，亲爱的朋友，究竟是什么让你戴着这两只奇丑无比的角呢？</seg>
<seg id="1787">You must find them as awkward as they are unsightly.</seg>
<seg id="1787">你一定也发现了，它们又笨拙又丑陋。</seg>
<seg id="1788">Believe me, you would do much better without them."</seg>
<seg id="1788">相信我，若是没有了这两只角，你肯定会更好。”</seg>
<seg id="1789">The Bull was foolish enough to be persuaded by this flattery to have his horns cut off;</seg>
<seg id="1789">公牛也够蠢的，竟然被这番恭维所说服，把自己的两只角折断了，</seg>
<seg id="1790">and, having now lost his only means of defence, fell an easy prey to the Lion.</seg>
<seg id="1790">刚刚失去用以防卫的武器，公牛就轻易地被狮子虏获了。</seg>
<seg id="1791">THE PARROT AND THE CAT</seg>
<seg id="1791">鹦鹉和猫</seg>
<seg id="1792">A Man once bought a Parrot and gave it the run of his house.</seg>
<seg id="1792">从前，有个人买了一只鹦鹉，让它在房子里自由自在地生活。</seg>
<seg id="1793">It revelled in its liberty, and presently flew up on to the mantelpiece and screamed away to its heart's content.</seg>
<seg id="1793">这只鹦鹉欣喜若狂，高兴地飞上了壁炉架，尽情地叫着。</seg>
<seg id="1794">The noise disturbed the Cat, who was asleep on the hearthrug.</seg>
<seg id="1794">一只猫正在壁炉前的地毯上睡觉，鹦鹉的吵闹声惊扰了她。</seg>
<seg id="1795">Looking up at the intruder, she said, "Who may you be, and where have you come from?"</seg>
<seg id="1795">看着这个刚来的入侵者，猫问道：“你是谁，从哪里来的？”</seg>
<seg id="1796">The Parrot replied, "Your master has just bought me and brought me home with him."</seg>
<seg id="1796">鹦鹉回答道：“你的主人刚刚买了我，带我来到这个房子里。”</seg>
<seg id="1797">"You impudent bird," said the Cat, "how dare you, a newcomer, make a noise like that?</seg>
<seg id="1797">“你这个放肆无礼的家伙，”猫说，“怎么刚到这里就这么吵闹呢？</seg>
<seg id="1798">Why, I was born here, and have lived here all my life, and yet, if I venture to mew, they throw things at me and chase me all over the place."</seg>
<seg id="1798">我可是在这里出生的，而且一直住在这个家里。但即便如此，如果我冒险喵喵地叫几声，主人就会朝我扔东西，到处追着赶我出去。”</seg>
<seg id="1799">"Look here, mistress," said the Parrot, "you just hold your tongue.</seg>
<seg id="1799">鹦鹉回答说：“喂，你最好赶快闭上嘴。</seg>
<seg id="1800">My voice they delight in; but yours--yours is a perfect nuisance."</seg>
<seg id="1800">我的声音多么悦耳动听呀，他们可都喜欢；而你的叫声，实在是一种噪音。”</seg>
<seg id="1801">THE STAG AND THE LION</seg>
<seg id="1801">雄鹿和狮子</seg>
<seg id="1802">A Stag was chased by the hounds, and took refuge in a cave, where he hoped to be safe from his pursuers.</seg>
<seg id="1802">有只鹿受到了猎犬的追捕，拼命地逃进一个洞里寻求庇护。他希望这是一个安全的地方，可以躲避猎犬。</seg>
<seg id="1803">Unfortunately the cave contained a Lion, to whom he fell an easy prey.</seg>
<seg id="1803">不幸的是，这个洞里有一只狮子，轻易地就抓获了鹿。</seg>
<seg id="1804">"Unhappy that I am," he cried, "I am saved from the power of the dogs only to fall into the clutches of a Lion."</seg>
<seg id="1804">鹿临死之前说：“我真是倒霉，刚脱离了猎犬的追捕，马上又掉进了狮子的大口。”</seg>
<seg id="1805">Out of the frying-pan into the fire.</seg>
<seg id="1805">刚从油锅里出来，又掉进了火坑。</seg>
<seg id="1806">THE IMPOSTOR</seg>
<seg id="1806">说谎的人</seg>
<seg id="1807">A certain man fell ill, and, being in a very bad way, he made a vow that he would sacrifice a hundred oxen to the gods if they would grant him a return to health.</seg>
<seg id="1807">有个人生了病，状况非常严重，他向众神发誓，如果能恢复健康，他一定会供奉一百头牛给众神。</seg>
<seg id="1808">Wishing to see how he would keep his vow, they caused him to recover in a short time.</seg>
<seg id="1808">众神想要看看他是否能遵守诺言，很快便让他痊愈了。</seg>
<seg id="1809">Now, he hadn't an ox in the world, so he made a hundred little oxen out of tallow and offered them up on an altar, at the same time saying, "Ye gods, I call you to witness that I have discharged my vow."</seg>
<seg id="1809">他其实根本没有一百头牛，于是就用酥油做成了一百头小牛，放到供台上供奉给众神，同时嘴里还说着：“众神灵，我请你们来见证，我已经还清了自己许下的愿。”</seg>
<seg id="1810">The gods determined to be even with him, so they sent him a dream, in which he was bidden to go to the sea-shore and fetch a hundred crowns which he was to find there.</seg>
<seg id="1810">众神决定要报复他，便带他进入了一个梦境。在梦里，他被命令到海边去，在那里他将找到一百个银元。</seg>
<seg id="1811">Hastening in great excitement to the shore, he fell in with a band of robbers, who seized him and carried him off to sell as a slave: and when they sold him a hundred crowns was the sum he fetched.</seg>
<seg id="1811">他带着激动的心情赶忙跑到海边，可是却遇上了一群强盗，强盗抓住他并将他卖了去当奴隶，而卖他所得的钱正好是一百个银元，也就是他要取的总数目。</seg>
<seg id="1812">Do not promise more than you can perform.</seg>
<seg id="1812">不要许下力所不能及的愿。</seg>
<seg id="1813">THE DOGS AND THE HIDES</seg>
<seg id="1813">狗和牛皮</seg>
<seg id="1814">Once upon a time a number of Dogs, who were famished with hunger, saw some Hides steeping in a river, but couldn't get at them because the water was too deep.</seg>
<seg id="1814">从前，有几条饥肠辘辘的狗，看见河里浸泡着一张牛皮，但是由于水太深，他们无法拿到那张皮。</seg>
<seg id="1815">So they put their heads together, and decided to drink away at the river till it was shallow enough for them to reach the Hides.</seg>
<seg id="1815">于是，他们合计着喝掉河里的水，这样就可以趁水浅一些时，过去拿那张牛皮了。</seg>
<seg id="1816">But long before that happened they burst themselves with drinking.</seg>
<seg id="1816">然而，还没等到去拿兽皮，他们的肚皮早已被河水胀破了。</seg>
<seg id="1817">THE LION, THE FOX, AND THE ASS</seg>
<seg id="1817">狮子、狐狸和驴</seg>
<seg id="1818">A Lion, a Fox, and an Ass went out hunting together.</seg>
<seg id="1818">狮子、狐狸和驴一起外出打猎。</seg>
<seg id="1819">They had soon taken a large booty, which the Lion requested the Ass to divide between them.</seg>
<seg id="1819">没过多久，他们就虏获了许多战利品，狮子命令驴在其面前分猎物。</seg>
<seg id="1820">The Ass divided it all into three equal parts, and modestly begged the others to take their choice;</seg>
<seg id="1820">驴将所有猎物平均分成三份，然后谦和地请狮子和狐狸先挑选自己的那一份。</seg>
<seg id="1821">at which the Lion, bursting with fury, sprang upon the Ass and tore him to pieces.</seg>
<seg id="1821">这时，狮子勃然大怒，猛扑过去，撕碎了驴。</seg>
<seg id="1822">Then, glaring at the Fox, he bade him make a fresh division.</seg>
<seg id="1822">接着，狮子又盯上了狐狸，命令他来重新分赃。</seg>
<seg id="1823">The Fox gathered almost the whole in one great heap for the Lion's share, leaving only the smallest possible morsel for himself.</seg>
<seg id="1823">狐狸把所有的猎物都堆在一起，然后请狮子来拿，只留下一点点东西给自己。</seg>
<seg id="1824">"My dear friend," said the Lion, "how did you get the knack of it so well?"</seg>
<seg id="1824">“我的好朋友，”狮子说，“你怎么学到的这个窍门呀？”</seg>
<seg id="1825">The Fox replied, "Me?</seg>
<seg id="1825">狐狸回答说：</seg>
<seg id="1826">Oh, I took a lesson from the Ass."</seg>
<seg id="1826">“我是从驴那里得到了教训。”</seg>
<seg id="1827">Happy is he who learns from the misfortunes of others.</seg>
<seg id="1827">你若懂得从他人的不幸中汲取教训，就能获得幸福。</seg>
<seg id="1828">THE FOWLER, THE PARTRIDGE, AND THE COCK</seg>
<seg id="1828">捕鸟人、鹧鸪和公鸡</seg>
<seg id="1829">One day, as a Fowler was sitting down to a scanty supper of herbs and bread, a friend dropped in unexpectedly.</seg>
<seg id="1829">有一天，当捕鸟人正坐在餐桌边吃着仅有香草和面包的晚餐时，一个朋友不期而至。</seg>
<seg id="1830">The larder was empty;</seg>
<seg id="1830">食品柜已经空了，</seg>
<seg id="1831">so he went out and caught a tame Partridge, which he kept as a decoy, and was about to wring her neck when she cried, "Surely you won't kill me?</seg>
<seg id="1831">于是捕鸟人跑出去捉那只驯养的鹧鸪，它可是一直被当做诱饵留下来的。就在捕鸟人要拧断她的脖子时，鹧鸪大喊道：“你确定要杀了我吗？</seg>
<seg id="1832">Why, what will you do without me next time you go fowling?</seg>
<seg id="1832">为什么，要是没有我，你下次捕鸟时该怎么办呢？</seg>
<seg id="1833">How will you get the birds to come to your nets?"</seg>
<seg id="1833">你如何能吸引那些鸟儿走到你的网里来呢？”</seg>
<seg id="1834">He let her go at this, and went to his hen-house, where he had a plump young Cock.</seg>
<seg id="1834">听了这番话，捕鸟人就放了鹧鸪，走到鸡舍那边，准备去捉那只胖乎乎的小公鸡。</seg>
<seg id="1835">When the Cock saw what he was after, he too pleaded for his life, and said, "If you kill me, how will you know the time of night?</seg>
<seg id="1835">公鸡看到自己将要成为下一个被杀的目标，也求主人饶命，并且说：“如果你杀了我，怎么能知道夜晚的时间呢？</seg>
<seg id="1836">and who will wake you up in the morning when it is time to get to work?"</seg>
<seg id="1836">谁能在清晨唤醒你，到时候该去干活了呢？”</seg>
<seg id="1837">The Fowler, however, replied, "You are useful for telling the time, I know;</seg>
<seg id="1837">然而，捕鸟人却回答说：“我知道，你的确能告诉我时间，</seg>
<seg id="1838">but, for all that, I can't send my friend supperless to bed."</seg>
<seg id="1838">尽管如此，我也不能让朋友饿着肚子去睡觉呀。”</seg>
<seg id="1839">And therewith he caught him and wrung his neck.</seg>
<seg id="1839">随后，他便捉住公鸡，拧断了它的脖子。</seg>
<seg id="1840">THE GNAT AND THE LION</seg>
<seg id="1840">蚊子和狮子</seg>
<seg id="1841">A Gnat once went up to a Lion and said, "I am not in the least afraid of you:</seg>
<seg id="1841">有只蚊子飞到狮子那里，说：“我一点儿也不害怕你，</seg>
<seg id="1842">I don't even allow that you are a match for me in strength.</seg>
<seg id="1842">我甚至都不承认你我力量相当。</seg>
<seg id="1843">What does your strength amount to after all?</seg>
<seg id="1843">你的力量究竟有多大？</seg>
<seg id="1844">That you can scratch with your claws and bite with your teeth--just like a woman in a temper--and nothing more.</seg>
<seg id="1844">你只会用爪子抓、用牙齿咬，就像一个发脾气的女人一样，除此之外，就没有什么了。</seg>
<seg id="1845">But I'm stronger than you:</seg>
<seg id="1845">可是，我却比你厉害得多。</seg>
<seg id="1846">if you don't believe it, let us fight and see."</seg>
<seg id="1846">若是你不相信，不妨来比试比试。”</seg>
<seg id="1847">So saying, the Gnat sounded his horn, and darted in and bit the Lion on the nose.</seg>
<seg id="1847">蚊子嗡嗡地吹着小喇叭，猛冲上前，在狮子的鼻子上咬了一口。</seg>
<seg id="1848">When the Lion felt the sting, in his haste to crush him he scratched his nose badly, and made it bleed, but failed altogether to hurt the Gnat, which buzzed off in triumph, elated by its victory.</seg>
<seg id="1848">狮子感觉到被蚊子叮了一口，马上就用爪子去抓，结果却划伤了自己的鼻子，流了好多血。狮子最终没能伤害到蚊子。于是，蚊子又嗡嗡叫着，兴高采烈地凯旋而归。</seg>
<seg id="1849">Presently, however, it got entangled in a spider's web, and was caught and eaten by the spider, thus falling a prey to an insignificant insect after having triumphed over the King of the Beasts.</seg>
<seg id="1849">然而，他很快就陷入了蜘蛛的网中，被一只蜘蛛抓住吃了，在战胜了百兽之王后，却被一只不起眼的蜘蛛消灭了。</seg>
<seg id="1850">THE FARMER AND HIS DOGS</seg>
<seg id="1850">农场主和他的狗</seg>
<seg id="1851">A Farmer was snowed up in his farmstead by a severe storm, and was unable to go out and procure provisions for himself and his family.</seg>
<seg id="1851">一个农夫因持续而来的风暴被困在自己的农场里，无法外出为自己和家人寻获食物。</seg>
<seg id="1852">So he first killed his sheep and used them for food;</seg>
<seg id="1852">迫于无奈，他杀死了自己的绵羊来充饥。</seg>
<seg id="1853">then, as the storm still continued, he killed his goats;</seg>
<seg id="1853">可是，风暴依然持续不停，继而又杀死山羊。</seg>
<seg id="1854">and, last of all, as the weather showed no signs of improving, he was compelled to kill his oxen and eat them.</seg>
<seg id="1854">最后，因为风暴丝毫没有减弱的意思，他又被迫杀死了自己的牛来填饱肚子。</seg>
<seg id="1855">When his Dogs saw the various animals being killed and eaten in turn, they said to one another, "We had better get out of this or we shall be the next to go!"</seg>
<seg id="1855">那些狗看到不同的动物依次被杀、被吃掉后，便相互诉说：“我们最好快点离开这里，不然就会成为下一个被杀的对象！”</seg>
<seg id="1856">THE EAGLE AND THE FOX</seg>
<seg id="1856">老鹰和狐狸</seg>
<seg id="1857">An Eagle and a Fox became great friends and determined to live near one another:</seg>
<seg id="1857">一只鹰和一只狐狸成为了好朋友，并决定比邻而居，</seg>
<seg id="1858">they thought that the more they saw of each other the better friends they would be.</seg>
<seg id="1858">他们以为经常能见到对方，就会维持更好的友谊。</seg>
<seg id="1859">So the Eagle built a nest at the top of a high tree, while the Fox settled in a thicket at the foot of it and produced a litter of cubs.</seg>
<seg id="1859">于是，老鹰在一棵大树的顶端建巢育子，而狐狸则走进树下的灌木丛中扎窝，并在那里生儿育女。</seg>
<seg id="1860">One day the Fox went out foraging for food, and the Eagle, who also wanted food for her young, flew down into the thicket, caught up the Fox's cubs, and carried them up into the tree for a meal for herself and her family.</seg>
<seg id="1860">有一天，狐狸出去觅食，老鹰正好也想给小鹰寻找食物，他便飞入灌木丛中，抓起狐狸的幼崽，飞上高枝，与雏鹰一起饱餐了一顿。</seg>
<seg id="1861">When the Fox came back, and found out what had happened, she was not so much sorry for the loss of her cubs as furious because she couldn't get at the Eagle and pay her out for her treachery.</seg>
<seg id="1861">待狐狸回来后，发现了老鹰的所作所为，她既为儿女的亡命而悲痛，又因自己无法到老鹰的巢穴吃掉她的幼崽报仇而愤怒。</seg>
<seg id="1862">So she sat down not far off and cursed her.</seg>
<seg id="1862">因此，她只好坐在不远的地方诅咒敌人。</seg>
<seg id="1863">But it wasn't long before she had her revenge.</seg>
<seg id="1863">没过多久，她就报了仇。</seg>
<seg id="1864">Some villagers happened to be sacrificing a goat on a neighbouring altar, and the Eagle flew down and carried off a piece of burning flesh to her nest.</seg>
<seg id="1864">一些村民碰巧在旁边的祭坛杀羊祭神，老鹰飞下来，从祭坛上抓起一块还带着火苗的羊肉，带回到自己的巢里。</seg>
<seg id="1865">There was a strong wind blowing, and the nest caught fire, with the result that her fledglings fell half-roasted to the ground.</seg>
<seg id="1865">这时，一阵狂风吹来，鹰巢立刻起火了，结果，那些快要被烧焦了的小雏鹰也一并掉到了地上。</seg>
<seg id="1866">Then the Fox ran to the spot and devoured them in full sight of the Eagle.</seg>
<seg id="1866">接着，狐狸便跑了过去，在老鹰的眼前，吃掉了那些小鹰。</seg>
<seg id="1867">False faith may escape human punishment, but cannot escape the divine.</seg>
<seg id="1867">带有欺骗性的忠诚或许能逃过人的惩罚，但却逃不过神的惩罚。</seg>
<seg id="1868">THE BUTCHER AND HIS CUSTOMERS</seg>
<seg id="1868">屠夫和他的顾客</seg>
<seg id="1869">Two Men were buying meat at a Butcher's stall in the market-place, and, while the Butcher's back was turned for a moment, one of them snatched up a joint and hastily thrust it under the other's cloak, where it could not be seen.</seg>
<seg id="1869">两个人正在市场里屠户的摊位上买肉，屠夫刚一转身背向他们，其中一人便抓起一块腱子肉，迅速放进另一人的斗篷里，谁也没看到他的举动。</seg>
<seg id="1870">When the Butcher turned round, he missed the meat at once, and charged them with having stolen it:</seg>
<seg id="1870">待屠夫转过身来，立刻注意到少了一块肉，便指控他们偷了肉。</seg>
<seg id="1871">but the one who had taken it said he hadn't got it, and the one who had got it said he hadn't taken it.</seg>
<seg id="1871">但是，拿了肉的那个人说自己没有偷，而得到肉的那个人也说自己没有拿。</seg>
<seg id="1872">The Butcher felt sure they were deceiving him, but he only said, "You may cheat me with your lying, but you can't cheat the gods, and they won't let you off so lightly."</seg>
<seg id="1872">屠夫确信他们是在欺骗自己，但仅仅说了一句话：“你可以用谎言来欺骗我，但却骗不了神，他们不会这么轻易放过你的。”</seg>
<seg id="1873">Prevarication often amounts to perjury.</seg>
<seg id="1873">相互推诿等同于欺骗。</seg>
<seg id="1874">HERCULES AND MINERVA</seg>
<seg id="1874">赫拉克勒斯和密涅瓦</seg>
<seg id="1875">Hercules was once travelling along a narrow road when he saw lying on the ground in front of him what appeared to be an apple, and as he passed he stamped upon it with his heel.</seg>
<seg id="1875">赫拉克勒斯有一次经过一条狭窄的路时，见到前面的地上有一个类似苹果的东西，走到那里时，他便用脚去踩它。</seg>
<seg id="1876">To his astonishment, instead of being crushed it doubled in size;</seg>
<seg id="1876">让他惊讶的是，那个东西不但没有碎，反而成倍增大了。</seg>
<seg id="1877">and, on his attacking it again and smiting it with his club, it swelled up to an enormous size and blocked up the whole road.</seg>
<seg id="1877">他又去踩了一下，而且还用大木棒去打它。结果，那个东西迅速膨胀起来，堵住了整条路。</seg>
<seg id="1878">Upon this he dropped his club, and stood looking at it in amazement.</seg>
<seg id="1878">他扔下木棒，不知所措地站在那里盯着看。</seg>
<seg id="1879">Just then Minerva appeared, and said to him, "Leave it alone, my friend;</seg>
<seg id="1879">这时，密涅瓦出现了，对他说：“朋友，随他去吧，</seg>
<seg id="1880">that which you see before you is the apple of discord:</seg>
<seg id="1880">你眼前看到的正是那个祸根。</seg>
<seg id="1881">if you do not meddle with it, it remains small as it was at first, but if you resort to violence it swells into the thing you see."</seg>
<seg id="1881">如果你不去理它，它就会依然小如苹果一样待在原地，可是，如果你采用暴力与之抗衡，它就会变成你看到的这个样子了。”</seg>
<seg id="1882">THE FOX WHO SERVED A LION</seg>
<seg id="1882">为狮子服务的狐狸</seg>
<seg id="1883">A Lion had a Fox to attend on him, and whenever they went hunting the Fox found the prey and the Lion fell upon it and killed it, and then they divided it between them in certain proportions.</seg>
<seg id="1883">狮子身边有一只狐狸在服侍他，每当出去打猎时，狐狸负责寻找猎物，而狮子则扑上去杀死猎物，之后他们按照一定比例瓜分猎物。</seg>
<seg id="1884">But the Lion always got a very large share, and the Fox a very small one, which didn't please the latter at all;</seg>
<seg id="1884">但狮子总会取走大部分猎物，而狐狸只能得到小小的一份，这让狐狸很不高兴。</seg>
<seg id="1885">so he determined to set up on his own account.</seg>
<seg id="1885">于是，狐狸决心自己去捕猎。</seg>
<seg id="1886">He began by trying to steal a lamb from a flock of sheep: but the shepherd saw him and set his dogs on him.</seg>
<seg id="1886">起初，他尝试着从羊群中偷取羔羊，但是牧羊人一见到狐狸，便放狗追他。</seg>
<seg id="1887">The hunter was now the hunted, and was very soon caught and despatched by the dogs.</seg>
<seg id="1887">原来的捕猎者，现在反而变成被猎者，而且狐狸很快就被狗捉住杀死了。</seg>
<seg id="1888">Better servitude with safety than freedom with danger.</seg>
<seg id="1888">安全的奴役更胜于有危险的自由。</seg>
<seg id="1889">THE QUACK DOCTOR</seg>
<seg id="1889">江湖郎中</seg>
<seg id="1890">A certain man fell sick and took to his bed.</seg>
<seg id="1890">从前，有一个人生病了，且卧床不起。</seg>
<seg id="1891">He consulted a number of doctors from time to time, and they all, with one exception, told him that his life was in no immediate danger, but that his illness would probably last a considerable time.</seg>
<seg id="1891">他咨询了很多医生，除了一个医生之外，其他人都说这病没有什么危险，但却需要持续一段时间。</seg>
<seg id="1892">The one who took a different view of his case, who was also the last to be consulted, bade him prepare for the worst:</seg>
<seg id="1892">那个持相反意见的医生，也是他最后咨询的一个医生，命令他做最坏的打算。</seg>
<seg id="1893">"You have not twenty-four hours to live," said he, "and I fear I can do nothing."</seg>
<seg id="1893">“你已经活不过明天了，”那人说，“恐怕我也帮不上什么忙。”</seg>
<seg id="1894">As it turned out, however, he was quite wrong;</seg>
<seg id="1894">然而，事实证明那个医生的确是错了。</seg>
<seg id="1895">for at the end of a few days the sick man quitted his bed and took a walk abroad, looking, it is true, as pale as a ghost.</seg>
<seg id="1895">过了些日子，尽管病人的脸色依然苍白，可他能够下床走动了。</seg>
<seg id="1896">In the course of his walk he met the Doctor who had prophesied his death.</seg>
<seg id="1896">在路上，他又遇见了那个宣判他死期将至的医生。</seg>
<seg id="1897">"Dear me," said the latter, "how do you do?</seg>
<seg id="1897">医生问他：“你好，感觉如何？</seg>
<seg id="1898">You are fresh from the other world, no doubt.</seg>
<seg id="1898">不用问，你从另一个世界回来了。</seg>
<seg id="1899">Pray, how are our departed friends getting on there?"</seg>
<seg id="1899">拜托，那些死去的朋友怎么样？”</seg>
<seg id="1900">"Most comfortably," replied the other, "for they have drunk the water of oblivion, and have forgotten all the troubles of life.</seg>
<seg id="1900">“非常舒服，”病人回答说，“因为他们喝了忘情水，忘掉了生命中的所有烦恼。</seg>
<seg id="1901">By the way, just before I left, the authorities were making arrangements to prosecute all the doctors, because they won't let sick men die in the course of nature, but use their arts to keep them alive.</seg>
<seg id="1901">顺便一提，就在我离开前，死神正准备控诉所有医生，因为他们没让病人自然死亡，而是利用各种方式来挽救其生命。</seg>
<seg id="1902">They were going to charge you along with the rest, till I assured them that you were no doctor, but a mere impostor."</seg>
<seg id="1902">原本你也在其中，但是我恳求他们放了你，因为你不是一个真正的医生，而仅仅是个江湖郎中。”</seg>
<seg id="1903">THE LION, THE WOLF, AND THE FOX</seg>
<seg id="1903">狮子、狼和狐狸</seg>
<seg id="1904">A Lion, infirm with age, lay sick in his den, and all the beasts of the forest came to inquire after his health with the exception of the Fox.</seg>
<seg id="1904">一只上了年纪的狮子，生病躺在自己的洞里。除了狐狸外，森林里的其他动物都来问候狮子。</seg>
<seg id="1905">The Wolf thought this was a good opportunity for paying off old scores against the Fox, so he called the attention of the Lion to his absence, and said, "You see, sire, that we have all come to see how you are except the Fox, who hasn't come near you, and doesn't care whether you are well or ill."</seg>
<seg id="1905">狼心想，这正是一个好机会，可以和狐狸算算旧账了。于是，他便提醒狮子注意到狐狸的缺席，并且说：“您看，大王，我们所有动物都来看望您，可狐狸却胆大包天，竟然不来问候。他根本都不关心您的健康状况是好是坏。”</seg>
<seg id="1906">Just then the Fox came in and heard the last words of the Wolf.</seg>
<seg id="1906">正在此时，狐狸进来了，听到了狼所说的最后一句话。</seg>
<seg id="1907">The Lion roared at him in deep displeasure, but he begged to be allowed to explain his absence, and said, "Not one of them cares for you so much as I, sire, for all the time I have been going round to the doctors and trying to find a cure for your illness."</seg>
<seg id="1907">狮子立刻冲狐狸怒吼起来，狐狸马上请求让他解释一下缺席的原因。狐狸说：“他们谁也没有我这样关心您，我一直在四处奔走，遍访名医，为您寻找治病的妙方呢！”</seg>
<seg id="1908">"And may I ask if you have found one?" said the Lion.</seg>
<seg id="1908">“我问一下，你找到了什么？”狮子说。</seg>
<seg id="1909">"I have, sire," said the Fox, "and it is this: you must flay a Wolf and wrap yourself in his skin while it is still warm."</seg>
<seg id="1909">“我找到了一个灵丹妙方，那就是——您必须活剥了狼，趁着它的皮还有体温时，赶紧披在身上。”</seg>
<seg id="1910">The Lion accordingly turned to the Wolf and struck him dead with one blow of his paw, in order to try the Fox's prescription;</seg>
<seg id="1910">为了试一下狐狸的偏方，狮子立刻转向狼，用一只爪子掐死了狼，</seg>
<seg id="1911">but the Fox laughed and said to himself, "That's what comes of stirring up ill-will."</seg>
<seg id="1911">而狐狸则笑着自言自语道：“这可是你自己激发出来的敌意。”</seg>
<seg id="1912">HERCULES AND PLUTUS</seg>
<seg id="1912">赫拉克勒斯和财神</seg>
<seg id="1913">When Hercules was received among the gods and was entertained at a banquet by Jupiter, he responded courteously to the greetings of all with the exception of Plutus, the god of wealth.</seg>
<seg id="1913">赫拉克勒斯被众神接纳为神以后，朱庇特为他设宴庆贺。宴会上，赫拉克勒斯热情友好地向众神们一一问好，唯独财神普路托斯除外。</seg>
<seg id="1914">When Plutus approached him, he cast his eyes upon the ground, and turned away and pretended not to see him.</seg>
<seg id="1914">当财神向他走去时，他却低下头盯着地面看，然后转身走开了，假装没有看到他。</seg>
<seg id="1915">Jupiter was surprised at this conduct on his part, and asked why, after having been so cordial with all the other gods, he had behaved like that to Plutus.</seg>
<seg id="1915">朱庇特看到他的举动十分惊讶，便问他为什么与其他神都能高兴地打招呼，唯独对财神普路托斯却另眼相看。</seg>
<seg id="1916">"Sire," said Hercules, "I do not like Plutus, and I will tell you why.</seg>
<seg id="1916">赫拉克勒斯回答说：“陛下，我不喜欢财神普路托斯，我会告诉您原因的。</seg>
<seg id="1917">When we were on earth together I always noticed that he was to be found in the company of scoundrels."</seg>
<seg id="1917">当我们俩都在人间时，总见到他与坏人在一起。”</seg>
<seg id="1918">THE FOX AND THE LEOPARD</seg>
<seg id="1918">狐狸与豹</seg>
<seg id="1919">A Fox and a Leopard were disputing about their looks, and each claimed to be the more handsome of the two.</seg>
<seg id="1919">一只狐狸和一只豹正在争论自己的外表，争着吹嘘自己是更俊朗的那一个。</seg>
<seg id="1920">The Leopard said, "Look at my smart coat; you have nothing to match that."</seg>
<seg id="1920">豹说：“看看我这漂亮的外套，你可没有什么能与之媲美的。”</seg>
<seg id="1921">But the Fox replied, "Your coat may be smart, but my wits are smarter still."</seg>
<seg id="1921">可是，狐狸却说：“你的外表或许比较漂亮，但我的智慧却更胜过你。”</seg>
<seg id="1922">THE FOX AND THE HEDGEHOG</seg>
<seg id="1922">狐狸与刺猬</seg>
<seg id="1923">A Fox, in swimming across a rapid river, was swept away by the current and carried a long way downstream in spite of his struggles, until at last, bruised and exhausted, he managed to scramble on to dry ground from a backwater.</seg>
<seg id="1923">一只狐狸正在渡过一条水流湍急的河，尽管他努力挣扎着，可依然被水流冲到了远处的河下游。后来，遍体鳞伤的他精疲力竭，想尽一切办法从水中爬回到了一块干燥的土地上，躺在那里一动也不能动。</seg>
<seg id="1924">As he lay there unable to move, a swarm of horseflies settled on him and sucked his blood undisturbed, for he was too weak even to shake them off.</seg>
<seg id="1924">这时，一群饥饿的马蝇叮满了他的全身，泰然自若地吮吸着他的血。因为狐狸实在太虚弱，根本无法抖落这些马蝇。</seg>
<seg id="1925">A Hedgehog saw him, and asked if he should brush away the flies that were tormenting him;</seg>
<seg id="1925">一只刺猬看见了他，并问他是否应该赶走这些害他的马蝇。</seg>
<seg id="1926">but the Fox replied, "Oh, please, no, not on any account, for these flies have sucked their fill and are taking very little from me now;</seg>
<seg id="1926">但是，狐狸却回答说：“不用啦，坚决不要打扰他们，因为这些马蝇已经吃饱，不再叮咬我了；</seg>
<seg id="1927">but, if you drive them off, another swarm of hungry ones will come and suck all the blood I have left, and leave me without a drop in my veins."</seg>
<seg id="1927">假如你把它们都赶走了，另外一群饥饿的马蝇就会过来，继续吸取我体内剩余的血，这样就会吸干血管里的血。”</seg>
<seg id="1928">THE CROW AND THE RAVEN</seg>
<seg id="1928">乌鸦与渡鸦</seg>
<seg id="1929">A Crow became very jealous of a Raven, because the latter was regarded by men as a bird of omen which foretold the future, and was accordingly held in great respect by them.</seg>
<seg id="1929">一只乌鸦非常妒忌渡鸦，因为渡鸦被人类当做一种能预测未来的神鸟，故而得到了人类的尊敬。</seg>
<seg id="1930">She was very anxious to get the same sort of reputation herself;</seg>
<seg id="1930">乌鸦十分羡慕，也想得到同样的声望。</seg>
<seg id="1931">and, one day, seeing some travellers approaching, she flew on to a branch of a tree at the roadside and cawed as loud as she could.</seg>
<seg id="1931">有一天，看见几个行人路过，她便飞到路边的一棵树上，用力地大声叫了起来。</seg>
<seg id="1932">The travellers were in some dismay at the sound, for they feared it might be a bad omen;</seg>
<seg id="1932">听到乌鸦的声音，行人都很郁闷，他们担心这是一个不好的预兆。</seg>
<seg id="1933">till one of them, spying the Crow, said to his companions, "It's all right, my friends, we can go on without fear, for it's only a crow and that means nothing."</seg>
<seg id="1933">其中一个人看到了乌鸦，就对同伴说：“没事了，朋友们，我们可以不用担心了，因为这是一只乌鸦，没什么特别的。”</seg>
<seg id="1934">Those who pretend to be something they are not only make themselves ridiculous.</seg>
<seg id="1934">假装成位高权重之流的人，只会让自己变得荒谬可笑。</seg>
<seg id="1935">THE WITCH</seg>
<seg id="1935">女巫</seg>
<seg id="1936">A Witch professed to be able to avert the anger of the gods by means of charms, of which she alone possessed the secret;</seg>
<seg id="1936">有个女巫声称自己能用某种方式使神灵息怒，只有她才拥有这个秘诀。</seg>
<seg id="1937">and she drove a brisk trade, and made a fat livelihood out of it.</seg>
<seg id="1937">她四处招摇撞骗，因此得到了不少酬金。</seg>
<seg id="1938">But certain persons accused her of black magic and carried her before the judges, and demanded that she should be put to death for dealings with the Devil.</seg>
<seg id="1938">但是，后来有人控告她乱用巫术，便将她送上了法庭，并要求将她处死，因为她与魔鬼打交道。</seg>
<seg id="1939">She was found guilty and condemned to death:</seg>
<seg id="1939">后来，她被定了罪，并判处了死刑。</seg>
<seg id="1940">and one of the judges said to her as she was leaving the dock, "You say you can avert the anger of the gods.</seg>
<seg id="1940">在离开被告席时，其中一个法官对她说：“你自称能平息神灵的愤怒，</seg>
<seg id="1941">How comes it, then, that you have failed to disarm the enmity of men?"</seg>
<seg id="1941">那么，现在为何连凡人的愤怒也平息不了呢？”</seg>
<seg id="1942">THE OLD MAN AND DEATH</seg>
<seg id="1942">老人与死神</seg>
<seg id="1943">An Old Man cut himself a bundle of faggots in a wood and started to carry them home.</seg>
<seg id="1943">有一个老人在森林里砍了一些柴，准备运回家。</seg>
<seg id="1944">He had a long way to go, and was tired out before he had got much more than half-way.</seg>
<seg id="1944">他十分吃力地挑着走了很远的路，还没走到一半，就已经累得走不动了。</seg>
<seg id="1945">Casting his burden on the ground, he called upon Death to come and release him from his life of toil.</seg>
<seg id="1945">他便将担子放在地上，要求死神快点来，让他尽快摆脱这个痛苦的生命。</seg>
<seg id="1946">The words were scarcely out of his mouth when, much to his dismay, Death stood before him and professed his readiness to serve him.</seg>
<seg id="1946">更令他沮丧的是，还没等话说出口，死神便站在他面前，声称已经准备好为他服务了。</seg>
<seg id="1947">He was almost frightened out of his wits, but he had enough presence of mind to stammer out, "Good sir, if you'd be so kind, pray help me up with my burden again."</seg>
<seg id="1947">老人几乎吓呆了，但却保持着沉着镇定，结结巴巴地说：“好人呀，你行行好，帮忙把那担子再放到我肩上吧。”</seg>
<seg id="1948">THE MISER</seg>
<seg id="1948">吝啬鬼</seg>
<seg id="1949">A Miser sold everything he had, and melted down his hoard of gold into a single lump, which he buried secretly in a field.</seg>
<seg id="1949">有一个守财奴变卖了所有家产，并将所有金器全部熔成了一个大金块，秘密埋在一个地方。</seg>
<seg id="1950">Every day he went to look at it, and would sometimes spend long hours gloating over his treasure.</seg>
<seg id="1950">他每天都会走过去看看，有时还会花很长时间得意洋洋地欣赏自己的宝藏。</seg>
<seg id="1951">One of his men noticed his frequent visits to the spot, and one day watched him and discovered his secret.</seg>
<seg id="1951">一个仆人注意到他经常去那个地方，便在某一天监视着他，发现了他的秘密。</seg>
<seg id="1952">Waiting his opportunity, he went one night and dug up the gold and stole it.</seg>
<seg id="1952">那人在一个夜晚伺机挖出了金块，并偷走了。</seg>
<seg id="1953">Next day the Miser visited the place as usual, and, finding his treasure gone, fell to tearing his hair and groaning over his loss.</seg>
<seg id="1953">第二天，当守财奴又像往常一样到那里来看宝贝时，发现自己的宝藏不翼而飞了，便捶胸顿足地痛哭起来。</seg>
<seg id="1954">In this condition he was seen by one of his neighbours, who asked him what his trouble was.</seg>
<seg id="1954">一个邻居见他如此悲痛，便问他遇上了什么麻烦。</seg>
<seg id="1955">The Miser told him of his misfortune;</seg>
<seg id="1955">守财奴告诉他自己的不幸，</seg>
<seg id="1956">but the other replied, "Don't take it so much to heart, my friend;</seg>
<seg id="1956">可是，邻居却说：“朋友，别太放在心上了，</seg>
<seg id="1957">put a brick into the hole, and take a look at it every day:</seg>
<seg id="1957">找一块石头放进洞里，然后每天都来看看它，</seg>
<seg id="1958">you won't be any worse off than before, for even when you had your gold it was of no earthly use to you."</seg>
<seg id="1958">只要你心里想着那是块金子，就不会再如此难过了。因为即使那是一块真的金子，对你来说也没什么用呀。”</seg>
<seg id="1959">THE FOXES AND THE RIVER</seg>
<seg id="1959">狐狸与河</seg>
<seg id="1960">A number of Foxes assembled on the bank of a river and wanted to drink;</seg>
<seg id="1960">一群狐狸聚集在河畔，想要喝河里的水。</seg>
<seg id="1961">but the current was so strong and the water looked so deep and dangerous that they didn't dare to do so, but stood near the edge encouraging one another not to be afraid.</seg>
<seg id="1961">但是，河里的水流很急，而河水似乎又很深、很危险，于是，他们都不敢下去喝水，只是站在河边，鼓动其他不害怕的狐狸下去喝水。</seg>
<seg id="1962">At last one of them, to shame the rest, and show how brave he was, said, "I am not a bit frightened!</seg>
<seg id="1962">其中有一只狐狸，嘲笑同伴们太胆小，为显示自己的勇敢，他说道：“我才不害怕呢！</seg>
<seg id="1963">See, I'll step right into the water!"</seg>
<seg id="1963">看吧，我马上就走进河里去！”</seg>
<seg id="1964">He had no sooner done so than the current swept him off his feet.</seg>
<seg id="1964">他刚步入河中，就被湍急的河水冲得站不稳脚跟。</seg>
<seg id="1965">When the others saw him being carried down-stream they cried, "Don't go and leave us!</seg>
<seg id="1965">眼看他就要被河水冲到下游去了，站在河边的其他狐狸冲他大喊：“别走呀，不要留下我们！</seg>
<seg id="1966">Come back and show us where we too can drink with safety."</seg>
<seg id="1966">快回来，告诉我们从哪里可以安全地下去喝水。”</seg>
<seg id="1967">But he replied, "I'm afraid I can't yet:</seg>
<seg id="1967">然而，被水冲走的狐狸却回答说：“恐怕我不能回去了，</seg>
<seg id="1968">I want to go to the seaside, and this current will take me there nicely.</seg>
<seg id="1968">我想到海边去，河水会带我过去的。</seg>
<seg id="1969">When I come back I'll show you with pleasure."</seg>
<seg id="1969">等我回来后，再告诉你们吧。”</seg>
<seg id="1970">THE HORSE AND THE STAG</seg>
<seg id="1970">马和雄鹿</seg>
<seg id="1971">There was once a Horse who used to graze in a meadow which he had all to himself.</seg>
<seg id="1971">从前，有一匹马曾经独自占有一片草场。</seg>
<seg id="1972">But one day a Stag came into the meadow, and said he had as good a right to feed there as the Horse, and moreover chose all the best places for himself.</seg>
<seg id="1972">有一天，一只雄鹿闯入了他的领地，说自己也像马一样有权利分享这里的草，不仅如此，还为自己选了一个最好的地方吃草。</seg>
<seg id="1973">The Horse, wishing to be revenged upon his unwelcome visitor, went to a man and asked if he would help him to turn out the Stag.</seg>
<seg id="1973">马一心想报复这只不请自来的鹿，便来到人那里询问是否能帮助自己惩罚鹿。</seg>
<seg id="1974">"Yes," said the man, "I will by all means; but I can only do so if you let me put a bridle in your mouth and mount on your back."</seg>
<seg id="1974">人回答说：“是的，我可以尽力帮你，不过，除非你愿意让我把一根勒马的缰绳放在你嘴里，并且骑在你的背上，我才能这么做。”</seg>
<seg id="1975">The Horse agreed to this, and the two together very soon turned the Stag out of the pasture:</seg>
<seg id="1975">马同意了人的要求，于是这两个合作者很快就把鹿赶出了草场。</seg>
<seg id="1976">but when that was done, the Horse found to his dismay that in the man he had got a master for good.</seg>
<seg id="1976">然而，一切结束后，马才发现自己永远成了人的奴隶。</seg>
<seg id="1977">THE FOX AND THE BRAMBLE</seg>
<seg id="1977">狐狸与荆棘</seg>
<seg id="1978">In making his way through a hedge a Fox missed his footing and caught at a Bramble to save himself from falling.</seg>
<seg id="1978">一只狐狸爬越篱笆时，差一点失足跌落下去，他拼命地抓住了一根荆棘，以防掉下去摔死。</seg>
<seg id="1979">Naturally, he got badly scratched, and in disgust he cried to the Bramble, "It was your help I wanted, and see how you have treated me!</seg>
<seg id="1979">狐狸自然被荆棘刺伤了，他厌恶地冲着荆棘大喊：“我只想得到你的帮助，可你却如此对待我！</seg>
<seg id="1980">I'd sooner have fallen outright."</seg>
<seg id="1980">还不如直接摔下去呢。”</seg>
<seg id="1981">The Bramble, interrupting him, replied, "You must have lost your wits, my friend, to catch at me, who am myself always catching at others."</seg>
<seg id="1981">荆棘打断了他的话，说：“朋友，向来都是我拉扯别人的，而你却来抓住我，那可就是你的愚蠢了。”</seg>
<seg id="1982">THE LION, THE FOX, AND THE STAG</seg>
<seg id="1982">狮子、狐狸和雄鹿</seg>
<seg id="1983">A Lion lay sick in his den, unable to provide himself with food.</seg>
<seg id="1983">一只生病的狮子躺在自己的洞里，没办法亲自去寻找食物。</seg>
<seg id="1984">So he said to his friend the Fox, who came to ask how he did, "My good friend, I wish you would go to yonder wood and beguile the big Stag, who lives there, to come to my den:</seg>
<seg id="1984">于是，他对前来探望自己的朋友——狐狸说：“我的好朋友，我希望你能到那片森林里去，用花言巧语把住在那里的一只最大的鹿骗到这里来，</seg>
<seg id="1985">I have a fancy to make my dinner off a stag's heart and brains."</seg>
<seg id="1985">我很想吃掉他的心和脑子。”</seg>
<seg id="1986">The Fox went to the wood and found the Stag and said to him, "My dear sir, you're in luck.</seg>
