<seg id="1986">狐狸来到树林里，看见了那只雄鹿，便对他说：“亲爱的朋友，你走运了。</seg>
<seg id="1987">You know the Lion, our King:</seg>
<seg id="1987">你知道我们的国王狮子吧，</seg>
<seg id="1988">well, he's at the point of death, and has appointed you his successor to rule over the beasts.</seg>
<seg id="1988">是的，他快要死了，可是却指名要你去继承他的王位，来统治百兽。</seg>
<seg id="1989">I hope you won't forget that I was the first to bring you the good news.</seg>
<seg id="1989">我希望你别忘了，我可是第一个向你报告好消息的。</seg>
<seg id="1990">And now I must be going back to him;</seg>
<seg id="1990">现在，我必须得回到狮子那里去了，</seg>
<seg id="1991">and, if you take my advice, you'll come too and be with him at the last."</seg>
<seg id="1991">如果你肯听我的话，就和我一起去，看他最后一眼吧。”</seg>
<seg id="1992">The Stag was highly flattered, and followed the Fox to the Lion's den, suspecting nothing.</seg>
<seg id="1992">雄鹿非常高兴，毫不设防地跟着狐狸来到了狮子的洞里。</seg>
<seg id="1993">No sooner had he got inside than the Lion sprang upon him, but he misjudged his spring, and the Stag got away with only his ears torn, and returned as fast as he could to the shelter of the wood.</seg>
<seg id="1993">刚一进来，狮子猛然朝鹿扑过来，然而，他错误地估计了自己的实力。雄鹿仅仅被撕扯掉了耳朵，他拼命地逃回树林里的避难处。</seg>
<seg id="1994">The Fox was much mortified, and the Lion, too, was dreadfully disappointed, for he was getting very hungry in spite of his illness.</seg>
<seg id="1994">狐狸很难过，狮子也很失望，因为生了病的他正在忍饥挨饿。</seg>
<seg id="1995">So he begged the Fox to have another try at coaxing the Stag to his den.</seg>
<seg id="1995">于是，狮子请求狐狸再想想办法，用诡计哄骗雄鹿再一次到洞里来。</seg>
<seg id="1996">"It'll be almost impossible this time," said the Fox, "but I'll try";</seg>
<seg id="1996">“这次不太可能了，”狐狸说，“不过，我会再试试。”</seg>
<seg id="1997">and off he went to the wood a second time, and found the Stag resting and trying to recover from his fright.</seg>
<seg id="1997">他又一次来到树林里，发现雄鹿正在休息疗伤。</seg>
<seg id="1998">As soon as he saw the Fox he cried, "You scoundrel, what do you mean by trying to lure me to my death like that?</seg>
<seg id="1998">一见到狐狸，雄鹿就哭喊道：“你这个大坏蛋，像那样骗我去送死，你到底什么意思？</seg>
<seg id="1999">Take yourself off, or I'll do you to death with my horns."</seg>
<seg id="1999">快走开，不然我就用鹿角刺死你。”</seg>
<seg id="2000">But the Fox was entirely shameless.</seg>
<seg id="2000">可是，狐狸却恬不知耻地说：</seg>
<seg id="2001">"What a coward you were," said he; "surely you didn't think the Lion meant any harm?</seg>
<seg id="2001">“你可真是个懦夫，你难道真的认为狮子要伤害你吗？</seg>
<seg id="2002">Why, he was only going to whisper some royal secrets into your ear when you went off like a scared rabbit.</seg>
<seg id="2002">他只是想在你耳边说一些关于王位的秘密罢了，可你却像只受了惊吓的兔子一样跑开了。</seg>
<seg id="2003">You have rather disgusted him, and I'm not sure he won't make the wolf King instead, unless you come back at once and show you've got some spirit.</seg>
<seg id="2003">你已经激怒了他，我不确定他是否要将王位传给狼，除非你立刻回去告诉狮子，你不是这样的胆小鬼。</seg>
<seg id="2004">I promise you he won't hurt you, and I will be your faithful servant."</seg>
<seg id="2004">我向你保证，狮子决不会伤害你，而且我也会做你的忠实奴仆。”</seg>
<seg id="2005">The Stag was foolish enough to be persuaded to return, and this time the Lion made no mistake, but overpowered him, and feasted right royally upon his carcase.</seg>
<seg id="2005">愚蠢的雄鹿又被说服了，再次跟着狐狸回到狮子的洞里。这一次，狮子没有再犯错误，轻易地制服了雄鹿，美美地享受了一顿。</seg>
<seg id="2006">The Fox, meanwhile, watched his chance and, when the Lion wasn't looking, filched away the brains to reward him for his trouble.</seg>
<seg id="2006">在一旁静候的狐狸，瞅准了机会，趁狮子不注意时，偷走了雄鹿的脑子，以此犒劳自己。</seg>
<seg id="2007">Presently the Lion began searching for them, of course without success:</seg>
<seg id="2007">一会儿，狮子开始寻找鹿的脑子，当然找不到了。</seg>
<seg id="2008">and the Fox, who was watching him, said, "I don't think it's much use your looking for the brains:</seg>
<seg id="2008">这时，在一旁观望的狐狸说：“我认为寻找鹿的脑子是白费工夫，</seg>
<seg id="2009">a creature who twice walked into a Lion's den can't have got any."</seg>
<seg id="2009">因为能两次走进狮子洞里来的动物，不可能有脑子。”</seg>
<seg id="2010">THE MAN WHO LOST HIS SPADE</seg>
<seg id="2010">丢了铁锹的人</seg>
<seg id="2011">A Man was engaged in digging over his vineyard, and one day on coming to work he missed his Spade.</seg>
<seg id="2011">一个人在他的葡萄园里掘土，有一天，要开始工作时发现铁锹没了。</seg>
<seg id="2012">Thinking it may have been stolen by one of his labourers, he questioned them closely, but they one and all denied any knowledge of it.</seg>
<seg id="2012">他以为可能是被某个工人偷走了，就过去质问他们，但工人们一个个都否认偷了铁锹。</seg>
<seg id="2013">He was not convinced by their denials, and insisted that they should all go to the town and take oath in a temple that they were not guilty of the theft.</seg>
<seg id="2013">尽管工人都否认了，可他依然不相信，一再坚持所有人都应该到城里的寺庙去发誓，自己没有犯盗窃罪。</seg>
<seg id="2014">This was because he had no great opinion of the simple country deities, but thought that the thief would not pass undetected by the shrewder gods of the town.</seg>
<seg id="2014">这是因为他对小镇上的神灵没有什么概念，以为小偷逃不过城里寺庙精明神灵的检测。</seg>
<seg id="2015">When they got inside the gates the first thing they heard was the town crier proclaiming a reward for information about a thief who had stolen something from the city temple.</seg>
<seg id="2015">他们刚走进大门，就听到了悬赏缉拿从寺庙偷东西的小偷。</seg>
<seg id="2016">"Well," said the Man to himself, "it strikes me I had better go back home again.</seg>
<seg id="2016">“好吧，”这人自言自语地说，“我最好还是赶快回家吧。</seg>
<seg id="2017">If these town gods can't detect the thieves who steal from their own temples, it's scarcely likely they can tell me who stole my Spade."</seg>
<seg id="2017">如果这些庙里的神都无法找到盗窃寺庙东西的贼，他们也不太可能告诉我是谁偷了我的铁锹。”</seg>
<seg id="2018">THE PARTRIDGE AND THE FOWLER</seg>
<seg id="2018">鹧鸪和捕鸟人</seg>
<seg id="2019">A Fowler caught a Partridge in his nets, and was just about to wring its neck when it made a piteous appeal to him to spare its life and said, "Do not kill me, but let me live and I will repay you for your kindness by decoying other partridges into your nets."</seg>
<seg id="2019">有个捕鸟的人在网里捉到一只鹧鸪，正要拧断他的脖子时，鹧鸪带着可怜的表情求他饶了自己的命，并说：“不要杀死我，让我活着吧，我会诱骗其他鹧鸪到你的网里来，以此来回报你对我的仁慈。”</seg>
<seg id="2020">"No," said the Fowler, "I will not spare you.</seg>
<seg id="2020">捕鸟人说：“不，我不能饶了你，</seg>
<seg id="2021">I was going to kill you anyhow, and after that treacherous speech you thoroughly deserve your fate."</seg>
<seg id="2021">无论如何都要杀了你。尤其是听了你这番背叛同类的宣言，你更应该去死了。”</seg>
<seg id="2022">THE HUNTER AND THE WOODMAN</seg>
<seg id="2022">猎人和樵夫</seg>
<seg id="2023">A Hunter was searching in the forest for the tracks of a lion, and, catching sight presently of a Woodman engaged in felling a tree, he went up to him and asked him if he had noticed a lion's footprints anywhere about, or if he knew where his den was.</seg>
<seg id="2023">一个猎人正在森林里搜寻狮子的踪迹，不久，他看到一个樵夫正在砍树，于是便走上前问他有没有注意到狮子的足迹，或者是否知道狮子躲在了哪里。</seg>
<seg id="2024">The Woodman answered, "If you will come with me, I will show you the lion himself."</seg>
<seg id="2024">樵夫回答说：“要是你和我一起去，就能亲自看到狮子了。”</seg>
<seg id="2025">The Hunter turned pale with fear, and his teeth chattered as he replied, "Oh, I'm not looking for the lion, thanks, but only for his tracks."</seg>
<seg id="2025">猎人吓得脸色惨白，牙齿打着颤说道：“我只想搜寻它的踪迹，并不是在找狮子本身。”</seg>
<seg id="2026">THE SERPENT AND THE EAGLE</seg>
<seg id="2026">毒蛇和鹰</seg>
<seg id="2027">An Eagle swooped down upon a Serpent and seized it in his talons with the intention of carrying it off and devouring it.</seg>
<seg id="2027">一只老鹰朝着一条毒蛇俯冲下来，用鹰爪抓住了蛇，想要把他带走并吃掉。</seg>
<seg id="2028">But the Serpent was too quick for him and had its coils round him in a moment;</seg>
<seg id="2028">可是，毒蛇却迅速缠住了老鹰，</seg>
<seg id="2029">and then there ensued a life-and-death struggle between the two.</seg>
<seg id="2029">接着展开了一场生死搏斗。</seg>
<seg id="2030">A countryman, who was a witness of the encounter, came to the assistance of the Eagle, and succeeded in freeing him from the Serpent and enabling him to escape.</seg>
<seg id="2030">一个农夫看到了整个过程，走过来帮老鹰解开了蛇的缠绕，让他重新获得了自由。</seg>
<seg id="2031">In revenge the Serpent spat some of his poison into the man's drinking-horn.</seg>
<seg id="2031">为了报复农夫，蛇便将自己的毒液注进了农夫喝水的角杯里。</seg>
<seg id="2032">Heated with his exertions, the man was about to slake his thirst with a draught from the horn, when the Eagle knocked it out of his hand, and spilled its contents upon the ground.</seg>
<seg id="2032">忙活了半天的农夫正想去解解渴，便拿起角杯要喝水，这时，老鹰飞过来撞掉了他手中的角杯，杯子里的水全都洒在了地上。</seg>
<seg id="2033">One good turn deserves another.</seg>
<seg id="2033">善有善报。</seg>
<seg id="2034">THE ROGUE AND THE ORACLE</seg>
<seg id="2034">无赖和圣人</seg>
<seg id="2035">A Rogue laid a wager that he would prove the Oracle at Delphi to be untrustworthy by procuring from it a false reply to an inquiry by himself.</seg>
<seg id="2035">一个狡猾的人下赌注，他能让德尔斐（希腊古都）的圣人用错误的回答来证明自己不值得信赖。</seg>
<seg id="2036">So he went to the temple on the appointed day with a small bird in his hand, which he concealed under the folds of his cloak, and asked whether what he held in his hand were alive or dead.</seg>
<seg id="2036">于是，到了约定好的那一天，他来到了庙里，手里拿着一只小麻雀，并将它藏在外衣里面。他问圣人自己手中拿着的东西是活的还是死的。</seg>
<seg id="2037">If the Oracle said "dead," he meant to produce the bird alive:</seg>
<seg id="2037">如果圣人说“是死的”，他便把活着的麻雀拿出来；</seg>
<seg id="2038">if the reply was "alive," he intended to wring its neck and show it to be dead.</seg>
<seg id="2038">如果圣人说“是活的”，他就捏死麻雀，然后再将死的拿出来。</seg>
<seg id="2039">But the Oracle was one too many for him, for the answer he got was this: "Stranger, whether the thing that you hold in your hand be alive or dead is a matter that depends entirely on your own will."</seg>
<seg id="2039">可是，圣人远比他更高明，说道：“陌生人，不管你手里的东西是死是活，完全取决于你自己的意愿！”</seg>
<seg id="2040">THE HORSE AND THE ASS</seg>
<seg id="2040">马和驴</seg>
<seg id="2041">A Horse, proud of his fine harness, met an Ass on the high-road.</seg>
<seg id="2041">一匹马对自己精美的马具感到自豪，他在一条小路上遇到了一头满载货物的驴。</seg>
<seg id="2042">As the Ass with his heavy burden moved slowly out of the way to let him pass, the Horse cried out impatiently that he could hardly resist kicking him to make him move faster.</seg>
<seg id="2042">驴因货物太重，只能慢慢地走，而无法让马先过去。马不耐烦地说恨不得踢他一脚，让他快点走。</seg>
<seg id="2043">The Ass held his peace, but did not forget the other's insolence.</seg>
<seg id="2043">驴默不作声，但是没有忘记马的傲慢无礼。</seg>
<seg id="2044">Not long afterwards the Horse became broken-winded, and was sold by his owner to a farmer.</seg>
<seg id="2044">不久，那匹马患了气喘病，被主人卖到了农场。</seg>
<seg id="2045">One day, as he was drawing a dung-cart, he met the Ass again, who in turn derided him and said, "Aha! you never thought to come to this, did you, you who were so proud!</seg>
<seg id="2045">有一天，当马正拉着粪车时，又遇到了驴，驴反而讥笑他说：“哈！你从没想到会来这里干这种活吧，不是吗，你那么傲慢！</seg>
<seg id="2046">Where are all your gay trappings now?"</seg>
<seg id="2046">现在，你那华丽的马具到哪里去了？”</seg>
<seg id="2047">THE DOG CHASING A WOLF</seg>
<seg id="2047">追赶狼的狗</seg>
<seg id="2048">A Dog was chasing a Wolf, and as he ran he thought what a fine fellow he was, and what strong legs he had, and how quickly they covered the ground.</seg>
<seg id="2048">一条狗正在追赶一只狼，他边跑边想，自己是一条多么好的狗呀，腿多么健壮，跑得又是多么的快。</seg>
<seg id="2049">"Now, there's this Wolf," he said to himself, "what a poor creature he is:</seg>
<seg id="2049">狗自言自语道：“现在，看看这只狼，多么可怜呀，</seg>
<seg id="2050">he's no match for me, and he knows it and so he runs away."</seg>
<seg id="2050">他根本不是我的对手，他很有自知之明，所以才会逃跑。”</seg>
<seg id="2051">But the Wolf looked round just then and said, "Don't you imagine I'm running away from you, my friend:</seg>
<seg id="2051">然而，狼却回过头来对他说：“朋友，不要以为我因为惧怕你才逃跑，</seg>
<seg id="2052">it's your master I'm afraid of."</seg>
<seg id="2052">让我害怕的是你身后的主人。”</seg>
<seg id="2053">GRIEF AND HIS DUE</seg>
<seg id="2053">悲伤和他被指派的份额</seg>
<seg id="2054">When Jupiter was assigning the various gods their privileges, it so happened that Grief was not present with the rest:</seg>
<seg id="2054">朱庇特正在给不同的神灵指派特权，恰巧悲伤没有到场。</seg>
<seg id="2055">but when all had received their share, he too entered and claimed his due.</seg>
<seg id="2055">但是，当所有神灵都得到了指派的份额后，悲伤进来了，也声称想要他应得的份额。</seg>
<seg id="2056">Jupiter was at a loss to know what to do, for there was nothing left for him.</seg>
<seg id="2056">朱庇特有点不知所措，因为什么都没有留给他。</seg>
<seg id="2057">However, at last he decided that to him should belong the tears that are shed for the dead.</seg>
<seg id="2057">然而，朱庇特最后决定，悲伤应该属于为亡人而流下的泪水。</seg>
<seg id="2058">Thus it is the same with Grief as it is with the other gods.</seg>
<seg id="2058">因此，悲伤与其他神灵一样，也得到了属于自己的份额。</seg>
<seg id="2059">The more devoutly men render to him his due, the more lavish is he of that which he has to bestow.</seg>
<seg id="2059">越发虔诚地回报给悲伤，悲伤就会越发大方地赋予你属于他的份额。</seg>
<seg id="2060">It is not well, therefore, to mourn long for the departed;</seg>
<seg id="2060">所以，长久地为逝者而悲伤并不好。</seg>
<seg id="2061">else Grief, whose sole pleasure is in such mourning, will be quick to send fresh cause for tears.</seg>
<seg id="2061">悲伤的唯一乐趣就在这样的哀悼中，否则，他会迅速为泪水寻找新的原因。</seg>
<seg id="2062">THE WOMAN AND THE FARMER</seg>
<seg id="2062">女人和农夫</seg>
<seg id="2063">A Woman, who had lately lost her husband, used to go every day to his grave and lament her loss.</seg>
<seg id="2063">有一个女人刚刚失去了丈夫，她每天都要到丈夫的坟上痛哭一场。</seg>
<seg id="2064">A Farmer, who was engaged in ploughing not far from the spot, set eyes upon the Woman and desired to have her for his wife:</seg>
<seg id="2064">有一个农夫在不远处耕地，一直观察着这个女人，想娶她为妻。</seg>
<seg id="2065">so he left his plough and came and sat by her side, and began to shed tears himself.</seg>
<seg id="2065">于是，农夫放下自己的犁，来到她身边坐下，也痛哭起来。</seg>
<seg id="2066">She asked him why he wept; and he replied, "I have lately lost my wife, who was very dear to me, and tears ease my grief."</seg>
<seg id="2066">女人问他为什么哭，农夫回答说：“我的妻子最近也死了，她和我非常恩爱，也许眼泪能够减轻我的悲伤。”</seg>
<seg id="2067">"And I," said she, "have lost my husband."</seg>
<seg id="2067">女人说：“我丈夫也是刚刚去世。”</seg>
<seg id="2068">And so for a while they mourned in silence.</seg>
<seg id="2068">两人就这样默然哀伤了一阵子。</seg>
<seg id="2069">Then he said, "Since you and I are in like case, shall we not do well to marry and live together?</seg>
<seg id="2069">接着，农夫说：“既然你我遭遇相同，我们为何不结为夫妻，在一起生活呢？</seg>
<seg id="2070">I shall take the place of your dead husband, and you, that of my dead wife."</seg>
<seg id="2070">我替代你死去的丈夫，而你则替代我死去的妻子。”</seg>
<seg id="2071">The Woman consented to the plan, which indeed seemed reasonable enough:</seg>
<seg id="2071">这个想法听起来的确很有道理，那女人高兴地同意了。</seg>
<seg id="2072">and they dried their tears.</seg>
<seg id="2072">[无]</seg>
<seg id="2073">Meanwhile, a thief had come and stolen the oxen which the Farmer had left with his plough.</seg>
<seg id="2073">这时候，有一个贼偷走了农夫丢下的公牛。</seg>
<seg id="2074">On discovering the theft, he beat his breast and loudly bewailed his loss.</seg>
<seg id="2074">看到自己的牛被偷了，农夫不禁捶胸顿足地悲叹自己的损失。</seg>
<seg id="2075">When the Woman heard his cries, she came and said, "Why, are you weeping still?"</seg>
<seg id="2075">此刻，女人听见了他的哭声，走过来问道：“为什么，你还在哭吗？”</seg>
<seg id="2076">To which he replied, "Yes, and I mean it this time."</seg>
<seg id="2076">农夫回答：“是的！这一次是真心的。”</seg>
<seg id="2077">PROMETHEUS AND THE MAKING OF MAN</seg>
<seg id="2077">普罗米修斯与造人</seg>
<seg id="2078">At the bidding of Jupiter, Prometheus set about the creation of Man and the other animals.</seg>
<seg id="2078">遵照朱庇特的命令，普罗米修斯创造了人和其他动物。</seg>
<seg id="2079">Jupiter, seeing that Mankind, the only rational creatures, were far outnumbered by the irrational beasts, bade him redress the balance by turning some of the latter into men.</seg>
<seg id="2079">其中，只有人是理性的生灵，朱庇特看到不理性的动物数量远远超过了人，便命令他更改一下比例，把一部分动物变成人。</seg>
<seg id="2080">Prometheus did as he was bidden, and this is the reason why some people have the forms of men but the souls of beasts.</seg>
<seg id="2080">普罗米修斯奉命行事。因此，正是这个原因，有些人虽然有着人的外形，内心却仍与动物一样。</seg>
<seg id="2081">THE SWALLOW AND THE CROW</seg>
<seg id="2081">燕子和乌鸦</seg>
<seg id="2082">A Swallow was once boasting to a Crow about her birth.</seg>
<seg id="2082">有一次，燕子冲着乌鸦吹嘘自己的出生多么显赫。</seg>
<seg id="2083">"I was once a princess," said she, "the daughter of a King of Athens, but my husband used me cruelly, and cut out my tongue for a slight fault.</seg>
<seg id="2083">“我曾经是一个公主，”燕子说，“是雅典国王的女儿，但是我的丈夫却因为我的一个小过失而割掉了我的舌头。</seg>
<seg id="2084">Then, to protect me from further injury, I was turned by Juno into a bird."</seg>
<seg id="2084">为了以免再次受到伤害，朱诺就把我变成了一只鸟。”</seg>
<seg id="2085">"You chatter quite enough as it is," said the Crow.</seg>
<seg id="2085">“你可真会搬弄是非，”乌鸦说，</seg>
<seg id="2086">"What you would have been like if you hadn't lost your tongue, I can't think."</seg>
<seg id="2086">“要是你没有损失舌头，又会变成什么样呢？我简直不敢想象。”</seg>
<seg id="2087">THE HUNTER AND THE HORSEMAN</seg>
<seg id="2087">猎人和骑手</seg>
<seg id="2088">A Hunter went out after game, and succeeded in catching a hare, which he was carrying home with him when he met a man on horseback, who said to him, "You have had some sport I see, sir," and offered to buy it.</seg>
<seg id="2088">有个猎人出外打猎后，扛着一只兔子归来，途中遇见一个骑马的人，那人停下来说：“你已经收获猎物回来了，先生。”而且还假装要买兔子。</seg>
<seg id="2089">The Hunter readily agreed;</seg>
<seg id="2089">猎人很高兴地同意了，</seg>
<seg id="2090">but the Horseman had no sooner got the hare in his hands than he set spurs to his horse and went off at full gallop.</seg>
<seg id="2090">可是骑马人一拿到兔子，立刻就用鞭子抽了马一下，飞奔而去。</seg>
<seg id="2091">The Hunter ran after him for some little distance;</seg>
<seg id="2091">猎人拼命地在后面追赶了一阵子，</seg>
<seg id="2092">but it soon dawned upon him that he had been tricked, and he gave up trying to overtake the Horseman, and, to save his face, called after him as loud as he could, "All right, sir, all right, take your hare:</seg>
<seg id="2092">但是很快就明白自己上当了，不再去追骑马人。为了挽回自己的颜面，猎人在骑马人身后大声喊道：“好吧，好吧，拿走吧！</seg>
<seg id="2093">it was meant all along as a present."</seg>
<seg id="2093">那只兔子送给你了。”</seg>
<seg id="2094">THE GOATHERD AND THE WILD GOATS</seg>
<seg id="2094">牧羊人和野山羊</seg>
<seg id="2095">A Goatherd was tending his goats out at pasture when he saw a number of Wild Goats approach and mingle with his flock.</seg>
<seg id="2095">牧羊人赶着羊群去牧场吃草，他看到几只野山羊混进了羊群里。</seg>
<seg id="2096">At the end of the day he drove them home and put them all into the pen together.</seg>
<seg id="2096">傍晚，他将所有的羊都赶回家，关进了羊圈。</seg>
<seg id="2097">Next day the weather was so bad that he could not take them out as usual:</seg>
<seg id="2097">第二天，天气很不好，无法像往常那样到牧场里去放牧了，</seg>
<seg id="2098">so he kept them at home in the pen, and fed them there.</seg>
<seg id="2098">于是，他只好让羊群待在羊圈里，在那里喂它们吃草。</seg>
<seg id="2099">He only gave his own goats enough food to keep them from starving, but he gave the Wild Goats as much as they could eat and more;</seg>
<seg id="2099">他只给自己的羊一点点刚够果腹的草，却给那些野山羊更多的草吃，</seg>
<seg id="2100">for he was very anxious for them to stay, and he thought that if he fed them well they wouldn't want to leave him.</seg>
<seg id="2100">因为他希望让那些野山羊留下来。他心想，只要给它们多吃点草，野山羊可能就不想离开他了。</seg>
<seg id="2101">When the weather improved, he took them all out to pasture again;</seg>
<seg id="2101">等天气转好，牧羊人又赶着所有的羊来到了牧场。</seg>
<seg id="2102">but no sooner had they got near the hills than the Wild Goats broke away from the flock and scampered off.</seg>
<seg id="2102">刚来到山下，那些野山羊立刻冲出羊群，四散而逃。</seg>
<seg id="2103">The Goatherd was very much disgusted at this, and roundly abused them for their ingratitude.</seg>
<seg id="2103">牧羊人十分生气，指责它们忘恩负义。</seg>
<seg id="2104">"Rascals!" he cried, "to run away like that after the way I've treated you!"</seg>
<seg id="2104">“你们这些混蛋！”他喊道，“我对你们那么好，竟然以这种方式纷纷逃跑了！”</seg>
<seg id="2105">Hearing this, one of them turned round and said, "Oh, yes, you treated us all right--too well, in fact;</seg>
<seg id="2105">野山羊听到他的话，回过头来说：“是的，你对我们很好，</seg>
<seg id="2106">it was just that that put us on our guard. </seg>
<seg id="2106">实际上是太好了，正因如此，我们才会更加小心。</seg>
<seg id="2107">If you treat newcomers like ourselves so much better than your own flock, it's more than likely that, if another lot of strange goats joined yours, we should then be neglected in favour of the last comers."</seg>
<seg id="2107">你对待我们这些新来的羊比你自己的羊群还要好，那么很有可能，当另外一群陌生的羊再加入进来时，我们也会受到冷落，而你却只偏爱它们了。”</seg>
<seg id="2108">THE NIGHTINGALE AND THE SWALLOW</seg>
<seg id="2108">夜莺和燕子</seg>
<seg id="2109">A Swallow, conversing with a Nightingale, advised her to quit the leafy coverts where she made her home, and to come and live with men, like herself, and nest under the shelter of their roofs.</seg>
<seg id="2109">一只燕子在和一只夜莺聊天，燕子劝她不要在茂密的树丛上做窝了，像自己一样与人住在一起。</seg>
<seg id="2110">But the Nightingale replied, "Time was when I too, like yourself, lived among men:</seg>
<seg id="2110">可是，夜莺却回答说：“我过去也曾像你一样和人住在一起，</seg>
<seg id="2111">but the memory of the cruel wrongs I then suffered makes them hateful to me, and never again will I approach their dwellings."</seg>
<seg id="2111">但是我所遭受的那份痛苦回忆让他们都不喜欢我，我永远都不想再接近他们的住所。”</seg>
<seg id="2112">The scene of past sufferings revives painful memories.</seg>
<seg id="2112">痛苦的回忆使得过去的痛苦体验历历在目。</seg>
<seg id="2113">THE TRAVELLER AND FORTUNE</seg>
<seg id="2113">旅人和命运女神</seg>
<seg id="2114">A Traveller, exhausted with fatigue after a long journey, sank down at the very brink of a deep well and presently fell asleep.</seg>
<seg id="2114">经过一段长途跋涉，一个疲劳过度的旅行者倒在一口深井的边缘，酣然入睡。</seg>
<seg id="2115">He was within an ace of falling in, when Dame Fortune appeared to him and touched him on the shoulder, cautioning him to move further away.</seg>
<seg id="2115">他差一点就掉到井里去，这时，命运女神出现在他面前，并且摸着他的肩膀，提醒他离井远一点。</seg>
<seg id="2116">"Wake up, good sir, I pray you," she said; "had you fallen into the well, the blame would have been thrown not on your own folly but on me, Fortune."</seg>
<seg id="2116">“朋友，拜托你，快醒醒，”女神说，“你若是掉到井里去，一定会责怪我，而不会责怪自己的愚蠢。”</seg>
